    1

    剪灯新话 明 瞿佑撰
    　　
    　　瞿佑，字宗吉，号存斋，钱塘（今浙江杭州）人，明初著名文学家。少时即有诗名，但终生怀才不遇，仅在洪武年间任教谕、训导、长史之类小官。永乐年间因写诗蒙祸，被贬谪十年。有小说集《剪灯新话》等著作。

    Explanation

    1

    A New Tale of Cutting the Lamp
    Ming Dynasty, by Qu You

    Qu You, courtesy name Zongji, pen name Cunzhai, was from Qiantang (now Hangzhou, Zhejiang). He was a renowned literary figure at the beginning of the Ming dynasty. From a young age, he gained a reputation as a poet, but throughout his life, he remained unrecognized despite his talent. He held minor positions such as teacher, instructor, and longshi (a type of official) during the Hongwu era. During the Yongle era, he suffered misfortune due to his poetry and was exiled for ten years. He is the author of the short story collection A New Tale of Cutting the Lamp and other works.

    2

    《剪灯新话》序一
    　　余既编辑古今怪奇之事。以为《剪灯录》，凡四十卷矣。好事者每以近事相闻，远不出百年，近止在数载，襞积于中，日新月盛，习气所溺，欲罢不能，乃援笔为文以纪之。其事皆可喜可悲，可惊可怪者。所惜笔路荒芜，词源浅狭，无嵬目鸿耳之论以发扬之耳。既成，又自以为涉于语怪，近于海淫，藏之书笥，不欲传出。客闻而求观者众，不能尽却之，则又自解曰：《诗》、《书》、《易》、《春秋》、皆圣笔之所述作，以为万世大经大法者也；然而《易》言龙战于野，《书》载雉雊于鼎，《国风》取淫奔之诗，《春秋》纪乱贼之事，是又不可执一论也。今余此编，虽于世教民彝，莫之或补，而劝善惩恶，哀穷悼屈，其亦庶乎言者无罪，闻者足以戒之一义云尔。客以余言有理，故书之卷首。

    Explanation

    2

    《Jian Deng Xin Hua》 Preface One
    Having compiled strange and marvelous events from ancient and modern times, I created the Jian Deng Lu, totaling forty volumes. Those fond of such tales often share recent events, ranging from not more than a century ago to as recent as a few years. These tales accumulate in my mind, becoming more abundant each day. My habitual fascination makes it impossible to stop, so I took up my pen to record them. The events are all joyful, sorrowful, surprising, and strange. The only regret is that my writing is barren and my vocabulary limited, lacking profound insight to elevate them. Once completed, I felt it delved into the realm of strange tales, verging on the bizarre. I kept it in a chest, not wanting it to be circulated. Many visitors heard about it and wanted to see it, and I couldn't refuse them all. I then explained: "The Shijing, Shujing, Yijing, and Chunqiu are all works of the sages, considered the great principles and laws for all ages. However, the Yijing speaks of dragons fighting in the wild, the Shujing records a rooster crowing from a tripod, the Guofeng includes poems about licentiousness, and the Chunqiu documents chaotic and rebellious events. These cannot be judged by a single criterion." My compilation, though it may not contribute much to the norms of society and morality, still serves to encourage good and punish evil, to pity the poor and mourn the oppressed, and it aligns with the principle that 'speakers should not be punished, and listeners should be warned.' The visitors found my reasoning sound, so I wrote it at the beginning of the volume.

    3

    洪武十一年岁次戊午六月朔日，山阳瞿佑书于吴山大隐堂
    　　《剪灯新活》序二
    　　昔陈鸿作《长恨传》并《东城老父传》，时人称其史才，咸推许之。及观牛憎孺之《幽怪录》，刘斧之《青琐集》，则又述奇纪异，其事之有无不必论，而其制作之体，则亦工矣。乡友瞿宗吉氏着《剪灯新话》，无乃类是乎？宗吉之志确而勤，故其学也博，具才充而敏，故其文也赡。是编虽稗官之流，而劝善惩恶，动存鉴戒，不可谓无补于世。矧夫造意之奇，措词之妙，粲然自成一家言，读之使人喜而手舞足蹈，悲而掩卷堕泪者，盖亦有之。自非好古博雅，工于文而审于事，曷能臻此哉！至于《秋香亭记》之作，则犹元稹之《莺莺传》也，余将质之宗吉，不知果然否？

    Explanation

    3

    On the first day of June in the year of Wuwu (戊午) of the 11th year of the Hongwu era, Qü You of Shanyang wrote this in the Great Hidden Hall on Mount Wu.

    Second Preface to New Tales Under the Lamp

    In the past, Chen Hong wrote The Story of Eternal Regret and The Tale of the Old Man from the Eastern City, and people at the time praised his historical talent and all commended him. When one looks at Niu Zengru's Records of the Mysterious and Strange and Liu Fu's Collection of the Green Lock, they too narrate strange and extraordinary events; whether the events are true or not need not be discussed, but the structure of the work is also well-crafted. My fellow townsman Qü Zongji wrote New Tales Under the Lamp; is it not similar to these works? Zongji's determination is firm and diligent, therefore his learning is extensive; his talent is abundant and quick, therefore his writing is rich and abundant. This collection, though a work of minor officials, encourages good and punishes evil, always serving as a moral lesson, and it cannot be said to be without benefit to the world. Especially the ingenious conception and the exquisite choice of words, they shine brightly, forming a unique style of their own. Reading it makes one joyful and dancing with delight, or sad and shedding tears; there are indeed such cases. Unless one is fond of antiquity, erudite, skilled in writing, and discerning in matters, how could one achieve this? As for the writing of Record of the Autumn Fragrance Pavilion, it is like Yuan Zhen's Tale of Yingying; I will discuss this with Zongji, I wonder if it is truly so.

    4

    洪武三十年夏四月，钱塘凌云翰序
    　　《剪灯新话》序三
    　　余观宗吉先生《剪灯新活》，其词则传奇之流。其意则子氏之寓言也。宗吉家学渊源，博及群集，屡荐明经，母老不仕，得肆力于文学。余尝接其论议，观其著述，如开武库。如游宝坊，无非惊人之奇，希世之珍；是编特武库、室坊中之一耳。然则观是编者，于宗吉之学之博，尚有愆也。
    　　洪武十四年秋八月，吴植书于钱塘邑庠进德斋

    Explanation

    4

    In the month of May in the thirtieth year of the Hongwu era, Ling Yunhan of Qiantang wrote the preface to the third preface of Jian Deng Xin Hua:
    　　I have read Mr. Zongji's Jian Deng Xin Hua. Its style is akin to that of legends, and its meaning is like the allegorical stories of the Zhuangzi school. Mr. Zongji has a family tradition of learning, extensive knowledge across various fields, and has been repeatedly recommended for official positions based on Confucian learning. However, due to his mother's advanced age, he chose not to take up such duties and instead devoted himself to literature. I have engaged in discussions with him and read his works, finding them as vast as an arsenal of military knowledge and as rich as a treasure trove of wisdom. They contain nothing but astonishing wonders and rare treasures of the world; this compilation is merely one item among many in such a vast collection. Therefore, those who read this compilation may not fully appreciate the breadth of Mr. Zongji's learning.
    　　In the month of August in the fourteenth year of the Hongwu era, Wu Zhi wrote this preface at the Jinde Hall of the school in Qiantang.

    5

    《剪灯新话》序四
    　　余观昌黎韩子作《毛颖传》，柳子厚读而奇之，谓若捕龙蛇，搏虎豹，急与之角，而力不敢暇；古之文人，其相推奖类若此。及子厚作《谪龙说》与《河间传》等，后之人亦未闻有以妄且淫病子厚者，岂前辈所见，有不逮今耶？亦忠厚之志焉耳矣。余友瞿宗吉之为《剪灯新话》，其所志怪，有过于马孺子所言，而淫则无若河间之甚者。而或者犹沾沾然置噱于其间，何俗之不古也如是！盖宗吉以褒善贬恶之学，训导之间，游其耳目于词翰之场，闻见既多，积累益富。恐其久而记忆之或忘也，故取其事之尤可以感发、可以惩创者，汇次成编，藏之箧笥，以自恰悦，此宗吉之志也。余下敏，则既不知其是，亦不知其非，不知何者为可取，何者为可讥。伏而观之，但见其有文、有诗、有歇、有词、有可喜、有可悲、有可骇、有可嗤。信宗吉于文学而又有余力于他著者也。宗吉索余题，故为赋古体一首以复之云。

    Explanation

    5

    Preface to New Tales of the Lamp Snipping

    I have observed that Master Han of Changli composed The Biography of Mao Ying, and Liu Zihou read it and found it extraordinary, saying it was like capturing dragons and snakes, wrestling tigers and leopards, and engaging them in fierce combat, yet he had no time to spare for such pursuits. Ancient writers would praise each other in this manner. Later, when Liu Zihou wrote The Exiled Dragon and The Biography of the River Intendant, I have not heard of anyone criticizing him for being frivolous or licentious. Is it that the vision of our predecessors was not as sharp as that of today? Or is it simply a reflection of their sincere and generous spirit? My friend Qu Zongji composed New Tales of the Lamp Snipping, and the strange tales he recorded are even more fantastic than those told by Ma Ruzi, though in terms of licentiousness, none surpasses the River Intendant. Yet some still take delight in finding amusement in it, lamenting how unrefined and modern the customs have become.

    Qu Zongji, with his principles of praising goodness and condemning evil, immersed himself in the world of literature and writing during his teaching. Having heard and seen much, his knowledge has grown richer. Fearing that over time, he might forget these things, he selected stories that could inspire or serve as a warning, compiled them into a collection, and kept them in his chest for his own pleasure. This is the intention of Qu Zongji.

    I, being less intelligent, do not know whether it is right or wrong, nor do I know what is praiseworthy and what is laughable. Upon reading it, I see that it contains prose, poetry, essays, lyrics, things to be pleased with, things to be sad about, things to be frightened by, and things to be laughed at. It is clear that Qu Zongji is skilled in literature and has the ability to write other works as well. Qu Zongji asked me to write a preface, so I composed an ancient-style poem in response.

    6

    山阳才人畴与侣？开口为今阖为古！
    　　春以桃花染性情，秋将桂子熏言语。
    　　感离抚遇心怦怦，道是无凭还有凭。
    　　沉沉帐底昼吹笛。煦煦窗前宵剪灯。
    　　倏而晴兮忽而雨，悲欲啼兮喜欲舞，

    Explanation

    6

    Talented individuals from Shanyang, who are your companions? Their words span the present and the past!
    In spring, the peach blossoms dye their temperaments; in autumn, the osmanthus flowers perfume their speech.
    Feeling the bittersweet encounters, their hearts beat rapidly; though it seems groundless, there is still a basis.
    In the dimly lit tent, they play the flute during the day; by the window, they trim the lamp warmly at night.
    Suddenly sunny, then suddenly rainy; they want to weep in sorrow, yet dance in joy.

    7

    玉萧倚月吹凤凰，金栅和烟锁鹦鹉。
    　　造化有迹尸者谁？一念才荫方寸移，
    　　善善恶恶苟无失，怪怪奇奇将有之。
    　　丈夫未达虎为狗，濯足沧浪泥数斗，
    　　气寒骨耸铮有声，脱帻目光如电走。
    　　道人青蛇天动摇，下斩寻常花月妖，
    　　茫茫尘海沤万点，落落云松酒半瓢。
    　　世间万事幻泡耳，往往有情能不死，
    　　十二巫山谁道深，云母屏凤薄如纸。
    　　莺莺宅前芳享述，燕燕楼中明月低，
    　　从来松柏有孤操，不独鸳鸯能并栖。
    　　久在钱塘江上住，厌见潮来又潮去，
    　　燕子衔春几度回？断梦残魂落何处？
    　　还君此编长啸歌，便欲酌以金叵罗，
    　　醉来呼枕睡一觉，高车驷马游南柯。
    　　洪武己巳六月六日，睦人桂衡书于紫薇深处
    　　目录
    　　剪灯新话卷一
    　　水宫庆会录
    　　三山福地志
    　　华亭逢故人记
    　　金凤钗记
    　　联芳楼记
    　　剪灯新话卷二

    Explanation

    7

    The Jade Flute leans on the moon, playing the phoenix; golden bars are entwined with smoke, trapping a parrot.
    Who leaves a trace in the natural order? A single thought can move the heart.
    If one does not fail in doing good and avoiding evil, strange and unusual things may come to pass.
    A man who has not achieved his goals may be reduced to a lowly state, like a tiger becoming a dog; washing one's feet in clear water, removing several measures of mud,
    Cold and rigid, with a voice that sounds sharp and metallic, removing one's hat and looking around with eyes that shine like lightning.
    A Taoist practitioner moves like a green snake in the sky, cutting down ordinary "flower and moon demons,"
    In the vast sea of dust, with countless bubbles, a lone pine tree in the clouds, with half a gourd of wine.
    All things in the world are like bubbles, but sometimes emotions or passions can endure.
    No one can truly know the depth of the Twelve Peaks of Wushan; a cloud-mother screen as thin as paper.
    The beauty of Yingying's house is described in detail; a low-hanging moon in a building where Yan Yan resides.
    Pines and cypresses have always had a solitary and upright character; not only can mandarin ducks live together, but other creatures can also do so.
    Having lived by the Qiantang River for a long time, one grows weary of seeing the tides come and go,
    Swallows bring spring back multiple times; broken dreams and fragmented spirits, where do they fall?
    Returning the book to the reader and singing a long song, desiring to drink from a golden cup,
    Falling asleep after drinking, a journey in a luxurious carriage, possibly a metaphor for a dream or a fleeting experience.
    Written by Gui Heng of Mu on June 6, 1399 (the fourth year of the Hongwu era of the Ming dynasty).

    　　剪灯新话卷一
    　　水宫庆会录
    　　至正甲申岁，潮州士人余善文于所居白昼闲坐，忽有力士二人，黄巾绣祆，自外而入，致敬于前曰：“广利王奉邀。”善文惊曰：“广利洋海之神，善文尘世之士，幽显路殊，安得相及？ ”二人曰：“君但请行，毋用辞阻。 ”遂与之偕出南门外，见大红船泊于江浒。登船，有两黄龙挟之而行，速如凤雨，瞬息已至。止于门下，二人入报。顷之，请入。广利降阶而接曰：“久仰声华，坐屈冠盖，幸勿见讶。 ”遂延之上阶，与之对坐。

    Volume One of A New Tale of the Lamp-Cut

    The Record of the Celebration in the Palace of Water

    In the year of Jia Shen during the reign of Emperor Renzong, a scholar from Chaozhou named Yu Shanwen was sitting idly in his home during the day when suddenly two strong men, wearing yellow turbans and embroidered robes, entered from outside and paid their respects before him, saying, "We are here on behalf of Prince Guangli to invite you." Shanwen was startled and replied, "Prince Guangli is the deity of the sea, while I am but a mere mortal. The paths of the living and the dead are vastly different; how could we possibly meet?" The two men said, "Please just go with us, there is no need to refuse." So they accompanied him out of the south gate, where they saw a large red boat moored by the riverbank. They boarded the boat, and two yellow dragons carried it forward at the speed of wind and rain, reaching their destination in an instant. The boat stopped at the gate, and the two men went inside to report. Shortly after, they invited Shanwen to enter. Prince Guangli descended the steps to greet him, saying, "I have long admired your reputation and have humbly requested your presence. I hope you will not be surprised." He then invited Shanwen up the steps and they sat facing each other.

    9

    善文局蹐退逊。广利曰：“君居阳界，寡人处水府，不相统摄，可毋辞也。”善文曰：“大王贵重，仆乃一介寒儒，敢当盛礼！ ”固辞。广利左右有二臣曰鼋参军、鳖主簿者，趋出奏曰：“客言是也，王可从其所请，不宜自损威德，有失观视。 ”广利乃居中而坐，别设一榻于右，命善文坐。乃言曰：“敝居僻陋，蛟鳄之与邻，鱼蟹之与居，无以昭示神威，阐扬帝命。今欲别构一殿，命名灵德，工匠已举，木石咸具，所乏者惟上梁文尔。侧闻君子负不世之才，蕴济时之略，故特奉邀至此，幸为寞人制之。 ”即命近侍取白玉之砚，捧文犀之管，井鲛绡丈许，置善文前。善文俯首听命，一挥而就，文不加点。其词曰：

    Explanation

    9

    Shanwen, with a hesitant and deferential demeanor, declined the invitation. Guangli said, "You reside in the world of the living, while I dwell in the realm of the waters. We do not have a hierarchical relationship, so there is no need for you to refuse." Shanwen replied, "Your Majesty is of great importance, but I am merely a humble scholar. How dare I accept such a great honor!" He firmly declined. Two officials on either side of Guangli, named Yuan Canjun and Bie Zhubu, stepped forward and said, "The guest's words are correct. Your Majesty should grant his request. It would be unwise to diminish your authority and lose the respect of others." Guangli then sat in the center, and had a separate seat placed to his right, instructing Shanwen to sit. He then said, "My humble abode is remote and secluded, surrounded by dragons and crocodiles, and inhabited by fish and crabs. It is difficult to demonstrate divine power and proclaim imperial decrees. Now, I wish to construct a new hall named Lingde. The craftsmen have been gathered, and the materials are ready. The only thing lacking is the beam inscription. I have heard that you possess extraordinary talent and strategies for saving the world, so I have specially invited you here to write it for me." Immediately, he ordered his attendants to fetch a white jade inkstone, a writing brush made of rhinoceros horn, and a piece of fine silk fabric, placing them before Shanwen. Shanwen bowed and followed orders, finishing the inscription in one stroke without making any corrections. The words read:

    "O Great Spirit, you who dwell in the depths of the waters, your power is vast and your wisdom profound. You who command the creatures of the sea, your presence is awe-inspiring. Now, as we build this hall of Spiritual Virtue, may it serve as a testament to your divine majesty. May it stand as a beacon of your glory, a place where the world may come to seek your favor. We, your humble servants, offer this inscription with reverence and gratitude, hoping that it will bring you honor and that our endeavors may be blessed by your divine presence."

    Guangli was pleased with the inscription and praised Shanwen for his talent and skill. The new hall of Lingde was soon completed, and it became a place of great importance in the realm of the waters.

    10

    伏以天壤之间，海为最大；人物之内，神为最灵。既属香火之依归，可乏庙堂之壮丽？是用重营宝殿，新揭华名；挂龙骨以为梁，灵光耀日；缉鱼鳞而作瓦，瑞气蟠空。列明珠白璧之帘栊，接青雀黄龙之舸舰。琐窗启而海色在户，绣闼开而云影临轩。雨顺风调，镇南溟八千余里；天高地厚，垂后世亿万斯年。通江汉之朝宗，受溪湖之献纳。天吴紫凤，纷纭而到；鬼国罗剎，次第而来。岿然着鲁灵光，美哉如汉景福。控蛮荆而引瓯越，永壮宏观；叫闾阖而呈琅玕，宜兴善颂。遂为短唱，助举修梁。
    　　抛梁东，方丈蓬莱指顾中。笑看扶桑三百尺，金鸡啼罢日轮红。

    Explanation

    10

    Considering the vastness of the world, the sea is the greatest; within the realm of humans and deities, the gods are the most spiritual. Since it is a place of worship, can it lack the grandeur of the temple hall? Therefore, the treasure hall is rebuilt, and a new splendid name is unveiled; dragon bones are used as beams, and divine light shines like the sun; fish-scale tiles are made, and auspicious qi coils in the sky. Curtains adorned with pearls and white jade are hung, and boats decorated with blue birds and yellow dragons are connected. When the intricately carved windows are opened, the sea color is visible at the door; when the embroidered doors are opened, the cloud shadows appear at the veranda. Favorable weather conditions stabilize the southern sea for over eight thousand miles; the vastness of heaven and earth endures for billions of years. It connects the tributaries of the Yangtze and Han rivers, receiving offerings from streams and lakes. The Heavenly Fish and Purple Phoenix arrive in a flurry; the demons of the Ghost Country and the Rakshasas come in turn. It stands firm like the Lingguang of Lu, beautiful like the Jingfu of Han. It controls the southern regions and guides the eastern regions, always enhancing the grand view; it calls out to the gates of heaven and presents lapis lazuli, inspiring good praise. Therefore, a short song is composed to assist in raising the beam.

    Throwing the beam to the east, the mythical islands of Fangzhang and Penglai are in sight. Looking at the mythical tree of the sun standing three hundred feet tall, with the golden rooster's cry signaling the rise of the sun, the temple's spiritual and cultural significance is evident.

    11

    抛粱西，弱水流沙路不迷。后衣瑶池王母降，一双青鸟向人啼。
    　　抛梁南，巨浸漫漫万族涵。要识封疆宽几许？大鹏飞尽水如蓝。
    　　抛梁北，众星绚烂环辰极。遥瞻何处是中原？一发青山浮翠色。
    　　抛梁上，乘龙夜去陪天仗。袖中奏罢一封书，尽与苍生除祸瘴。
    　　抛梁下，水族纷纶承德化。清晓频闻赞拜声，江坤河伯朝灵驾。
    　　伏愿上粱之后，万族归仁，百灵仰德。珠宫贝阙，应无上之三光，衮衣绣裳，备人间之五福。
    　　书罢，进呈。广利大喜。卜日落戍，发使诣东西北三海，请其王赴庆殿之会。翌日，三神皆至，从者千乘万骑，神鲛毒蜃，踊跃后先，长鲸大鲲，奔驰左右，鱼头鬼面之卒，执旌旄而操戈戟者，又不知其几多也。是日，广利顶通天之冠，御绎纱之袍，秉碧玉之圭，趋迎于门，其礼甚肃。三神亦各盛其冠冕，严其剑佩，威仪极俨恪，但所服之袍，各随其方而色不同焉。叙暄凉毕，揖让而坐。

    Explanation

    11

    The West of Throw-Bridge, the weak river flows through the desert, the path is not lost. The Queen Mother of the West descends in her splendid attire from the Jade Pool, and a pair of green birds sing towards people.
    To the South of Throw-Bridge, the vast waters spread out, containing countless tribes. To know the width of the boundaries, how far does the great Peng bird fly until the water turns blue?
    To the North of Throw-Bridge, the stars shine brightly around the North Star. Looking far into the distance, where is the Central Plains? A single line of green mountains floats with a green hue.
    Above Throw-Bridge, riding a dragon at night to accompany the heavenly guard. After presenting a letter in the sleeve, it is all for the benefit of all living beings, removing calamities and miasmas.
    Below Throw-Bridge, the aquatic creatures are diverse and receive the grace of the divine. In the early morning, the sounds of praise and worship are frequent, as the River Gods and Lake Lords attend the divine carriage.
    May it be wished that after raising the ridge beam, all tribes return to benevolence, and all spirits revere virtue. The palaces of pearls and shell gates should reflect the three luminaries, and the dragon robes and embroidered skirts should be prepared for the five blessings.
    After writing, the document was presented. Guangli was greatly pleased. A day was chosen to settle in the camp, and envoys were sent to the three seas in the east, west, and north, inviting their kings to attend the celebration hall meeting. The next day, the three gods arrived, accompanied by thousands of chariots and tens of thousands of horses. Divine dolphins and toxic sea monsters leap and jump, long whales and great fish gallop left and right, soldiers with fish heads and ghost faces hold flags and wield spears and halberds, and their numbers are countless. On that day, Guangli wore a crown that reaches the sky, a robe of fine silk, and a tablet of green jade, hastening to welcome them at the door, the ceremony being very solemn. The three gods also wore their respective crowns, their swords and belts strict, their majesty extremely dignified and respectful, but the colors of their robes varied according to their directions. After exchanging greetings, they bowed and yielded, and then sat down.

    12

    善文亦以白衣坐于殿角，方欲与三神叙礼，忽东海广渊王座后有一从臣，铁冠而长髭者，号赤餫公，跃出广利前而请曰：“今兹贵殿落成，特为三王而设斯会，虽江汉之长，川泽之君，咸不得预席，其礼可谓严矣。彼白衣而末坐者为何人斯？乃敢于此唐突也！ ”广利曰：“此乃潮阳秀士余君善文也，吾构灵德殿，请其作上梁文，故留之在此尔。 ”广渊遽言曰：“文士在座，汝乌得多言？姑退！ ”赤餫公乃赧然而下。已而酒进乐作，有美女二十人，摇明珰，曳轻裾，于筵前舞凌波之队，歌凌波之词曰：
    　　若有人兮波之中，折杨柳兮采芙蓉。振瑶环兮琼佩，璆锵呜兮玲珑。衣翩翩兮若惊鸿，身矫矫兮如游龙。轻尘生兮罗袜，斜日照兮芳容。蹇独立兮西复东，羌可遏兮不可从。忽飘然而长往，御泠泠之轻凤。

    Explanation

    12

    Shanwen, dressed in plain clothes, sat at the corner of the hall. He was just about to exchange greetings with the three deities when suddenly, behind the seat of King Guangyuan of the East Sea, there was a court official with a hat of iron and long mustaches, known as Redyuan Gong. He leaped out in front of Guangli and asked, "This grand hall has now been completed, and this gathering is specially arranged for the three kings. Even the leaders of the Yangtze and Han rivers, and the kings of lakes and marshes, cannot participate in the banquet. The etiquette here is truly strict. What kind of person is that one dressed in plain clothes sitting at the end? How dare he be so bold?" Guangli replied, "This is Shanwen, a talented scholar from Chaoyang. I built the Lingde Hall and asked him to write the beam-lifting text, so I kept him here." Guangyuan immediately said, "With a scholar present, why are you saying so much? Retreat for now!" Redyuan Gong then blushed and stepped down. Soon after, the wine was served and the music began. Twenty beautiful women, shaking their bright pendants and dragging their light skirts, danced in front of the banquet, performing the Lingbo dance and singing the Lingbo lyrics:
    If there is someone in the waves, picking willows and plucking lotus flowers. Shaking jade rings and crystal pendants, ringing and tinkling melodiously. Dressed gracefully like a startled wild goose, their bodies agile like a swimming dragon. Light dust rises under their silk socks, the slanting sun illuminates their beautiful faces. Standing alone, they move back and forth, their grace is uncontainable and untraceable. Suddenly they float away, riding on the cool, light wind.

    13

    舞竟，复有歌童四十辈，倚新妆，飘香袖，于庭下舞采莲之队，歌采莲之曲曰：
    　　桂棹兮兰舟，泛波光兮远游。捐予玦兮别浦，解予佩兮芳洲。波摇摇兮舟不定，折荷花兮断荷柄。露何为兮沾裳？风何为兮吹鬓？棹歌起兮彩袖挥，翡翠散兮鸳鸯飞。张莲叶兮为盖，缉藕丝兮为衣。日欲落兮风更急，微烟生兮淡月出。早归来兮难久留，对芳华兮乐不可以终极。
    　　二舞既毕，然后击灵鼍之鼓，吹玉龙之笛，众乐毕陈，觥筹交错。于是东西北三神，共捧一觥，致善文前曰：“吾等僻处遐陬，不闻典礼，今日之会，获睹盛仪，而又幸遇大君子在座，光采倍增，愿为一诗以记之，使流传于龙官水府，抑亦一胜事也。不知可乎？ ”善文不可辞，遂献水宫庆会诗二十韵：
    　　帝德乾坤大，神功岭海安。
    　　渊宫舟栋宇，水路息波澜。
    　　列爵王侯贵，分符地界宽。
    　　威灵闻赫羿，事业保全完。
    　　南极常通奏，炎方永授官。

    Explanation

    13

    After the dance concluded, forty young singers appeared, dressed in fresh makeup and perfumed sleeves, performing a dance and singing a song about picking lotus flowers:
    　　On fragrant boats made of cinnamomum and orchid, sailing on the shimmering waves, far away on a journey. Throwing away my jade ring at the parting shore, unfastening my jade pendant at the fragrant island. The boat sways in the waves, uncertain and unstable, breaking off the lotus flower and cutting the stem. Why should the dew wet my clothes? Why should the wind blow through my hair? The oarsman's song rises, and the colorful sleeves are waved, the jade green birds scatter, and the mandarin ducks fly. Spreading lotus leaves as a canopy, weaving lotus threads into clothing. The sun is setting, and the wind is getting stronger; a light smoke rises, and a faint moon appears. Return early, it is hard to stay long; enjoying the beauty, happiness cannot be fully realized.
    　　After the two dances were completed, then the magical turtle drums were struck, and the jade dragon flutes were blown, all the music was presented, and wine glasses and chopsticks were mixed together. Thus, the three gods of east, west, and north, together holding a cup, presented it to the good man before him and said, "We live in remote corners, unaware of ceremonies; today's gathering allows us to witness a grand ceremony, and it is fortunate to have a great gentleman present, greatly enhancing the splendor. We wish to compose a poem to commemorate this, so that it may be passed down to the dragon palaces and water realms, which would also be a splendid event. Do you not think so?" The good man could not refuse, and thus presented a poem celebrating the gathering in twenty rhyming couplets:
    　　The imperial virtue is vast as heaven and earth, the divine power ensures peace in the mountains and seas.
    　　The deep palace has boats and buildings, the waterways are calm.
    　　Titles and ranks of nobility are bestowed, territories are wide and expansive.
    　　The divine power is known far and wide, achievements are complete and secure.
    　　Messages from the southern pole are always conveyed, officials are appointed in the southern regions.

    14

    登堂朝玉帛，设宴会衣冠。
    　　凤舞三檐盏，龙驮七宝鞍。
    　　传书双鲤跃，扶辇六鳌蟠。
    　　王母调金鼎，天妃捧玉盘。
    　　杯凝红琥珀，袖拂碧琅玕。
    　　座上湘灵舞，频将锦瑟弹。
    　　曲终汉女至，忙把翠旗看。
    　　瑞雾迷珠箔，祥烟绕画栏。
    　　屏开云母莹，帘卷水晶寒。
    　　共饮三危露，同餐九转丹。
    　　良辰宜酩酊，乐事称盘桓。
    　　异昧充喉舌，灵光照肺肝。
    　　浑如到兜率，又似梦邯郸。
    　　献酢陪高台，歌呼得尽欢。
    　　题诗传胜事，春色满毫端。
    　　诗进，座间大悦。已而，日落咸池，月生东谷，诸神大醉，倾扶而出，各归其国，车马骈阗之声，犹逾时不绝。明日，广利特没一宴，以谢善文。宴罢，以玻璃盘盛照夜之珠十，通天之犀二，为润笔之资，复命二使送之还郡。善文到家，携所得于波斯宝肆鬻焉，获财忆万计，遂为富族。后亦不以功名为意，弃家修道，遍游名山，不知所终。

    Explanation

    14

    Ascending the hall to receive jade and silk, a banquet is held for the gentry.
    The phoenix dances in three-tiered cups, the dragon carries a saddle adorned with seven treasures.
    Messages are delivered by leaping carp, six sea turtles support the carriage.
    The Queen Mother stirs a golden cauldron, the Heavenly Consort holds a jade plate.
    Cups made of red amber, sleeves brushing against green jade-like stones.
    On the seat, Lady Xiang Ling dances, frequently playing the lute.
    At the end of the performance, a maiden from the Han dynasty arrives, holding a green flag.
    Auspicious mist obscures pearl curtains, auspicious smoke curls around painted railings.
    Screens made of mica gleam, curtains of crystal are drawn back.
    Together, they drink the dew of the Three Dangers, eat the Nine Transformations Pill.
    A good time is fit for intoxication, pleasant events are worthy of lingering.
    Exotic flavors fill the mouth, spiritual light illuminates the inner organs.
    As if one had reached the Tushita Heaven, or as if dreaming in Handan.
    Offering wine and singing on a high platform, joy and festivity are fully enjoyed.
    Writing poetry to record glorious events, spring colors fill the brush.
    The poem is presented, the audience is delighted. Soon, the sun sets in the western sea, the moon rises in the eastern valley, the gods become drunk and stagger out, each returning to their realm, the sound of chariots and horses lined up in abundance still echoing after a while. The next day, a special banquet is held to thank the skilled writer. After the banquet, a glass dish holds ten night-lighting pearls and two sky-reaching rhinoceros horns, as a reward for the writer, two envoys are sent to return him to the prefecture. The writer arrives home, selling the treasures in a Persian jewelry shop, gaining wealth in the tens of thousands, becoming a wealthy family. Later, he no longer cares about fame and fortune, abandons his family to seek the Dao, wandering through famous mountains, his ultimate fate unknown.

    15

    三山福地志
    　　元自实，山东人也。生而质钝，不通诗书。家颇丰殖，以田庄为业。同里有缪君者，除得闽中一官，缺少路费，于自实处假银二百两。自实以乡党相处之厚，不问其文券，如数贷之。至正末，山东大乱，自实为群盗听劫，家计一空。时陈有定据守福建，七闽颇安。自实乃挈奏子由海道趋福州，将访缪君而投托焉。至则缪君果在有定幕下，当道用事，威权隆重，门户赫弈。自实大喜，然而患难之余，跋涉道途，衣裳褴缕，客貌憔粹，未敢遽见也。乃于城中僦屋，安顿其妻孥，整饰其冠服，卜日而往。适值缪君之出，拜于马首。初似不相识，及叙乡井，通姓名，方始惊谢。即延之入室，待以宾主之礼。良久，啜茶而罢。明日，再往，酒果三杯而已，落落无顾念之意，亦不言银两之事。

    Explanation

    15

    Records of the Three Mountains as Auspicious Places

    Mr. Zizhi was from Shandong. He was born with a dull nature and unable to understand poetry and books. His family was quite wealthy, and they engaged in managing estates. There was a Mr. Miao in the same village who was appointed to an official position in Fujian but lacked travel expenses. He borrowed two hundred taels of silver from Mr. Zizhi. Mr. Zizhi, trusting their relationship as fellow villagers, did not ask for a written document and lent the full amount. At the end of the Zhizheng era, Shandong was in chaos, and Mr. Zizhi was robbed by a band of thieves, leaving his family's wealth completely depleted. At that time, Chen Youding was holding Fujian, and the seven regions of Fujian were relatively peaceful. Mr. Zizhi then took his son and traveled by sea to Fuzhou, intending to visit Mr. Miao and seek his protection. When they arrived, Mr. Miao was indeed serving under Chen Youding, holding power and influence, with great authority and prestige, and a prominent and influential household. Mr. Zizhi was very happy, but after the hardships, he had traveled long and arduous journeys, wearing tattered clothes and looking haggard and worn out, so he did not dare to see Mr. Miao immediately. Instead, he rented a house in the city, settled his wife and children, dressed up his attire, and chose a day to go. Just as Mr. Miao was about to leave, Mr. Zizhi bowed at the head of the horse. At first, Mr. Miao seemed not to recognize him, but when they talked about their hometown and introduced their names, Mr. Miao was surprised and thanked him. He then invited Mr. Zizhi into the room and treated him with the courtesy of a host and guest. After a long time, they drank tea and then parted. The next day, Mr. Zizhi went again, and they had only three cups of wine and fruit. Mr. Miao treated him coldly and without concern, and he did not mention the matter of the silver.

    16

    自实还家，旅寓荒凉，妻孥怨詈曰：“汝万里投人，听干何事？今为三杯薄酒所卖，即便不出一言，吾等何所望也！ ”自实不得已，又明日，再往访焉，则似已厌之矣。自实方欲启口，缪君遽曰：“向者承借路费，铭心不忘，但一宦萧条，俸入微薄，故人远至，岂敢辜恩，望以文券付还，则当如数陆续酬纳也。 ”自实悚然曰：“与君共同乡里，自少交契深密，承命周急，素无文券，今日何以出此言也？ ”缪君正色曰：“文券承有之，但恐兵火之后，君失之耳。然券之有无，某亦不较，惟望宽其程限，使得致力焉。 ”自实唯唯而出，怪其言辞矫妄，负德若此，羝羊触藩，进退维谷。半月之后，再登其门，惟以温言接之，终无一钱之惠。展转推托，遂及半年。市中有一小庵，自实往缪君之居，适当其中路，每于门下憩息。庵主轩辕翁者，有道之士也，见其往来颇久，与之叙话，因而情熟。

    Explanation

    16

    Zi Shi returned home, staying in a desolate and lonely place. His wife and children complained and scolded him, saying, "You traveled thousands of miles to seek help, what did you do? Now you are sold by three cups of thin wine, even if you didn't say a word, what do we hope for?" Zi Shi had no choice but to visit again the next day. The recipient seemed to have become tired of him. As Zi Shi was about to speak, the recipient suddenly said, "I remember with deep gratitude the loan of travel expenses you gave me before. However, as a low-ranking official in a poor condition with a meager salary, how could I betray your kindness? I hope to repay with a promissory note, and I will repay gradually in full." Zi Shi was startled and said, "We are from the same hometown, and we have known each other since childhood with a close bond. I received your help in times of need, and there was never a written agreement. Why are you saying this now?" The recipient said seriously, "The promissory note is still there, but I am afraid after the war, you may have lost it. However, whether the note exists or not, I do not care. I only hope for a longer repayment period so that I can make efforts." Zi Shi nodded and left, finding his words exaggerated and false, betraying his kindness like this. He was in a dilemma, unable to move forward or backward. After half a month, he visited again, but the recipient received him with warm words, finally giving no money. Repeatedly evading and delaying, until half a year later. There was a small temple in the market, on the way to the recipient's residence, where Zi Shi often rested at the door. The temple's owner, Master Xuan Yuan, was a wise man. Seeing him come and go for a long time, he talked with him, and they became familiar.

    17

    时值季冬，已迫新岁，自实穷居无聊，诣缪君之居，拜且泣曰：“新正在迩，妻子饥寒，囊乏一钱，瓶无储粟。向者银两，今不敢求，但愿捐斗水而活涸辙之枯，下壶飨而救翳桑之饿，此则故人之赐也。伏望怜之悯之，哀之恤之！ ”遂匍匐于地。缪君扶之起，屈指计日之数，而告之曰： “更及一旬，当是除夕，君可于家专待，吾分禄米二右及银二锭，令人驰送于宅，以为过岁之资，幸勿以少为怪。 ”且又再三丁宁。毋用他出以候之。自实感谢而退。归以缪君之言慰其妻子。至日，举家悬望，自实端坐于床，令椎子于里门觇之。须臾，奔入曰：“有人负米至矣。”急出俟焉，则越其庐而不顾。自实犹谓来人不识其家，趋往问之，则曰：“张员外之馈馆宾者也。 ”默然而返。顷之，稚子又入告曰：“有人携钱来矣。 ”急出迓焉，则过其门而不入。再住扣之，则曰：“李县令之赆游客者也。”怃然而惭。

    Explanation

    17

    As the last month of winter approached, the new year was drawing near. Self-Realized, living in poverty and boredom, visited Master Miao's residence and knelt, weeping, as he said, "The new year is almost here, and my wife and children are suffering from hunger and cold. My purse lacks even a single coin, and my jar has no stored grain. The silver I received before, I dare not ask for now. I only wish to give a measure of water to revive a fish stranded in a dried-up ditch, or offer a pot of food to save someone starving in the shade of a mulberry tree. This would be a favor from an old friend. I humbly beg for your pity, compassion, and help!" He then prostrated himself on the ground. Master Miao helped him up, counted the days on his fingers, and said, "In ten more days, it will be New Year's Eve. You can stay at home and wait. I will send two measures of grain and two ingots of silver. I will have someone deliver them to your house as funds for the new year. Please do not be surprised by the small amount." And he repeatedly warned him, "Do not leave your home to wait." Self-Realized thanked him and left, returning home to comfort his wife and children with what Master Miao had said. On that day, the whole family anxiously awaited. Self-Realized sat calmly on the bed, sending someone to the gate to watch for the delivery. Soon, the messenger ran in and said, "Someone is carrying grain here!" He rushed out to meet them, but they passed by his house without stopping. Self-Realized still thought the deliverers did not recognize his home and hurried to ask them. They said, "This is from Mr. Zhang, who is sending it to his guest." He silently returned. Soon after, the young child came in and reported, "Someone is bringing money!" He rushed out to greet them, but they passed by his door without entering. He stopped them and asked, "This is from County Magistrate Li, who is sending it to his guest." He looked dejected and felt ashamed.

    18

    如是者凡数度。至晚，竟绝影响。明日，岁旦矣，反为所误，粒米束薪，俱不及办，妻子相向而哭。自实不胜其愤，阴砺白刃，坐以待旦。鸡鸣鼓绝，径投缪君之门，将俟其出而刺之。是时，晨方未启，道无行人，惟小庵中轩辕翁方明烛转经，当门而坐，见自实前行，有奇形异状之鬼数十辈从之，或握刀剑，或执椎凿，披头露体，势甚凶恶；一饭之顷，则自实复回，有金冠玉佩之士百余人随之，或击幢盖，或举旌幡，和容婉色，意甚安闲。轩辕翁叵测，谓其已死矣。诵经已罢，急往访之，则自实固无恙。坐定，轩辕翁问曰：“今日之晨，子将奚适？何其去之匆匆，而回之缓缓也？愿得一闻。 ”自实不敢隐，具言：“缪君之不义，令我狼狈！今早实砺霜刃于怀，将往杀之以快意，及至其门，忽自思曰：‘彼实得罪于吾，妻子何尤焉。且又有老母在堂，今若杀之，其家何所依？宁人负我，毋我负人也。 ’遂隐忍而归耳。 ”

    Explanation

    18

    In this manner, it happened several times. By evening, he finally completely cut off all traces. The next day was New Year's Day, but he was misled by the situation, and basic necessities like grains and firewood were not available, causing his wife and children to cry facing each other. Zi Shi could not bear his anger any longer and secretly sharpened his blade, sitting and waiting for dawn. At dawn, he directly went to the door of Mr. Miao, intending to wait for him to come out and stab him. At that time, the morning had not yet opened, and the road was empty. Suddenly, dozens of ghosts with strange shapes and forms appeared behind him, some holding swords and spears, others holding hammers and chisels, bareheaded and naked, with a very fierce appearance. In a moment, Zi Shi returned, followed by over a hundred gentlemen with golden crowns and jade pendants, some hitting the canopy, others raising the banners, with gentle demeanor and pleasant expressions, the intention very calm. The elderly man,轩辕翁, was unpredictable and thought that Zi Shi had died. After finishing reciting the scriptures, he hurried to visit Zi Shi, only to find that Zi Shi was still alive. Sitting down,轩辕翁 asked, "Today's morning, where were you going? Why did you leave so quickly and return so slowly? I would like to hear about it." Zi Shi dared not hide and spoke in detail: "Mr. Miao's injustice has made me so miserable! This morning, I secretly sharpened my blade, intending to go and kill him to satisfy my anger. When I arrived at his door, I suddenly thought to myself: 'He has indeed wronged me, but why should my wife and children suffer? Moreover, my mother is old and needs support. If I kill him, his family will have no one to rely on. Rather let others wrong me, than I wrong others.' So I restrained myself and returned."

    19

    轩辕翁闻之，稽首而贺曰：“吾子将有后禄，神明已知之矣。”自实问其故。翁曰：“子一念之恶，而凶鬼至；一念之善，而福神临。如影之随形，如声之应响，固知暗室之内，造次之间，不可荫心而为恶，不可造罪而损德也。 ”因具言其所见而慰抚之，且以钱米少许周其急。然而自实终郁郁不乐。至晚，自投于三神山下八角井中。其水忽然开辟，两岸皆石壁如削，中有狭径，仅通行履。自实扪壁而行，将数百步，壁尽路穷，出一弄口，则天地明朗，日月照临，俨然别一世界也。见大宫殿，金书其榜曰：“三山福地。

    Explanation

    19

    Laoxuanyuan heard this and bowed respectfully, congratulating, "Your son will have future rewards; the divine has already known." Zishí asked for the reason. The old man said, "A single thought of evil brings forth an evil spirit; a single thought of goodness brings forth a benevolent spirit. It is like a shadow that follows its form, or an echo that responds to sound. Therefore, one must not harbor evil in one's heart, nor commit sins that harm virtue, even in secret or in haste." He then explained what he had seen and comforted him, giving him a small amount of money and rice to help him in his urgent need. However, Zishí remained gloomy and unhappy. By evening, he threw himself into the eight-cornered well at the foot of the Three Divine Mountains. The water suddenly parted, revealing stone walls on both sides as sharp as cut, with a narrow path inside, barely wide enough for a person to walk. Zishí felt his way along the wall, walking several hundred steps, until the path ended and he emerged at a small opening. There, the sky and earth were clear, the sun and moon shone down, and it was clearly a different world. He saw a grand palace, with golden characters on the signboard reading "Three Divine Mountains of Blessing."

    20

    ”自实瞻仰而入，长廊昼静，古殿烟消，徘徊四顾，阒无人踪，惟闻钟盘之声，隐隐于云外。饥馁颇甚，行末能前，困卧石坛之侧。忽一道土，曳青霞之裾，振明月之佩，至前呼起之，笑而问曰：“翰林识旅游滋味乎？”自实拱而对曰：“旅游滋味，则尽足矣。翰林之称，一何误乎？ ”道士曰：“子不忆草西蕃诏于兴圣殿乎？ ”自实曰：“某山东鄙人，布衣贱士，生岁四十，目不知书，平生未尝游览京国，何有草诏之说乎？”道士曰：“子应为饥火所恼，不暇记前事耳。 ”乃于袖中出梨枣数枚令食之，曰：“此谓交梨火枣也。食之当知过去未来事。”

    Explanation

    20

    Zi Shi entered the temple after gazing in. The long corridor was quiet during the day, and the incense from the ancient temple had dissipated. Wandering and looking around, there was no sign of anyone. Only the faint sound of the temple bells and drums could be heard, coming from afar. Hungry and weak, he could not move forward and lay tired beside the stone altar. Suddenly, a Taoist priest appeared, dragging a robe of blue clouds and shaking a jade pendant like a bright moon. He approached and called Zi Shi up, smiling and asking, "Do you know the taste of traveling, Scholar?" Zi Shi bowed and replied, "The taste of traveling, I have had enough of it. How mistaken the title of Scholar is!" The Taoist priest said, "Do you not remember drafting the imperial edict for the Western Regions in the Xing Sheng Temple?" Zi Shi replied, "I am a simple man from Shandong, a humble scholar. Forty years old, never having read a book, I have never traveled to the capital. How could there be such a thing as drafting an imperial edict?" The Taoist priest said, "You must be troubled by hunger, not having the time to remember past events." He then took out a few pears and jujubes from his sleeve and offered them to eat, saying, "These are called the pear of exchange and the jujube of fire. Eating them will allow you to know past and future events."

    21

    自实食讫，惺然明悟，因记为学士时，草西蕃沼于大都兴圣殿侧，如昨日焉。遂请于道士曰：“某前世造何罪而今受此报耶？”道士曰：“子亦无罪，但在职之时，以文学自高，不肯汲引后进，故今世令君愚懵而不识字；以爵位自尊，不肯接纳游士，故今世令君漂泊而无所依耳。 ”自实因指当世达官而问之曰：“某人为丞相。而贪饕不止，贿赂公行，异日当受何报？ ”道士曰：“彼乃无厌鬼王，地下有十炉以铸其横财，今亦福满矣，当受幽囚之祸。 ”又问曰：“某人为平章，而不戢军士，杀害良民，异日当受何报？ ”道士曰：“彼乃多杀鬼王，有阴兵三百，皆铜头铁额，辅之以助其虐，今亦命衰矣，当受割截之殃。

    Explanation

    21

    Upon finishing his meal, he became clearly awake and enlightened, remembering that he had once served as a scholar and drafted the West Famine Pool beside the Xingsheng Temple in the capital, as if it were yesterday. He then asked the Taoist priest, "What sin did I commit in my past life that I now suffer this retribution?" The priest replied, "You are not guilty. But while in office, you held your literary talent in high regard and did not help promote younger scholars, so in this life you are ignorant and illiterate; you held your position in high regard and did not accept wandering scholars, so in this life you are wandering without support. " Zi Shi then pointed to a high-ranking official of the present day and asked, "This person is the Chancellor. He is never satisfied with his greed, openly practices bribery, and what punishment will he face in the future?" The priest said, "He is the king of insatiable greed, with ten furnaces in the underworld to cast his ill-gotten wealth, and now his fortune is full, so he will suffer the disaster of imprisonment. " He asked again, "This person is the Pingzhang, and he does not restrain his soldiers, killing innocent people. What punishment will he face in the future?" The priest said, "He is the king of many killings, with three hundred dark soldiers, all with copper heads and iron foreheads, to assist him in his cruelty. Now his fate has declined, and he will suffer the calamity of being cut up."

    22

    ”又问：“某人为监司，而刑罚不振；某人为郡守，而赋役不均；某人为宣慰，不闻所宣之何事；某人为经略，不闻所略之何方，然则当受何报也？ ”道士曰：“此等皆已杻械加其身，缧绁系其颈，腐肉秽骨，待戮余魂，何足算也！ ”自实因举缪君负债之事。道士曰：“彼乃王将军之库子，财物岂得妄动耶？”道士因言：“不出三年，世运变革，大祸将至，甚可畏也。汝宜择地而居，否则恐预池鱼之殃。”自实乞指避兵之地。

    Explanation

    22

    "Another person asked, 'If someone is a high-ranking official responsible for overseeing local administration, but fails to enforce the law; if someone is a prefectural governor, but taxes and labor services are not evenly distributed; if someone is an official responsible for pacifying and consoling local areas, but does not know what is being announced; if someone is a high-ranking military or administrative official, but does not know which direction is being conquered, then what kind of punishment should they receive?' The Taoist replied, 'All of these individuals have already been subjected to handcuffs and shackles, their necks bound with chains, their bodies reduced to rotten flesh and filthy bones, awaiting the fate of their souls after execution. The Taoist then added, 'Within three years, the world will undergo a transformation, great disaster will come, and it is very frightening. You should choose a place to live, otherwise you might share the calamity of the fish in the pond.' Zi Shi asked for a place to avoid the war."

    23

    道士曰：“福清可矣。 ”又曰：“不若福宁。 ”言讫，谓自实曰：“汝到此久，家人悬望，今可归矣。”自实告以无路，道士指一径令其去，遂再拜而别。行二里许，于山后得一穴出，到家，则已半月矣。急携妻子径往福宁村中，垦田治圃而居。挥镢之际，铮然作声，获瘫银四锭，家遂稍康。其后张氏夺印，达丞相被拘，大军临城，陈平章遭掳，其余官吏多不保其首领，而缪君为王将军者所杀，家资皆归之焉。以岁月记之，仅及三载，而道士之言悉验矣。
    　　华亭逢故人记
    　　松江士人有全、贾二子者，皆富有文学，豪放自得，嗜酒落魄，不拘小节，每以游侠自任。至正末，张氏居有浙西，松江为属郡。二子来往其间，大言雄辩，旁若无人。豪门叵族，望风承接，惟恐居后。全有诗曰：

    23

    The Taoist priest said, "Fuqing is acceptable." He then said, "It is not as good as Funing." After speaking, he told Zi Shi, "You have been here for a long time, your family is anxiously waiting, you may return now." Zi Shi informed him that there was no way out, and the Taoist priest pointed a path for him to leave. He then bowed twice and took his leave. After walking about two miles, he emerged from a cave at the back of the mountain and arrived home, but it had been half a month. He hurriedly took his wife and children directly to the village of Funing, where he cultivated land and tended a garden to make a living. While swinging the hoe, a metallic sound was heard, and he found four ingots of silver. His family then gradually became more prosperous.

    Later, Zhang seized the seal, the Grand Secretary was detained, the army approached the city, Chen was captured, other officials could not protect their heads, and Master Miao was killed by General Wang, whose family assets were all taken. Counting by years, it was only three years, and the Taoist's words were all proven true.

    A Record of Meeting an Old Friend in Huating

    There were two scholars named Quan and Jia from Songjiang. Both were rich in literature, free-spirited, fond of wine, and unconcerned with minor details. They often took on the role of a wandering knight. During the late Yuan Dynasty, Zhang held power in Zhejiang West, and Songjiang was a subordinate prefecture. The two scholars came and went among the powerful, speaking grandly and arguing forcefully, as if no one else was present. Wealthy families and powerful clans welcomed them, fearing to be left behind. Quan wrote a poem:

    Gray hair crowns the head, feeling the two hairs.
    The west wind penetrates the phoenix robe with its chill.
    Looking up at the sky, he dared not exhale deeply,
    Transforming into a rainbow ten thousand feet high.

    24

    贾亦有诗曰：
    　　四海干戈未息肩，书生岂合老林泉！
    　　袖中一把龙泉剑，撑拄东南半壁天。
    　　其诗大率类是，人益信其自负。吴元年，国兵围姑苏，未拨。上洋人钱鹤皋起兵援张氏，二子自以严庄、尚让为比，杖策登门，参其谋议，遂陷嘉兴等郡。未几，师溃，皆赴水死。洪武四年。华亭士人石若虚，有故出近郊。素与二子友善，忽遇之于途，随行僮仆救人，气象宛如平昔。迎谓若虚曰：“石君无恙乎？”若虚忘其已死，与之揖让，班荆而坐子野，谈论逾时。全忽慨然长叹曰：“诸葛长民有言：‘贫贱长思富贵，富贵复履危机。 ’此语非确论。苟慕富贵，危机岂能避？世间宁有扬州鹤耶？丈夫不能流芳百世，亦当遗臭万年。刘黑闼既立为汉东王，临死乃云：‘我本在家锄莱，为高雅贤辈所误至此！ ’陋哉斯言，足以发千古一笑也！ ”贾曰：“黑闼何足道！如汉之田横，唐之李密，亦可谓铁中铮铮者也。

    Explanation

    24

    The Scholar had a poem that went:

    Across the land, the turmoil of war has not ceased,
    How could a scholar be suited to live in seclusion in the mountains and forests!
    In my sleeve, I carry a sword of Qilin,
    Supporting half of the southeastern sky.

    His poems were generally of this kind, and people further believed in his self-confidence. In the first year of the Wu dynasty, the national army besieged Suzhou, but it was not yet conquered. A person from Shangyang named Qian He Gao raised an army to support the Zhang clan. The two sons compared themselves to Yan Zhuang and Shang Rang, and they carried their staff to the door of the Zhang clan, participating in their plans, and then captured Jiaxing and other counties. Not long after, the army was defeated, and they all drowned. In the fourth year of the Hongwu era, a scholar from Huating named Shi Ruoxu had an errand in the suburbs. He had always been friendly with the two sons, and he suddenly encountered them on the road. They were accompanied by servants who were trying to save people, and their demeanor was just as it had been before. They greeted Shi Ruoxu and said, "Shi Jun, are you well?" Shi Ruoxu forgot that they were already dead, and he bowed and conversed with them, and they sat on mats of pine branches. They talked for a long time. One of them suddenly sighed deeply and said, "Zhuge Changmin once said, 'Those in poverty often think of wealth, and those in wealth often face danger.' This statement is not a definitive truth. If one desires wealth, how can one avoid danger? How can there be a crane in Yangzhou? A man cannot leave a good name for a hundred generations, but he should leave a bad name for ten thousand years. Liu Heti, after becoming the King of Han Dong, spoke these words on his deathbed: 'I was originally at home tilling the fields, but I was misled by the high-minded and virtuous ones to this point!' What a vulgar statement, it is enough to make people laugh for a thousand years!" The Scholar said, "Liu Heti is not worth mentioning! Like Han's Tianheng and Tang's Li Mi, they too can be considered shining stars in iron."

    25

    横始与汉祖俱南面称孤，耻更称臣，逃居诲岛，可以死矣，乃眩于大王小侯之语，行至东都而死。密之起兵，唐祖以书贺之，推为盟主，及兵败入关，乃望以台司见处，其无知识如此！大丈夫死即死矣，何忍向人喉下取气耶？夫韩信建炎汉之业，卒受诛夷；刘文静启晋阳之祚，终加戮辱。彼之功臣尚尔，于他人何有哉！ ”全曰：“骆宾王佐李敬业起兵，檄武氏之恶，及兵败也，复能优游灵隐，咏桂子天香之句。黄巢扰乱唐室，罪下容诛，至于事败，乃削发被缁，逃遁踪迹，题诗云：‘铁衣着尽着僧衣。 ’若二人者，身为首恶，而终能脱祸，可谓智术之深矣。 ”贾笑曰：“审如此，吾辈当愧之矣！ ”全遽曰：“故人在坠，不必闲论他事，徒增伤感尔。 ”因解所御绿裘，令仆于近村质酒而饮。酒至，饮数巡，若虚请于二子曰： “二公平日篇什，播在人口，今日之会，可无佳制以记之乎？ ”于是筹思移时，全诗先成，即吟曰：

    Explanation

    25

    Xiang Yu, at the beginning, ruled alongside Liu Bang (汉祖) as a king (南面称孤), ashamed to submit as a vassal (耻更称臣), fled to the island of Hui (诲岛), where he could have died, but was deceived by the words of great kings and petty princes (眩于大王小侯之语), and died while traveling to the eastern capital (东都). Li Mi (密) led a rebellion, and the founder of the Tang Dynasty (唐祖) sent a letter congratulating him, proclaiming him as the leader of an alliance (推为盟主), but after his defeat and retreat into the Guanzhong region (及兵败入关), he hoped to be appointed as a high-ranking official (乃望以台司见处), showing his lack of wisdom (其无知识如此)! A man of integrity dies when he must (大丈夫死即死矣), how can one bear to live by breathing on someone's throat (何忍向人喉下取气耶)? Han Xin (韩信) established the Han Dynasty (建炎汉之业), but finally suffered execution (卒受诛夷); Liu Wenjing (刘文静) initiated the rise of the Tang Dynasty from Jinyang (启晋阳之祚), but finally suffered humiliation (终加戮辱). Even their meritorious ministers were like this (彼之功臣尚尔), what about others (于他人何有哉)! "Luo Binwang (骆宾王) assisted Li Jingye (李敬业) in a rebellion, drafting a declaration exposing the evils of the Wu family (檄武氏之恶), and after his defeat, he was able to live in leisure at Lingyin Temple, composing verses praising the fragrance of osmanthus flowers (咏桂子天香之句). Huang Chao (黄巢) disrupted the Tang Dynasty, deserving punishment, but after his defeat, he shaved his head and dressed in monk's robes (削发被缁), escaping his pursuers, and wrote a poem: 'Having worn out his armor, he now wears monk's robes (铁衣着尽着僧衣).' If these two men, as the chief villains (身为首恶), could ultimately escape disaster (终能脱祸), their wisdom and strategy were indeed profound (可谓智术之深矣)." Jia (贾) laughed and said, "If it is indeed so, we should be ashamed of ourselves!" Quan (全) quickly replied, "The old people have fallen (故人在坠), there's no need to discuss other matters, it only adds to sadness (徒增伤感尔)." He then unbuttoned the green fur coat he was wearing (解所御绿裘), instructing his servant to exchange it for wine in the nearby village (令仆于近村质酒而饮). When the wine arrived, they drank several rounds, and Ruo Xu (若虚) asked the two men, "Your writings, widely spoken of (播在人口), today's gathering, can we not have a fine work to commemorate it (可无佳制以记之乎)?" After thinking for a while, Quan's poem was completed first, and he immediately recited it:

    26

    几年兵火接天涯，白骨丛中度岁华。
    　　杜宇有冤能泣血，邓攸无子可传家。
    　　当时自诧辽东豕，今日翻成井底蛙。

    　　漠漠荒郊鸟乱飞，人民城郭叹都非。
    　　沙沉枯骨何须葬，血污游魂不得归。
    　　麦饭无人作寒食，绨袍有泪哭斜晖。
    　　生存零落皆如此，惟恨平生壮志违。
    　　吟已，若虚骇曰：“二公平日吟咏极宕，今日之作，何其哀伤之过，与畴昔大不类耶？ ”二人相顾无语，但愀然长啸数声。须臾，酒罄，告别而去。行及十数步，阒无所见。若虚大惊，始悟其死久矣。但见林梢烟瞑，岭首日沈，乌啼鹊噪于丛薄之间而已。急投前村酒家，访其历以取质酒之裘视之，则触手纷纷而碎，若蝶翅之抟风焉。若虚借宿酒家，明早急回。其后再下敢经由是路矣。

    Explanation

    26

    For several years, war has connected the ends of the earth, and we have spent our years among heaps of bones. Du Yu, with his grievances, wept blood, and Deng You, without children, could not continue his family line. At the time, they boasted like pigs of Liaodong, but today they have become frogs at the bottom of a well. Who is the master of this spring scene, as wildflowers bloom amidst thorns and sand? In the vast, desolate wilderness, birds fly chaotically, and people and cities sigh at the change. The bones of the dead are buried in the sand, why bother to bury them, and the souls stained with blood cannot return. No one makes cold food offerings, and the coarse robe weeps tears under the slanting evening light. All of us living are scattered like this, and the only regret is that my lifelong ambitions were thwarted. After reciting, Ruoxu was shocked and said, "The two gentlemen usually recited very freely, but today's work, how much more sorrowful than usual, how different from before?" They looked at each other in silence, but sighed deeply and let out a few long cries. Soon, the wine ran out, and they bid farewell and left. Walking a dozen steps, they saw nothing, and Ruoxu was shocked, finally realizing that he had been dead for a long time. They only saw the forest edges shrouded in smoke, and the mountain peaks bathed in sunset, with only crows and magpies chirping in the dense undergrowth. They hurried to a wine shop in the nearby village, checked the ledger, and examined the fur coat used as collateral, which crumbled to pieces upon touch, like butterfly wings caught in the wind. Ruoxu stayed overnight at the wine shop and hurried back the next morning. After this, he dared not pass this way again.

    27

    金凤钗记
    　　大德中，扬州富人吴防御居春风楼侧，与宦族崔君为邻，交契甚厚。崔有子曰兴哥，防御有女曰兴娘，俱在襁褓。崔君因求女为兴哥妇，防御许之，以金凤钗一只为约。既而崔君游宦远方，凡一十五载，并无一字相闻。女处闺闱，年十九矣。其母谓防御曰：“崔家郎君一去十五载，不通音耗，兴娘长成矣，不可执守前言，令其挫失时节也。 ”防御曰：“吾已许吾故人矣，况成约已定，吾岂食言者也。 ”女亦望生不至，因而感疾，沉绵枕席，半岁而终。父母哭之恸。

    Explanation

    27

    The Gold Phoenix Hairpin Record

    During the Da De period, a wealthy merchant named Wu lived next to the Spring Wind Pavilion in Yangzhou, and he was a close friend of Cui, an official. Wu had a daughter named Xingniang, and Cui had a son named Xingge, both of whom were infants. Cui asked Wu to let his daughter marry his son, and Wu agreed, using a gold phoenix hairpin as a symbol of the promise. Soon after, Cui went on a distant official tour and did not communicate for fifteen years.

    Xingniang, now living in the inner chambers, was nineteen years old. Her mother said to Wu, "Cui's son has been away for fifteen years without any news, and Xingniang has grown up. We cannot keep to our previous words and let her lose her prime." Wu replied, "I have already promised my old friend, and the agreement is already made. How could I go back on my word?"

    Xingniang, hoping for her husband's return, fell ill and lay bedridden for half a year before passing away. Her parents mourned deeply.

    28

    临敛，母持金凤钗抚尸而泣曰：“此汝夫家物也，今汝已矣，吾留此安用！ ”遂簪于其髻而殡焉。殡之两月，而崔生至。防御延接之，访问其故，则曰：“父为宣德府理官而卒，母亦先逝数年矣，今已服除，故不远千里而至此。 ”防御下泪曰：“兴娘薄命，为念君故，得疾，于两月前饮恨而终，今已殡之矣。 ”因引生入室，至其灵几前，焚楮钱以告之，举家号恸。防御谓生曰：“郎君父母既殁，到途又远，今既来此，可便于吾家宿食。故人之子，即吾子也，勿以兴娘殁故，自同外人。 ”

    Explanation

    28

    At the time of her death, her mother held a gold phoenix hairpin and wept over her body, saying, "This is something from your husband's family. Now that you are gone, what use would I have for this?" She then placed the hairpin in her hair and buried her. Two months later, Cui arrived. The defense official welcomed him warmly and inquired about the reason for his visit. Cui replied, "My father was a magistrate of Xuande Prefecture and has passed away, and my mother also died several years ago. I have now completed the mourning period and have traveled a long distance to reach here." The defense official shed tears and said, "Xing娘 had a short life. She fell ill because she thought of you and died with regret two months ago. She has been buried." He then led Cui into the room, to the table before her spirit tablet, and burned paper money to inform her. The whole family wailed in grief. The defense official said to Cui, "Your parents have both passed away, and the journey was long. Now that you are here, you can stay and eat at our house. The son of an old friend is like my own son. Do not treat yourself as an outsider because Xing娘 has died."

    29

    即令搬挈行李，于门侧小斋安泊。将及半月。时值清明，防御以女殁之故，举家上冢。兴娘有妹曰庆娘，年十七矣，是日亦同往。惟留生在家看守。至暮而归，天已曛黑，生于门左迎接；有轿二乘，前轿已入，后轿至生前，似有物堕地，铿然作声，生俟其过，急往拾之，乃金凤钗一只也。欲纳还于内，则中门已阖，不可得而入矣。遂还小斋，明烛独坐。自念婚事不成，只身孤苦，寄迹人入门，亦非久计，长叹数声。方欲就枕，忽闻剥啄扣门声，问之不答，斯须复扣，如是者三度。乃启关视之，则一美姝立于门外，见户开，遽搴裙而入。生大惊。女低容敛气，向生细语曰：“郎不识妾耶？妾即兴娘之妹庆娘也。向者投钗轿下，郎拾得否？ ”即挽生就寝。生以其父待之厚，辞曰：“不敢。

    Explanation

    29

    Immediately, he was ordered to pack his belongings and settle in a small study near the gate. Nearly half a month had passed. It was Qingming Festival, and because of the death of a female member, the entire family went to the ancestral tomb. Xing娘 had a sister named Qing娘, who was seventeen years old, and she also went along that day. Only Sheng was left at home to guard the house. By evening, they returned, and the sky was already dark. Sheng stood on the left side of the gate to greet them. There were two carriages; the first had already entered, and the second approached Sheng. It seemed as though something had fallen to the ground, making a clinking sound. Sheng waited for the carriage to pass, then quickly picked it up and found it to be a gold phoenix hairpin. He wanted to return it inside, but the inner door was already closed, and he could not enter. So he returned to the small study and sat alone with a lit candle. He thought about the failure of his marriage and felt alone and miserable, realizing that staying as a guest was not a long-term plan. He sighed several times. Just as he was about to go to bed, he suddenly heard the sound of someone knocking on the door. When he asked, no one answered. Soon, the knocking continued, repeating three times. He then opened the door and saw a beautiful young woman standing outside. When she saw the door open, she quickly pulled her skirt and entered. Sheng was greatly surprised. The woman spoke softly and discreetly to him, saying, "Don't you recognize me, sir? I am Qing娘, the sister of Xing娘. Earlier, I dropped my hairpin from the carriage, did you pick it up?" She immediately led Sheng to bed. Sheng, considering the kindness of the host, declined, saying, "I dare not."

    30

    ”拒之甚厉，至于再三。女忽赪尔怒曰：“吾父以子侄之礼待汝，置汝门下，汝乃于深夜诱我至此，将欲何为？我将诉之于父，讼汝于官，必不舍汝矣。 ”生惧，不得已而从焉。至晓，乃去。自是暮隐而入，朝隐而出，往来于门侧小斋，凡及一月有半。一夕，谓生曰：“妾处深闺，君居外馆，今日之事，幸而无人知觉。诚恐好事多魔，佳期易阻，一旦声迹彰露，亲庭罪责，闭笼而锁鹦鹉，打鸭而惊鸳鸯，在妾固所甘心，于君诚恐累德。莫若先事而发，怀璧而逃，或晦迹深村，或藏踪异郡，庶得优游偕老，不致睽离也。 ”生颇然其计，曰：“卿言亦自有理，吾方思之。 ”因自念零丁孤苦，素质亲知，虽欲逃亡，竟将焉往？尝闻父言：有旧仆金荣者，信义人也，居镇江吕城，以耕种为业。今往投之，庶不我拒。

    Explanation

    30

    The girl rejected him very severely, up to three times. Suddenly, she blushed and angrily said, "My father treats you with the courtesy of a son or nephew, and has entrusted you to me. Yet you lured me here in the middle of the night. What are you planning to do? I will report this to my father and sue you in court, and I will certainly not let you go." The man was afraid and, having no choice, agreed to her demands. By dawn, he left. From then on, he would secretly enter at dusk and leave at dawn, coming and going between her room and a small study by the gate, for more than a month and a half. One evening, she said to him, "I live in the inner chambers, and you reside outside. Today's events were fortunate in that no one noticed. But I fear that good things often have many obstacles, and happy times can be easily interrupted. If our actions become known, my father will punish us, and we will be locked up like a parrot in a cage, or startled like a pair of ducks. Although I am willing to endure this, I am afraid it might tarnish your reputation. It would be better to act before it happens, carry something valuable and flee, or hide in a remote village, or conceal ourselves in a different region, so that we may live together in peace and harmony until old age, and avoid being separated." The man agreed with her plan and said, "Your words have reason, and I am thinking about it." He then thought to himself, feeling lonely and pitiful, with only a few close friends, that although he wanted to escape, where could he go? He remembered his father telling him that there was an old servant named Jin Rong, a man of integrity and righteousness, living in Lücheng, Zhenjiang, who engaged in farming as his occupation. Now, he would go to him, hoping he would not reject him.

    31

    至明夜五鼓，与女轻装而出，买船过瓜州，奔丹阳，访于村氓，果有金荣者，家甚殷富，见为本村保正。生大喜，直造其门，至则初不相识也，生言其父姓名爵里及己乳名，方始记认，则设位而哭其主，捧生而拜于座，曰：“此吾家郎君也。”生具告以故，乃虚正堂而处之，事之如事旧主，衣食之需，供给甚至。生处荣家，将及一年。女告生曰：“始也惧父母之责，故与君为卓氏之逃，盖出于不获已也。今则旧谷既没，新谷既登，岁月如流，已及朞矣。且爱子之心，人皆有之，今而自归，喜于再见，必不我罪。况父母生我，恩莫大焉，岂有终绝之理？盍往见之乎？ ”生从其言，与之渡江入城。将及其家，谓生曰：“妾逃窜一年，今遽与君同往，或恐逢彼之怒，君宜先往觇之，妾舣舟于此以俟。

    Explanation

    31

    By the fifth drumbeat of the night, the man and the woman went out lightly dressed, bought a boat, and crossed to Guazhou, rushing to Danyang. They inquired among the villagers and indeed found one named Jin Rong, whose family was very wealthy, and who served as the village headman. The man was overjoyed and went directly to his door. Upon arrival, they did not recognize each other at first. The man told him his father's name, title, and hometown, as well as his own nickname, and only then did Jin Rong remember and recognize him. He set up a seat and mourned his master, holding the man and bowing before the seat, saying, "This is our family's young master." The man fully informed him of the reason, and Jin Rong vacated the main hall and lived there, treating him as if he were the old master. All his needs for clothing and food were provided abundantly. The man lived with Jin Rong's family for nearly a year. The woman told the man, "At first, I feared my parents' reprimand, so I fled with you like Zuo, out of necessity. Now, the old grain has been consumed, and the new grain has been harvested. Time flows like water, and it has already been a year. Moreover, the love for one's child is a universal human sentiment. If I return on my own, they will be happy to see me again and will not punish me. After all, my parents gave birth to me, and their kindness is immeasurable. How could there be a reason to sever ties forever? Why not go and see them?" The man agreed and went with her across the river into the city. As they approached his home, she said to the man, "I have been in hiding for a year. Now, if we suddenly go together, perhaps we will encounter their anger. You should go first to see, and I will moor the boat here and wait."

    32

    ”临行，复呼生回，以金凤钗授之，曰：“如或疑拒，当出此以示之，可也。”生至门，防御闻之，欣然出见，反致谢曰：“日昨顾待不周，致君不安其所，而有他适，老夫之罪也。幸勿见怪！ ”生拜伏在地，不敢仰视，但称“死罪”，口不绝声。防御曰：“有何罪过？遽出此言。愿赐开陈，释我疑虑。 ”生乃作而言曰：“曩者房帷事密，儿女情多，负不义之名，犯私通之律，不告而娶，窃负而逃，窜伏村墟，迁延岁月，音容久阻，书问莫传，情虽笃于夫妻，恩敢忘乎父母！今则谨携令爱，同此归宁，伏望察其深情，恕其重罪，使得终能偕老，永遂又于飞。大人有溺爱之恩，小子有宜家之乐，是所望也，惟翼悯焉。 ”防御闻之，惊曰：“吾女卧病在床，今及一岁，饘粥不进，转侧需人，岂有是事耶？ ”

    Explanation

    32

    On the eve of his departure, the man was called back again, and a golden phoenix hairpin was given to him, with the words: "If there is any doubt or refusal, show this to them, and it will be acceptable." Upon reaching the door, the defense heard of this and came out to greet him, returning to express gratitude, saying, "Yesterday's care was inadequate, causing you to be uncomfortable in your place, and you had another place to go. It is my fault as an old man. Please do not take it amiss!" The man knelt and bowed to the ground, dared not look up, and only said, "Death penalty," with words that did not stop. The defense said, "What crime have I committed? Hastily said this. Please allow me to explain, relieve my doubts." The man then stood up and said, "In the past, the matter in the bedroom was secret, and there was much affection between us. I bear the name of being unjust, and I violated the law of private intercourse. I married without informing anyone, stole and fled, hid in a village, delayed time, long separated by distance and silence, letters and messages did not reach. Our feelings were deep between husband and wife, but how could I forget the kindness of my parents? Now I carefully bring your beloved daughter, together to return to your parents' home. I humbly hope you will understand our deep feelings, forgive our grave sins, so that we can live together until old age, forever happy and free. You have the kindness of indulgent love, and I have the joy of a suitable home. This is what I hope for, only hope for mercy." The defense, upon hearing this, was surprised and said, "My daughter is lying ill in bed, refusing even porridge, turning and needing help. How could there be such a thing?"

    33

    生谓其恐为门户之辱，故饰词以拒之，乃曰：“目今庆娘在于舟中，可令人舁取之来。 ”防御虽不信，然且令家僮驰往视之，至则无所见。方诘怒崔生，责其妖妄，生于袖中，出金凤钗以进。防御见，始大惊曰：“此吾亡女兴娘殉葬之物也，胡为而至此哉？ ”疑惑之际，庆娘忽于床上欻然而起，直至堂前，拜其父曰：“兴娘不幸，早辞严侍，远弃荒郊，然与崔家郎君缘分未断，今之来此，意亦无他，特欲以爱妹庆娘，续其婚耳。如所请肯从，则病患当即痊除；不用妾言，命尽此矣。 ”举家惊骇，视其身则庆娘，而言词举止则兴娘也。父诘之曰：“汝既死矣，安得复于人世为此乱惑也？ ”对曰：“妾之死也，冥司以妾无罪，不复拘禁，得隶后士夫人帐下，掌传笺奏。妾以世缘未尽，故特给假一年，来与崔郎了此一段因缘尔。 ”

    Explanation

    33

    The father, fearing that accepting the proposal would bring shame to the family, used polite words to refuse it. He then said, "At present, Qingniang is in the boat. You can have someone carry her here." Despite his skepticism, the father sent a servant to check, but upon arrival, the servant saw nothing. The father then angrily scolded Cui Sheng, calling him superstitious and absurd. Cui Sheng, however, pulled out a golden phoenix hairpin from his sleeve and presented it to the father. Upon seeing the hairpin, the father was greatly surprised and exclaimed, "This is the hairpin my deceased daughter Xingniang was buried with! How did it come to be here?" While still in doubt, Qingniang suddenly rose from her bed, walked up to the front hall, and bowed to her father, saying, "Unfortunate Xingniang left her parents early and was abandoned in a remote place. However, my bond with Cui Lang is not broken. I have come here today with no other intention than to continue the marriage with my beloved sister Qingniang. If you agree, the illness will immediately be cured; if you do not listen to me, my life will end here." The whole family was shocked, as they saw the body of Qingniang but her speech and behavior were that of Xingniang. The father questioned her, "You are already dead, how can you be back in the world causing such confusion?" She replied, "I was not detained in the underworld because I was innocent. I was under the command of a noble lady, in charge of delivering messages. Since my bond in this life is not yet finished, I was given a year off to settle this bond with Cui Lang."

    34

    父闻其语切，乃许之，即敛容拜谢，又与崔生执手歔欷为别。且曰：“父母许我矣！汝好作娇客，慎毋以新人而忘故人也。 ”言讫，恸哭而仆于地，视之，死矣。急以汤药灌之，移时乃苏，疾病已去，行动如常，问其前事，并不知之，殆如梦觉。遂涓吉续崔生之婚。生感兴娘之情，以钗货于市，得钞二十锭，尽买香烛楮币，赉诣琼花观，命道士建醮三昼夜以报之。复见梦于生曰：“蒙君荐拔，尚有余情，虽隔幽明，实深感佩。小妹柔和，宜善视之。 ”生惊悼而觉。从此遂绝。呜呼异哉！

    Explanation

    34

    When the father heard her words with sincerity, he finally agreed. He then composed himself, bowed in thanks, and, taking Cui Sheng’s hand, wept bitterly as they parted. He said, “My parents have given their consent! You have always been a spoiled guest; be careful not to forget the old love for the new one.” After speaking these words, she wept uncontrollably and collapsed to the ground. When they looked at her, she was dead. They hurriedly gave her soup and medicine, but after some time she regained consciousness. Her illness had passed, and she moved as usual. When asked about previous events, she did not remember them at all, as though waking from a dream. They then chose an auspicious day to proceed with Cui Sheng’s marriage. Moved by Xing Niang’s affection, Cui Sheng sold her hairpin in the market, obtaining twenty ingots of silver. He used all of it to buy incense, candles, and paper money, and brought them to the Qionghua Temple, ordering the Taoist priests to conduct a three-day and three-night ritual to thank her. She appeared to him again in a dream and said, “I am grateful for your recommendation and elevation, and still have lingering feelings. Though separated by the realms of the living and the dead, I truly feel deeply indebted to you. My younger sister is gentle; you should treat her well.” Cui Sheng awoke in shock and sorrow. From then on, the dreams ceased. Alas, what a strange thing!

    联芳楼记
    　　吴郡富室有姓薛者，至正初，居于阊阖门外，以粜米为业。有二女，长曰兰英，次曰蕙英，皆聪明秀丽，能为诗赋。遂于宅后建一楼以处之，名曰兰蕙联芳之楼。适承天寺僧雪窗，善以水墨写兰蕙，乃以粉涂四壁，邀其绘画于上，登之者蔼然如入春风之室矣。二女日夕于其间吟咏不辍，有诗数百首，号《联芳集》，好事者往往传诵。时会稽杨铁崖制西湖《竹枝曲》，和者百余家，镂版书肆。二女见之，笑曰：“西湖有《竹枝曲》，东吴独无《竹枝曲》乎？”乃效其体，作苏台《竹枝曲》十章曰：

    35

    The Record of the Lian Fang Pavilion

    In Wu Prefecture, there was a wealthy family surnamed Xue, living in the early years of the Zhi Zheng era, outside the Changle Gate, engaged in the business of selling rice. They had two daughters, the elder named Lan Ying and the younger named Hui Ying, both intelligent and beautiful, skilled in composing poetry and prose. Therefore, they built a pavilion behind their residence to house them, naming it the Lian Fang Pavilion. Coincidentally, the monk Xuechuang from Chenting Temple, who was adept at painting orchids and lilies with ink and wash, was invited to paint the walls. The walls were coated with powder, and he painted upon them, creating an atmosphere that felt as if one had entered a room bathed in the warmth of spring. The two daughters continuously composed poetry day and night within the pavilion, producing hundreds of poems, which were titled Lian Fang Ji. Enthusiasts often circulated and recited these poems. At that time, Yang Tiayan of Kuaiji composed the Zhuzhi Qu of West Lake, and over a hundred families responded with their own compositions, which were engraved on woodblocks and published in bookshops. The two daughters, upon seeing this, smiled and said, "If West Lake has a Zhuzhi Qu, does Eastern Wu lack one?" Thus, they imitated its style and composed ten chapters of the Zhuzhi Qu of Suzhou, which read:

    36

    姑苏台上月团团，姑苏台下水潺潺。
    　　月落西边有时出，水流东去几时还？
    　　馆娃宫中麋鹿游，西施去泛五湖舟。
    　　香魂玉骨归何处？不及真娘葬虎丘。
    　　虎丘山上塔层层，夜静分明见佛灯。
    　　约伴烧香寺中去，自将钗钏施山僧。
    　　门泊东吴万里船，乌啼月落水如烟。
    　　寒山寺里钟声早，渔火江枫恼客眠。
    　　洞庭金柑三寸黄，笠泽银鱼一尺长。
    　　东南佳味人知少，玉食无由进尚方。
    　　荻芽抽笋楝花开，不见河豚石首来。
    　　早起腥风满城市，郎从海口贩鲜回。
    　　杨柳青青杨柳黄，青黄变色过年光。
    　　妾似柳丝易憔悴，郎如柳絮太颠狂。
    　　翡翠双飞不待呼，鸳鸯并宿几曾孤！
    　　生憎宝带桥头水，半入吴江半太湖。
    　　一纲凤髻绿于云，八字牙梳白似银。
    　　斜倚朱门翘首立，往来多少断肠人。
    　　百尺高楼倚碧天，阑干曲曲画屏连。
    　　侬家自有苏台曲，不去西湖唱采莲。

    Explanation

    36

    The moon above Gusu Terrace is round and full, while the water below it flows gently and softly.
    The moon sets in the west at times, but when will the water flowing east return?
    In the Palace of Gua Wa, deer roam freely, while Xi Shi has departed on her boat to the Five Lakes.
    Where does the fragrant soul and delicate bones of Xi Shi return to? It is not as good as Zhen Niang being buried at Tiger Hill.
    On the hills of Tiger Hill, there are many layers of pagodas, and at night, the Buddhist lamps can be seen clearly.
    I will visit the temple with friends to burn incense, and I will offer my jewelry to the mountain monks.
    There are ships from the eastern port, and the water is shrouded in mist as the moon sets and the crows cry.
    The early bell ringing at Hanshan Temple, the fishing lights and river maple trees disturb the traveler's sleep.
    The golden tangerines from Dongting are three inches long, while the silver fish from Lize are one foot long.
    The local delicacies are known by few, and the fine food cannot be brought to the imperial court.
    The reed shoots sprout and the lilac flowers bloom, but the pufferfish and stonefish do not come.
    The morning air is filled with the smell of fish, and the man returns from the coast with fresh seafood.
    The willow trees change color from green to yellow, and the seasons pass.
    I am like the willow silk, easily withered, while the man is like the willow fluff, too carefree and reckless.
    The jade green birds fly together without being called, while the mandarin ducks sleep together, never alone.
    I hate the water at the Baodai Bridge, which flows into both the Wujiang River and Taihu Lake.
    The woman with the phoenix hairdo green as clouds, and the eight-character tooth comb white as silver.
    She leans against the red door and looks up, and there are many heartbroken people coming and going.
    The hundred-foot tall building leans against the blue sky, and the curved railings and painted screens are connected.
    We have our own music of Gusu Terrace, and we do not go to West Lake to sing the song of picking lotus flowers.

    37

    他作亦皆称是，其才可知矣。铁崖见其稿，手写二诗于后曰：
    　　锦江只说薛涛笺，吴郡今传兰蕙篇。
    　　文采风流知有自，联珠合璧照华筵。
    　　难弟难兄并有名，英英端不让琼琼。

    Explanation

    37

    His works are all equally excellent, and his talent can be known. Iron Cliff saw his manuscript and wrote two poems afterward:

    　　The Jiang of Brocade is only known for Xue Tao's letters, but in Wu Prefecture, the Lan Hui chapter is now passed down.
    　　The elegance and brilliance of his writing are known to have their source, like pearls and jade shining at the feast.
    　　His brothers, both talented, are equally famous, and their beauty and grace are not inferior to that of the precious jade.
    　　How wonderful to take the spring breeze from the tip of his pen and set it to the music of a jade zither.
    　　Thus, his fame spread far and wide, and all believed that Ban Jieyu and Cai Wenji had returned, surpassing Li Qingzhao and Zhu Shuzhen and others. The lower part of his building overlooked the official river, and boats passed by. There was a young man named Zheng Sheng from Kunshan, also a member of a prominent family, whose father had a close relationship with Xue, and thus sent Zheng to trade in the area. Upon arrival, he moored his boat below the building and relied on Xue as his host. Xue treated him as a close family member due to his father's relationship, and they came and went together without any barriers. Zheng, being young, had a gentle and refined temperament. In the summer months, he bathed at the bow of his boat, and the two women, seeing him through the window, threw down a pair of lychees. Although Zheng understood their intention, he still looked up at the towering and lofty building, which seemed to float in the sky, and unless he had wings, he could not reach it. As the night grew deeper and the moon fell into the river, all sounds ceased, and he stood on the ship's rail, as if waiting for something. Suddenly, he heard a sound from the window, and in the blink of an eye, the two women lowered a bamboo basket on a swing rope, which fell in front of him. Zheng then climbed into it and ascended. When he met them, he was so overjoyed that he could not speak, and they took him to bed, fully expressing their affection. The eldest daughter spontaneously composed a poem to give to him:

    38

    玉砌雕栏花两枝，相逢恰是未开时。
    　　妖姿未惯风和雨，吩咐东君好护持。

    Explanation

    38

    On a stone terrace with carved railings, two flowers bloom, and we meet just as they are about to open. Their graceful appearance is not yet accustomed to the winds and rains of life, so I instruct the East Lord to take good care of them. The younger daughter also recites:

    The smoke from the incense fades, and the candlelight dims; the screen at the foot of the bed gently shakes, holding the silk curtains in place. Her grace is like a fish swimming in water, moving fluidly from east to west. At dawn, they descend together again, and so they meet every night without fail. The two daughters have many more poems, but not all can be remembered. Feeling ashamed for not being able to respond with a poem, one evening, he sees a fine piece of paper from the Yanshan River area on the table and writes a poem on it, saying:

    39

    误入蓬山顶上来，芙蓉芍药两边开。
    　　此身得似偷香蝶，游戏花丛日几回。
    　　二女得诗，喜甚，藏之箧笥。已而就枕，生复索其吟咏。长女即唱曰：
