    　　遂足成律诗一篇。又一夕，中夜之后，生忽怅然曰：“我本羁旅，托迹门下；今日之事，尊人惘知。一旦事迹彰闻，恩情间阻，则乐昌之镜，或恐从此而遂分；延平之剑，不知何时而再合也。 ”因哽咽泣下。二女曰：“妾之鄙陋，自知甚明。久处闺闱，粗通经史，非不知钻穴之可丑，韫椟之可佳也。然而秋月春花，每伤虚度，云情水性，失于自持。曩者偷窥宋玉之墙，自献汴和之璧。感君不弃，特赐俯从，虽六礼之未行，谅一言之已定。

    Explanation

    39

    Mistakenly entering the top of the Penglai Mountain, lotus and peony flowers bloom on both sides.
    This body could be like a butterfly that steals fragrance, playing among the flowers how many times a day.
    The two girls received the poem, greatly delighted, and hid it in their chests. Soon after, they went to bed, and the man again requested their verses. The eldest girl immediately sang:
    On the intertwined branches, a double-flowered bloom, a pearl of inestimable value and jade without flaws.
    The younger girl continued:
    Fortunately, we have met in harmony like Xianghua, but it is hard to visit each other in the same spontaneous spirit as Xie Xuan and his friend.
    The eldest girl then added:
    Silk stockings walking on dust, the soul feels light and carefree; a jade hairpin falls onto the pillow.
    The younger girl concluded:
    Some day, revealing the news of spring, we will not regret tonight's momentary mistake.
    Thus, they completed a regulated poem. Another night, after midnight, the man suddenly felt melancholy and said, "I am a traveler, relying on your door; today's events, your parents may not know. Once the facts become known, affection and feelings may be interrupted; the mirror of Lechang may be divided forever; the sword of Yanping, who knows when it will be reunited again." He choked and wept. The two girls said, "We are aware of our own shortcomings. Living long in the inner chambers, we have a rough understanding of the classics and histories. We are not ignorant of the ugliness of drilling through walls or the beauty of keeping treasures. However, the autumn moon and spring flowers often make us lament the wasted time, our emotions and natures unstable. In the past, we secretly peered at the wall of Song Yu, offering our own jade. Grateful for your kindness, you have graciously accepted us, though the six rites have not been performed, I believe our words are already agreed upon."

    40

    方欲同欢衽席，永奉衣巾，奈何遽出此言，自生疑阻？郑君郑君，妾虽女子，计之审矣！他日机事彰闻，亲庭谴责，若从妾所请，则终奉箕帚于君家；如不遂所图，则求我于黄泉之下，必不再登他门也。一日，登楼，于箧中得生所为诗，大骇。然事已如此，无可奈何，顾生亦少年标致，门户亦正相敌，乃以书抵生之父，喻其意。生父如其所请。仍命媒氏通二姓之好，问名纳彩，赘以为婿。是时生年二十有二，长女年二十，幼女年十八矣。吴下人多知之，或传之为掌记云。

    Explanation

    40

    She was just about to share joy on the bed, forever serving the clothing and headgear, how could she suddenly say this, causing her own doubts and obstacles? Vizier, Vizier, I, though a woman, have carefully considered it! One day, the secret matter will become known, and the father will rebuke me. If you follow my request, I will finally serve the broom and dustpan in your family; if not achieving what is planned, seek me in the netherworld, and I will never step into another door again. One day, she climbed the tower and found the man's poem in the chest, greatly startled. However, the matter has come to this, and there is nothing to be done. Considering the man is also a handsome youth, and our families are also well-matched, she then wrote a letter to the man's father, expressing her intention. The man's father agreed to her request. Still, he ordered the matchmaker to arrange the union of the two families, inquiring about the name and offering gifts, arranging for him to marry into the family. At that time, the man was twenty-two years old, the eldest daughter was twenty, and the youngest daughter was eighteen. Many people in Wu knew about it, or it was recorded as a matter of record.

    41

    剪灯新话卷二
    　　令狐生冥梦录
    　　令狐譔者，刚直之士也，生而不信神灵，傲诞自得。有言及鬼神变化幽冥果报之事，必大言折之。所居邻近，右乌老者，家赀巨宫，贪求不止，敢为不义，凶恶着闻。一夕，病卒；卒之三日而再苏。人问其故，则曰：“吾殁之后，家人广为佛事，多焚楮币，冥官喜之，因是得远。 ”譔闻之，尤其不忿，曰： “始吾谓世间贪官污吏受财曲法，富者纳贿而得圭，贫者无赀而抵罪，岂意冥府乃更甚焉！ ”因赋诗曰：
    　　一陌金钱便返魂，公私随处可通门！
    　　鬼神有德开生路，日月无光照覆盆。

    Explanation

    41

    Volume Two of New Tales of the Lamp*
    *The Record of Linghu's Ghostly Dream

    Linghu Zuan was a man of integrity and uprightness, born without belief in gods and spirits, and he was arrogant and self-satisfied. Whenever someone spoke of the transformations and retributions of ghosts and spirits in the underworld, he would always vehemently refute them. Near his residence lived an elderly man named Wu, who was extremely wealthy, greedy, and ceaselessly sought more, daring to commit unjust acts, and his wickedness was notorious. One night, he fell ill and died; three days later, he revived. When people asked him why, he said, "After my death, my family widely performed Buddhist rituals and burned many paper money offerings. The officials of the underworld were pleased with this, and therefore, I was spared." Upon hearing this, Linghu was especially resentful and said, "At first, I thought that in this world, corrupt officials and bureaucrats would bend the law for money, the rich would bribe their way to success, and the poor would be punished for lack of wealth. How could I have expected that the underworld is even worse!" He then composed a poem:

    A single sheet of paper money can bring the dead back to life,
    Public and private matters can be resolved through bribery everywhere!
    The gods and spirits have virtue and open the path to life,
    But the sun and moon do not shine on the overturned pot.

    42

    贫者何缘蒙佛力？富家容易受天恩。
    　　早知善恶都无报，多积黄金遗子孙！
    　　诗成，朗吟数过。是夜，四烛独坐，忽有二鬼使，状貌狞恶，径至其前，曰：“地府奉追。”譔大惊，方欲辞避，一人执其衣，一人挽其带，驱迫出门，足不履地，须臾已至。见大官府若世间台、省之状。二使将譔入门，遥望殿上有王者被冕据案而坐。二使挟譔伏于阶下，上殿致命曰：“奉命追令狐譔已至。”即闻王者厉声曰：“既读儒书，不知自检，敢为狂辞，诬我官府！合付犁舌狱。”遂有鬼卒数人，牵捽令去。譔大惧，攀挽槛楣不得去，俄而槛折，乃大呼曰：“令狐譔人间儒士，无罪受刑，皇天有知，乞赐昭鉴！ ”见殿上有一绿袍秉笏者，号称明法，禀于王曰：“此人好讦，遽尔加罪，必不肯伏，不若令其供责所犯，明正其罪，当无词也。 ”王曰：“善！ ”乃有一吏，操纸笔置于譔前，逼其供状。譔固称无罪，不知所供。

    Explanation

    42

    How can the poor ever receive the power of the Buddha? The wealthy easily receive the grace of heaven.
    If only I had known that good and evil are not rewarded, I would have amassed gold to leave for my descendants!
    The poem was completed, and he recited it aloud several times. That night, sitting alone with four candles burning, suddenly two spirit messengers appeared before him, their appearances fierce and sinister. They approached him and said, "The underworld has summoned you." Zuan was greatly startled and was about to try to refuse or turn away, but one seized his robe and another pulled his sash, forcing him out the door. His feet did not touch the ground, and in an instant they had arrived. He saw a grand official hall, resembling the administrative offices of the earthly world. The two messengers led Zuan inside and looked up to see a king wearing a crown seated at a table. The messengers seized Zuan and made him kneel at the base of the steps. They then ascended the hall and announced, "We have arrived as commanded to pursue Linghu Zuan." Immediately, the king spoke in a harsh voice: "Having studied the Confucian classics, yet failing to examine yourself, you dare to speak recklessly and slander my officials! You should be sent to the Tongue-Pulling Hell." Soon, several ghost officials appeared and dragged him away. Zuan was greatly terrified and tried to hold onto the railings, but could not resist. Suddenly, the railing broke, and he cried out, "Linghu Zuan is a scholar of the human world, and I am innocent yet being punished! May Heaven above know this, and grant me clear judgment!"
    At that moment, a man in a green robe holding a tablet appeared in the hall, known as the Clarifier of Law, who addressed the king, saying, "This man is known for his accusations. To hastily condemn him will surely lead to resistance. It would be better to have him confess his crimes and clearly establish his guilt, and then he will have no defense."
    The king said, "Good!" Then a clerk appeared, holding paper and brush and placing them before Zuan, compelling him to write a confession. Zuan firmly declared his innocence, yet did not know what to write.

    43

    忽闻殿上曰：“汝言无罪，所谓‘一陌金钱便返魂，公私随处可通门’，谁所作也？ ”譔始大悟，即下笔大书以供曰：伏以混沦二气，初分天地之形；高下三才，不列鬼神之数。降自中古，始肇多端。焚币帛以通神，诵经文以谄佛。于是名山大泽，咸有灵焉；古庙丛祠，亦多主者。盖以群生昏瞶，众类冥顽，或长恶以不悛，或行凶而自恣。以强凌弱，恃富欺贫。上不孝于君亲，下不睦于宗党。贪财悖义，见利忘恩。

    Explanation

    43

    Suddenly, a voice from the hall declared: "Your words are not guilty, but what does this mean: 'With a small amount of money, one can easily gain access, whether in public or private matters'? Who said this?" The author suddenly realized the truth and immediately wrote a detailed response: "I submit that in the primordial chaos of the two fundamental forces, the shape of heaven and earth was initially divided; the three fundamental elements—Heaven, Earth, and Humanity—are not counted among the numbers of ghosts and gods. Descending from the middle ages, many practices began to emerge. Paper money and silk were burned to communicate with spirits, and scriptures were recited to flatter the Buddha. Thus, famous mountains and large lakes are all inhabited by spirits; ancient temples and shrines also have many masters. This is because all beings are dim-sighted, and all kinds are stubborn and ignorant. Some continue evil without repentance, and some commit violence and act at will. They use strength to bully the weak and rely on wealth to deceive the poor. They are disobedient to superiors and parents and unfriendly to relatives and clan members. They are greedy for wealth and contrary to justice, seeing profit and forgetting gratitude."

    44

    天门高而九重莫知，地府深而十殿是列，立锉烧舂磨之状，具轮回报应之科，使为善者劝而益勤，为恶者惩而知戒，可谓法之至密，道之至公。然而威令所行，既前瞻而后仰；聪明所及，反小察而大遗。贫者入狱而受殃。宫者转经而兔罪。惟取伤弓之鸟，每漏吞舟之鱼。赏罚之条，不宜如是。至如譔者，三生贱士，一介穷儒。左枝右梧，未免儿啼女哭，东涂西抹，不救命蹇时乖。偶以不平而鸣，遽获多言之咎。悔噬脐而莫及，耻摇尾而乞怜。今蒙责其罪名，逼其状伏。

    Explanation

    44

    The heavens are high and their nine layers unknown, the underworld is deep with its ten courts arrayed, and there are the instruments of punishment such as the guillotine, fire, mortar, and mill, along with the detailed system of karma and retribution. This encourages the virtuous to become even more diligent and punishes the wicked so they know to refrain from evil, which can be said to be the law's utmost meticulousness and the way's utmost fairness. However, the strict enforcement of laws is both forward-looking and backward-looking, while human intelligence, though perceptive, often overlooks the bigger picture. The poor are imprisoned and suffer, while those who enter the palace can avoid punishment by reciting sutras. The law only captures the wary bird, often missing the larger fish. The rules of reward and punishment should not be like this. As for the author, a humble and poor scholar through three lifetimes, one who has had a difficult and sorrowful life, with futile and unsuccessful efforts, occasionally speaking out against injustice and thus incurring criticism, regretting not being able to change the past and feeling ashamed of pleading for mercy. Now, being held accountable and forced to admit guilt.

    45

    批龙鳞，探尤颔，岂敢求生；料虎头，编虎须，固知受祸。言止此矣，伏乞鉴之！王览毕，批曰：“令狐譔持论颇正，难以罪加，秉志不回，非可威屈。今观所陈，实为有理，可特放还，以彰遗直。 ”仍命复追乌老，置之于狱。复遣二使送譔还家。譔恳二使曰：“仆在人间，以儒为业，虽闻地狱之事，不以为然，今既到此，可一观否？ ”二使曰：“欲观亦不难，但禀知刑曹录事耳。 ”即引譔循西廊而行，别至一厅，文簿山积，录事中坐，二使以譔入白，录事以朱笔批一帖付之，其文若篆籒不可识。譔出府门，投北行里余，见铁城巍巍，黑雾涨天，守卫者甚众，皆牛头曳面，青体绀发，各执戈戟之属，或坐或立于门左右。二使以批帖示之，即放之入，见罪人无数，被剥皮刺血，剔心剜目。叫呼怨痛，宛转其间，楚毒之声动地。至一处，见铜柱二，缚男女二人于上，有夜叉以刃剖其胸，肠胃流出，以沸汤沃之，名为洗涤。譔问其故。

    Explanation

    45

    批龙鳞，探尤颔，岂敢求生；料虎头，编虎须，固知受祸。言止此矣，伏乞鉴之！王览毕，批曰：“令狐譔持论颇正，难以罪加，秉志不回，非可威屈。今观所陈，实为有理，可特放还，以彰遗直。 ”仍命复追乌老，置之于狱。复遣二使送譔还家。譔恳二使曰：“仆在人间，以儒为业，虽闻地狱之事，不以为然，今既到此，可一观否？ ”二使曰：“欲观亦不难，但禀知刑曹录事耳。 ”即引譔循西廊而行，别至一厅，文簿山积，录事中坐，二使以譔入白，录事以朱笔批一帖付之，其文若篆籒不可识。譔出府门，投北行里余，见铁城巍巍，黑雾涨天，守卫者甚众，皆牛头曳面，青体绀发，各执戈戟之属，或坐或立于门左右。二使以批帖示之，即放之入，见罪人无数，被剥皮刺血，剔心剜目。叫呼怨痛，宛转其间，楚毒之声动地。至一处，见铜柱二，缚男女二人于上，有夜叉以刃剖其胸，肠胃流出，以沸汤沃之，名为洗涤。譔问其故。

    To criticize the emperor, to dare to challenge powerful forces, how could one dare to seek life? To predict the intentions of a dangerous person, to handle a dangerous situation with extreme care, one firmly knows that calamity will befall. The words end here, I humbly request your judgment! The king, after reading, wrote: "Lingfu Zhan holds a rather correct view, it is difficult to add to the charges, he holds steadfastly to his purpose without turning back, cannot be coerced by force. Now observing what is presented, truly has reason, can be specially released, to highlight the remaining integrity." He still ordered to pursue Ula, placing him in prison. He then sent two envoys to send Zhan back home. Zhan pleaded with the two envoys, saying: "I have been in the world, taking Confucianism as my profession, though I have heard of the matters of hell, I did not believe it, now that I have arrived here, can I take a look?" The two envoys said: "To take a look is also not difficult, but you must inform the Recorder of the Criminal Department." They immediately led Zhan along the west corridor and to a different hall, where documents piled up like mountains, the Recorder sat in the middle, the two envoys entered to report, the Recorder wrote a note with a red pen and gave it to him, the text was like ancient script and was not recognizable. Zhan left the government gate, traveled north for several miles, saw a towering iron city, black mist filling the sky, many guards, all with ox heads dragging their faces, green bodies and indigo hair, each holding weapons such as spears and halberds, some sitting or standing on either side of the door. The two envoys showed him the note, immediately allowing him to enter, where he saw countless criminals, having their skin peeled and blood drawn, their hearts removed and eyes gouged out. They cried out in pain and resentment, twisting and turning among them, the sounds of torture shook the earth. At one place, he saw two copper pillars, two men and women bound to them, a yaochi (demon) used a blade to cut open their chests, their intestines spilled out, poured boiling water over them, named it cleansing. Zhan asked the reason.

    46

    曰：“此人在世为医。因疗此妇之夫，遂与妇通。已而其夫病卒，虽非二人杀之，原情定罪，与杀同也，故受此报。 ”又至一处，见僧尼裸体，诸鬼以牛马之皮覆之，皆成畜类。有趦趄未肯就者，即以铁鞭击之，流血狼藉。譔又问其故。曰：“此徒在世，不耕而食，不织而衣，而乃不守戒律，贪淫茹荤，故令化为异类，出力以报人耳。 ”最后至一处，榜曰：“误国之门。”见数十人坐铁床上，身俱桎梏，以青石为枷压之。

    Explanation

    46

    The person said, "This man was a doctor in the world. Because he treated the wife's husband, he then had an affair with the wife. Later, the husband died of illness, although the two did not directly cause his death, considering the circumstances and determining the crime, it is the same as murder, hence he received this punishment."

    He then went to another place and saw monks and nuns stripped naked, with various ghosts covering them with cow and horse skins, transforming them into animal forms. Those who hesitated to accept this transformation were immediately struck with iron whips, causing them to bleed profusely.

    The person asked the reason for this. They replied, "These people in the world, without farming, ate and without weaving, wore clothes, yet they did not abide by the precepts, indulging in lust and eating meat, so they were transformed into different kinds of beings, to repay people with effort."

    Finally, he arrived at a place marked with a sign that read, "The Gate of Betraying the Nation." He saw several dozen people sitting on iron beds, bound with shackles, and their necks were pressed down by large stone collars.

    47

    二使指一人示譔曰：“此即宋朝秦桧也。谋害忠良，迷误其主，故受重罪。其余亦皆历代误国之臣也。每一朝革命，即驱之出，令毒虺噬其肉，饥鹰啄其髓，骨肉糜烂至尽，复以神水洒之，业风吹之，仍复本形。此辈虽历亿万劫，不可出世矣。”譔观毕，求回。二使送之至家。譔顾谓曰：“劳君相送，无以为报。 ”二使笑曰：“报则不敢望，但请君勿更为诗以累我耳。”譔亦大笑。欠伸而觉，乃一梦也。及旦，叩乌老之家而问焉，则于是夜三更逝矣。

    Explanation

    47

    Two envoys pointed to a person and told Zuan, "This is Qin Hui of the Song Dynasty. He plotted to harm loyal ministers and misled his sovereign, therefore he suffered a severe punishment. The others are also officials from past dynasties who betrayed their country. Whenever a new dynasty is established, they are driven out and made to suffer as venomous snakes devour their flesh and hungry eagles peck at their marrow, until their flesh and bones are completely devoured. Then they are sprinkled with divine water and blown by the wind of karma, and they return to their original forms. These individuals, even after countless eons, cannot be reborn into the world." Zuan finished looking and asked to return. The two envoys escorted him home. Zuan turned and said, "Thank you for seeing me off, but I have no way to repay you." The envoys laughed and said, "We do not expect repayment, but please do not write more poems that will burden us." Zuan also laughed. He yawned and stretched, then woke up, realizing it was a dream. By dawn, he went to the home of Old Owl and asked about it, and it was said that he passed away at the third watch of that night.

    天台访隐录

    Record of Visiting Recluses at Tiantai

    A man from Taizhou named Xu Yi had only a basic knowledge of books and history. On the fifth day of the fifth lunar month, he entered Wutai Mountain to gather herbs. A few others had gone with him, but fearing the dangers ahead, they turned back halfway. Only Xu Yi was captivated by the clear mountains and beautiful waters, the dense shade of the trees, and proceeded without knowing when to stop. He recited a poem by Sun Xinggong and praised its excellence, saying: “Chicheng rises with a thunderous surge and establishes its mark; waterfalls and springs flow and define the path.” Indeed, these words were not empty.

    Going another few li ahead, the sun slanted over the hilltop, birds flew into the forest, and there was nowhere to go forward, and it was too late to return. While hesitating, he suddenly saw a large gourd floating out from the stream. Delighted, he said, “Could there be a resident here? Otherwise, it must be a Daoist temple or a Buddhist monastery.” He then followed the stream, for a little over a li, until he reached a narrow pass. There, a huge stone formed the entrance. He stepped inside for several dozen paces.

    49

    则豁然宽敞，有居民四五十家，衣冠古朴，气质淳厚，石田茅屋，竹户荆扉，犬吠鸡鸣，桑麻掩映，俨然一村落也。见逸垒，惊问曰：“客何为者？焉得而涉吾境？ ”逸告以入山采药，失路至此，遂相顾不语，漠然无延接之意。惟一老人，衣冠若儒者，扶藜而前，自称太学陶上舍，揖逸而言曰：“山泽深险，豺狼之所嗥，魑魅之所游，日又晚矣，若固相拒，是见溺而不援也。”乃邀逸归其室。坐定，逸起问曰：“仆生于斯，长于斯，游于斯久矣，未闻有此村落也。敢问。 ”上舍颦蹙而答曰：“避世之士，逃难之人，若述往事，徒增伤感耳！ ”逸固请其故。始曰：“吾自宋朝已卜居于此矣。 ”逸大惊。

    Explanation

    49

    Then suddenly, the place appeared spacious and open, with about forty or fifty households, the residents dressed in ancient and simple attire, their demeanor sincere and thick. The fields were stony, the houses thatched, the doors made of bamboo, and the gates woven with thorns. Dogs barked and roosters crowed, and mulberry trees and hemp plants interwove, creating a scene that was truly a village.

    Seeing Yi Lei, they were startled and asked, "Who are you, and how did you enter our territory?" Yi Lei explained that he had entered the mountain to gather herbs and lost his way here. They looked at each other without speaking, showing no intention of welcoming him. Only one old man, dressed like a scholar, carried a staff and approached, introducing himself as Tao Shang She from the Imperial College. He bowed to Yi Lei and said, "The mountains and marshes are deep and dangerous, where wolves howl and demons roam. The day is already late. If you firmly reject me, it would be like seeing someone drowning and not helping." He then invited Yi Lei to return to his room. After sitting down, Yi Lei stood up and asked, "I was born here, grew up here, and have been here for a long time. I have never heard of this village. I dare to ask." Tao Shang She frowned and replied, "Those who avoid the world and those who flee from trouble. If you recount past events, it will only increase sadness." Yi Lei insisted on knowing the reason. The old man began, "I have been living here since the Song Dynasty." Yi Lei was greatly surprised.

    50

    上舍乃具述曰：“仆生于理宗嘉熙丁酉之岁，既长，寓名太学，居率履斋，以讲《周易》为众所推。度宗朝，两冠堂试，一登省荐，方欲立身扬名，以显于世，不幸度皇晏驾，太后临朗，北兵渡江，时事大变。嗣君改元德佑之岁，则挈家逃难于此。其余诸人，亦皆同时避难者也。年深岁久，因遂安焉。种田得粟，采山得薪，凿井而饮，架屋而息。寒往暑来，日居月诸，但见花开为春，叶脱为秋，不知今日是何朝代，是何甲子也。

    50

    The guest then elaborately stated: "I was born in the year Ding You of the Jiaxi era during the reign of Emperor Lizong. After growing up, I enrolled in the Imperial Academy, residing in the Ratefuli Hall and being renowned for my lectures on the I Ching (Book of Changes). During the reign of Emperor Duozong, I twice passed the hall examination and was once recommended to the provincial examination. I intended to establish myself and gain fame in the world, but unfortunately, Emperor Duozong passed away, and the Empress Dowager assumed regency. The northern army crossed the Yangtze River, and the situation underwent great changes. The successor emperor changed the era name to Deyou, and I fled with my family to this place. The other people here also fled at the same time. After many years, we settled down here. We grew grain and gathered firewood, dug wells for water, and built houses for shelter. Seasons changed, and days passed. We only saw flowers bloom in spring and leaves fall in autumn, and we did not know what dynasty or year it was."

    The guest said, "The present emperor is wise, martial, and divinely inspired, continuing the legacy and initiating a new era, unifying the Chinese lands, and establishing the state of Great Ming. The current year is the seventh year of the Hongwu era, during the year of the sexagenary cycle known as 'Yuan Feng She Ti Ge.'" The host replied, "Ah, I only know about the Song dynasty, not the Yuan, and how would I know that today is the era of Great Ming! I wish the guest could briefly recount the rise and fall of the three dynasties so that I may hear it." The guest then said, "In the year of Ding Si during the Song dynasty, the Yuan forces invaded Lin'an, and the imperial family and court were relocated to the north. That year, Guang Wang established a new court on the sea, changing the era name to Jing Yan. Soon after, he died, and was posthumously titled as the Duan Emperor. Yi Wang succeeded him, but was forced by the Yuan forces to commit suicide, leading to the demise of the Song dynasty, which occurred in the year of Wu Yin during the Yuan dynasty. The Yuan then unified the north and south, and by the year of Ding Wei during the Yuan dynasty, it had passed through half of a sexagenary cycle and eventually perished. Now, the Great Ming dynasty has been established, and it is the seventh year of the Hongwu era. It has been nearly a century since the year of Ding Si in the Song dynasty." The host, upon hearing this, could not help but shed tears. As the night grew quiet and the mountains became empty, the sounds around them grew still. The guest stayed in the host's room, where the bed was made of earth and the pillow of stone, yet it was very neat. However, the guest felt mentally clear and physically cool, unable to fall asleep. The next day, the host killed a chicken and prepared millet, serving the guest wine in a simple earthenware vessel. The host composed a poem called "Gold Thread Lyrics," singing to accompany the drinking.

    而师相方且铺张太平，迷惑主听，一旦虏马饮江，家国倾覆，师相亦安得久有此富贵耶？ ’遂扼吭而死。谢堂乃太后之侄，殷富无比，尝夜宴客，设水晶帘，烧沉香火，以径尺玛璃盘，盛大珠四颗，光照一室，不用灯烛；优人献诵乐语，有黄金七宝酒瓮，重十数斤，即于座上赐之不吝。谢后临朝，梦天倾东南。一人擎之，力若不胜，蹶而复起者三。己而一日坠地，傍有一人捧之而奔，觉而遍访于朝，得二人焉，厥状极肖，擎天者文天祥，捧日者陆秀夫也，遂不次用之。江万里去国，都民送之郭外者以千计，攀辕忍舍去，城门既阖，多宿于野。贾似道出督，御白银铠，真珠马鞍；千里马二，一驮督府之印，一载制书并随军赏格，以黄帕覆之，都民罢市而观。出师之盛，末之有也。 ”又论当时诸臣曰：“陈宜中谋而不断，家铉翁节而不通，张世杰勇而不果，李庭芝智而不达，其最优者，文天祥乎！ ”如是者凡数百言，皆历历可听。

    53

    While the chancellor was boasting about peace and prosperity, misleading the emperor's ears, once the enemy's horses drink from the river, the family and country are overthrown. How could the chancellor long enjoy such wealth and status? Thus, he choked himself to death. Xie Tang, the uncle of the empress dowager, was incredibly wealthy. He once held a night banquet for guests, setting up crystal curtains and burning sandalwood incense. Using a jade plate a foot in diameter, he placed four large pearls, their light illuminating the room, making no need for lamps or candles. Entertainers recited auspicious words, presenting a golden seven-treasure wine jar weighing several dozen pounds, which he immediately bestowed upon them without hesitation. After the empress dowager took the throne, she dreamed that the sky was tilting to the southeast. One person was holding it up, his strength barely sufficient, falling and rising three times. Later, one day it fell to the ground, and beside it, a person held it up and ran. Upon waking, she searched throughout the court and found two people who looked exactly like them: the one holding up the sky was Wen Tianxiang, and the one holding up the sun was Lu Shoufu. She then promoted them without regard to seniority. When Jiang Wanli left the country, thousands of citizens followed him out of the city, clinging to the carriage and reluctant to let go. After the city gates were closed, many stayed overnight in the fields. When Jia Sidao was dispatched, he wore silver armor and a pearl-studded saddle. He had two thousand-mile horses, one carrying the seal of the governor's office, and the other carrying the imperial edict and military reward chart, covered with yellow silk. The citizens stopped their businesses to watch. The grandeur of his departure was unprecedented. He further commented on the officials of that time: "Chen Yizhong was thoughtful but indecisive, Jia Xuanweng was principled but ineffective, Zhang Shijie was brave but hesitant, and Li Tingzhi was intelligent but unwise. The best among them was Wen Tianxiang." Such were his words, numbering in the hundreds, all clear and audible.

    That night, Yi stayed again. The next morning, he announced his departure, and the host composed a poem in the style of "Gufeng" (ancient ballad) to see him off, saying:

    The move southward during Jianyan was marked by many upheavals, with the emperor escaping on a mud horse to govern the yellow palace. All the old possessions were handed over to others, and Jiangnan became a separate realm. Pitifully, two young maids served wine, and a myriad of sorrows and regrets, who can know them? The cold moonlight shone over the city of Wuguo, and the north wind blew over the Yellow Dragon Pass. The plan was hatched in the east chamber to achieve peace, and E Wang was executed while Qi Wang grew old. Dong Si Xiang was not seen in the wine, and one must look for Song Wu Sao by the lake. For generations, the throne was passed internally, and war was no longer spoken of, and for over eighty years, it was called a time of peace. The emperor's death left the bow and sword far away, and Jia Xiang led the army, with the sound of drums startling the enemy. Taking the family to hide in the empty valley, looking west toward the main gate and crying with bowed head, destroying the chariot and killing the horse to sever all traces, digging wells and farming to barely make ends meet. Marrying within the southern and northern neighbors, the old customs resembling those of Zhu Chen Village, not serving in the city as a laborer or paying taxes, only growing children and grandchildren under the roof. I am glad you came to visit despite the dangers, often asking about the old and supporting the nine-jointed staff. The times have changed, and events have shifted too quickly, the things remain the same, but the people have changed, causing even more sorrow. I am grateful that you stayed with me for a while, using wild vegetables and mountain delicacies as offerings.

    　　君到人间烦致语，今遇升平乐安处。
    　　相逢不用苦相疑，我辈非仙亦非鬼。
    　　遂送逸出路口，挥袂而别。逸沿途每五十步插一竹枝以记之。到家数日，乃具酒醴，携肴馔，率家僮辈赍往访之，则重冈迭蟑，不复可寻，丰草乔林，绝无踪迹。往来于樵蹊牧径之间，但闻谷鸟悲鸣，岭猿哀啸而己，竟惆怅而归。逸念上舍自言生于嘉熙丁酉，至今则百有四十岁矣，而颜貌不衰，言动详雅，止若五六十者，岂有道之流欤？
    　　滕穆醉游聚景园记
    　　延佑初，永嘉滕生名穆，年二十六，美风调，善吟咏，为众所推许。素闻临安山水之胜，思一游焉。甲寅岁，科举之诏兴，遂以乡书赴荐。至则侨居涌金门外，无日不往于南北二山及湖上诸剎，灵隐、天竺、净慈、宝石之类，以至玉泉、虎跑、天龙、灵鹫。石屋之洞，冷泉之亭，幽涧深林，悬崖绝壁，足迹殆将遍焉。七月之望，于曲院赏莲，因而宿湖，泊雷峰塔下。

    Explanation

    55

    The Chickens at Home Are Fat, Why Buy More? The Wine by the Bed Is Ready, No Need for More.
    When you come to the human world, please convey my message: Now that peace and prosperity have been achieved, there is a place of joy and peace.
    We do not need to doubt each other when we meet; we are neither gods nor ghosts.
    So I sent Yi out at the crossroads, waving goodbye and parting. Yi placed a bamboo stick every fifty steps along the way to mark it. After returning home after several days, he prepared wine and spirits, carried food and dishes, and led the household servants to visit the place. However, the mountains were too steep and the terrain too complex to find again, with lush grass and tall trees, no trace at all. Walking along the paths of woodcutters and shepherds, he only heard the birds in the valley crying mournfully and the apes on the mountain wailing sadly, and finally returned with a sense of melancholy. Yi remembered that the person at the inn said they were born in the year Ding You of Jiaxi, and now they are one hundred and forty years old, but their appearance has not aged, their speech and actions are refined and elegant, as if only fifty or sixty years old, could they be a person of Dao?
    Record of Teng Mu's Drunken Wandering in the Juyi Garden
    In the early years of the Yanyou era, Teng Mu from Yongjia was twenty-six years old, with a beautiful demeanor and temperament, skilled in poetry, and highly praised by many. He had always heard of the beauty of the mountains and rivers of Lin'an and thought to visit once. In the year of Jia Yin, the imperial examination was held, and he then went to take the exam. Upon arrival, he temporarily resided outside the Yongjin Gate, going every day to the two mountains north and south and various temples by the lake, such as Lingyin, Tiantu, Jingci, Gemstone, Yuping, Hupao, Tianlong, and Lingjiu. The cave of Shiwu, the pavilion of Lengquan, deep valleys and dense forests, steep cliffs and sheer rocks, his footsteps almost covered everything. On the full moon of July, he admired lotus flowers at Quyuan and so stayed by the lake, anchoring under Leifeng Pagoda.

    56

    是夜，月色如昼，荷香满身，时闻大鱼跳掷于波间，宿鸟飞鸣于岸际。生已大醉，寝不能寐，披襟而起，绕堤观望。行至聚景园，信步而入。时宋亡已四十年，园中台馆，如会芳殿、清辉阁、翠光亭皆已颓毁。惟瑶津西轩岿然然独存。生至轩下，倚栏少憩。俄见一美人先行，一侍女随之，自外而入。风鬟雾鬓，绰约多姿，望之殊若神仙。生于轩下屏息以观其所为。美人言曰：“湖山如故，风景不殊，但时移世换，令人有《黍离》之悲尔！ ”行至园北太湖石畔，遂咏诗曰：
    　　湖上园林好，重来忆旧游。
    　　征歌调《玉树》，阅舞按《梁州》。
    　　径狭花迎辇，池深柳拂舟。
    　　昔人皆已殁，谁与话风流！
    　　生放逸者，初见其貌，已不能定情。及闻此作，技痒不可复禁，即于轩下续吟曰：

    Explanation

    56

    That night, the moonlight was like daylight, and the fragrance of lotus flowers filled the air. Occasionally, one heard the sound of large fish leaping in the waves, and birds that had settled flew and called by the shore. The protagonist, already deeply drunk, lay in bed but could not sleep. He unfastened his robe and rose, walking around the embankment and looking around. He walked to the Juying Garden and entered at his leisure. At that time, forty years had passed since the fall of the Song Dynasty, and the pavilions and halls in the garden, such as the Hui Fang Hall, Qing Hui Pavilion, and Cui Guang Pavilion, had all fallen into disrepair. Only the Western Pavilion of the Jade Spring remained standing. The protagonist reached the pavilion, leaned against the railing, and rested for a moment. Suddenly, he saw a beautiful woman leading the way, followed by a maid, entering from outside. Her hair was like wind and her hairpins like mist, and she was graceful and full of charm, looking like a fairy. The protagonist held his breath and watched her actions. The woman said, "The lakes and mountains remain unchanged, and the scenery is no different, but time has changed and the world has transformed, making one feel the sorrow of the Shu Li!" She walked to the north of the garden, by the Taihu stone, and then recited a poem:
    The gardens by the lake are beautiful, and returning reminds one of past travels.
    Singing songs in the style of Yushu, dancing in the style of Liangzhou.
    The narrow path is lined with flowers greeting the carriage, the deep pool has willows brushing the boat.
    The former people have all died, who can talk about elegance?
    The protagonist, a free-spirited man, was immediately captivated by her appearance at first sight. Upon hearing her poem, he felt an irresistible urge to write and, without restraint, continued to recite his own poem at the pavilion:

    57

    湖上园亭好，相逢绝代人。
    　　嫦娥辞月殿，织女下天津。
    　　未会心中意，浑疑梦里身。
    　　愿吹邹子律，幽谷发阳春。
    　　吟已。趋出赴之。美人亦不惊讶，但徐言曰：“固知郎君在此，特来寻访耳。 ”生问其姓名，美人曰：“妾弃人间已久，欲自陈叙，诚恐惊动郎君。 ”生闻此言，审其为鬼，亦无所惧。固问之，乃曰：“芳华姓卫，故宋理宗朝宫人也。年二十三而殁，殡于此园之侧。今晚因往演福访贾贵妃，蒙延久坐，不觉归迟，致令郎君于此久待。 ”即命侍女曰：“翘翘，可于舍中取裀席酒果来，今夜月色如此，郎君又至，不可虚度，可便于此赏月也。 ”翘翘应命而去。须臾，携紫氍毹，设白玉碾花樽，碧琉璃盏，醪醴馨香，非世所有，与生笑谑笑咏，词旨清婉。复命翘翘歌以侑酒。翘翘请歌柳耆卿《望海潮》词，美人曰：“对新人不宜歌旧曲。 ”即于席上自制《木兰花慢》一阕，令翘翘歌之曰：

    Explanation

    57

    The garden by the lake is beautiful, and I have met a person of unparalleled beauty.
    Chang'e has left her palace on the moon, and Zhinv has descended from the Milky Way.
    I do not understand her inner feelings, and I feel as if I am in a dream.
    I wish to play the music of Zou Yan, bringing spring to a remote valley.
    After reciting, I hurriedly went out to meet her. The beautiful lady was not surprised but calmly said, "I knew you were here, and I came specifically to visit you." The man asked her name, and she replied, "I have been away from the human world for a long time. If I were to tell my story, I fear it might startle you." Upon hearing this, the man realized she was a ghost but felt no fear. He insisted on knowing more, and she said, "My name is Wei Fanghua. I was a palace lady during the reign of Emperor Lizong of the Song Dynasty. I died at the age of twenty-three and was buried beside this garden. Tonight, I went to visit Princess Jia at the Yanyu Palace. I was invited to stay for a long time and didn't realize I was late, causing you to wait for so long." She then ordered her maid, "Qiao Qiao, go to the house and bring out the mats, wine, and fruits. The moon is so beautiful tonight, and you are here, so we cannot waste this time. Let us enjoy the moon here." Qiao Qiao obeyed and went to fetch them. Soon, she brought a purple rug, set up a white jade flower carver, and placed green glass cups. The wine was fragrant and unique, not found in the world. They laughed and recited poetry together, with her words being clear and elegant. She then ordered Qiao Qiao to sing to accompany the wine. Qiao Qiao requested to sing a song by Liu Qi卿's "Looking at the Sea Tide," but the lady said, "It is not appropriate to sing old songs for a new person." She then composed a new piece of "Mu Lan Hua Man" on the spot and ordered Qiao Qiao to sing it.

    58

    记前朝旧事，曾此地，会神仙。向月砌云阶，重携翠袖，来拾花钿。繁华总随流水，叹一场春梦杳难圆。废港芙渠滴露，断堤杨柳垂烟。两峰南北只依然，辇路草芊芊。恨别馆离宫，烟销凤盖，波浸龙船。平时银屏金屋，对漆灯无焰夜如年。落日牛羊垄上，西风燕雀林边。
    　　歌竟，美人潜然垂泪，生以言尉解，仍微词挑之，以观其意。即起谢曰：“殂谢之人，久为尘土，若得奉侍巾栉，虽死不朽。且郎君适间诗句，固已许之矣。愿吹邹子之律，而一发幽谷之春也。 ”生曰：“向者之诗，率口而成，实本无意，岂料便为语谶。 ”良久，月隐西垣，河倾东岭，即命翘翘撤席。美人曰：“敝居僻陋，非郎君之所处，只此西轩可也。 ”遂携手而入，假寝轩下。交会之事，一如人间。将旦，挥涕而别。

    Explanation

    58

    Recording the old affairs of the previous dynasty, once here, I met the immortals. Facing the moon, stepping on the cloud-strewn stairs, I again carried the green sleeves, coming to pick up the flower ornaments. Prosperity always follows the flowing water; I lament a spring dream that is hard to fulfill. In the abandoned harbor, the lotus drops dew; on the broken dike, willows hang in smoke. The two peaks in the north and south remain unchanged; the imperial road is covered with lush grass. Hating the guesthouses and imperial palaces, the smoke dissipates from the phoenix canopy, the waves submerge the dragon boat. In the past, the silver screens and golden houses, facing the lamp with no flame, the night feels like a year. The setting sun on the hillside, with cattle and sheep; the west wind at the edge of the forest, with swallows and sparrows.

    When the song ended, the beautiful woman silently shed tears. I comforted her with words, still gently teasing her to see her intentions. She immediately rose and thanked me, saying, "A person who has passed away, long turned to dust, if I could serve you by tending to your daily needs, I would be immortal even in death. And your verses just now, they have already promised me. I wish you could blow the law of Zou Zi, and release the spring from the depths of the valley." I replied, "The poetry I composed earlier was spoken offhand, truly without any intention, how could I have expected it to become an omen." After a long while, the moon hid behind the western wall, the river tilted eastward toward the mountain, and I immediately ordered the removal of the table. The woman said, "My humble abode is remote and shabby, not a place for you to stay; only this western pavilion would be suitable." So we took each other's hands and entered, taking a temporary rest beneath the pavilion. The meeting that took place was just like in the human world. As dawn approached, we parted ways with tears.

    59

    至昼，往访于园侧，果有宋宫人卫芳华之墓。墓左一小丘，即翘翘瘗也。生感叹逾时。迨暮，又赴西轩，则美人已先至矣。迎谓生曰：“日间感君相访，然而妾止卜其夜，未卜其昼，故不敢奉见。数日之后，当得无间矣。 ”自是，无夕而不会。经旬之后，白昼亦见。生遂携归所寓安焉。已而生下第东归，美人愿随之去。生问：“翘翘何以不从？”曰：“妾既奉侍君子，旧宅无人，留其看守耳。 ”生与之同回乡里，见亲识，绐之曰：“娶于杭郡之良家。 ”众见其举止温柔，言词慧利，信且悦之。美人处生之室，奉长上以礼，待婢仆以恩，左右邻里，俱得其欢心。且又勤于治家，洁于守己，虽中门之外，未尝轻出。众咸贺生得内助。

    Explanation

    59

    During the day, he visited the side of the garden and indeed found the tomb of Wei Fanghua, a palace woman from the Song dynasty. To the left of the tomb was a small mound, which was the "翘翘瘗." The protagonist was moved and reflected for a long time. By evening, he again went to the western pavilion, and the beauty had already arrived. She greeted him and said, "I was moved by your visit, but I could only foresee the night, not the day, so I dared not meet you. After several days, we will meet continuously." From then on, they met every night. After a few weeks, they also met during the day. The protagonist then brought her back to his residence and settled her there. Soon after, the protagonist failed the examination and returned home, and the beauty wished to accompany him. The protagonist asked, "Why is '翘翘' not accompanying us?" She replied, "I am serving the gentleman, and the old house is empty, so I left '翘翘' to watch over it." The protagonist and the beauty returned to his hometown together, and when he met his relatives, he told them, "I married into a good family in Hangzhou." They believed and were pleased with her. Neighbors and those around her were all pleased with her. She was diligent in managing the household and pure in self-discipline. Though she never went out lightly beyond the main gate, everyone congratulated the protagonist on gaining an excellent wife.

    60

    荏苒三岁，当丁巳年之初秋，生又治装赴浙省乡试。行有日矣，美人请于生曰：“临安，妾乡也。从君至此，已阅三秋，今愿得偕行，以顾视翘翘。”生许诺，遂赁舟同载，直抵钱塘，僦屋居焉。至之明日，适值七月之望，美人谓生曰：“三年前曾于此夕与君相会，今适当其期，欲与君同赴聚景，再续旧游可乎？”生如其言，载酒而往。

    Explanation

    60

    Three years had passed, and it was the early autumn of the Ding Si year. The scholar once again prepared his belongings and set out for the provincial examination in Zhejiang. After several days of travel, the beauty requested of the scholar, saying, "Lin'an is my hometown. I have been with you here for three autumns. Now, I wish to travel with you, to look back fondly." The scholar agreed, and they rented a boat and traveled together, directly to Qiantang, where they rented a house to live in. The next day, it happened to be the full moon night of the seventh month. The beauty said to the scholar, "Three years ago, we met on this very night. Now, it is the same time, and I wish to go with you to Juyi Garden, to continue our old tour, is it possible?" The scholar agreed as said, and they carried wine and went.

    61

    至晚，月上东垣，莲开南浦，露柳烟篁，动摇堤岸，宛然若昔时之景。行至园前，则翘翘迎拜于路首曰：“娘子陪侍郎君，遨游城郭，首尾三年，已极人间之欢，独不记念旧居乎？ ”三人入园，同至西轩而坐。美人忽涕泪而告生曰：“感君不弃，侍奉房帷，未遂深欢，又当永别。 ”生曰：“何故？ ”对曰：“妾本幽阴之质，久戚阳明之世，甚非所宜。特以与君有夙世之缘，故冒犯条律以相从耳。今而缘尽，自当奉辞。 ”生惊问曰：“然则何时？ ”对曰：“止在今夕耳。”生凄惶不忍。美人曰：“妾非不欲终事君子，永奉欢娱。然而程命有限，不可违越。若更迟留，须当获戾。非止有损于妾，亦将不利于君。岂不见越娘之事乎？ ”生意稍悟，然亦悲伤感怆，彻晓不寐。及山寺钟鸣，水村鸡唱，急起与生为别，解所御玉指环系于生之衣带，曰：“异日见此，无忘旧情。”遂分袂而去，然犹频频而顾，良久始灭。生大恸而返。

    Explanation

    61

    By evening, the moon rose above the eastern wall, the lotus bloomed in the southern shore, dewy willows and misty bamboo groves swayed gently against the embankments, the scene as if it were the same as of old. When he reached the garden gate, a figure stood eagerly at the path’s head and bowed respectfully, saying, “Lady, you have accompanied Lord Sir on wanderings through the city for three full years, having already reached the height of earthly joy. Do you not remember your old home?” The three entered the garden and sat together in the western pavilion. Suddenly, the beauty wept and told the man, “I am grateful that you did not cast me aside, and that I have served in your household. Yet our deep joy has not yet been fulfilled, and now we must part forever.” The man asked, “Why?” She replied, “I am by nature a being of the spirit world, long dwelling in the realm of light and brightness. It is most unsuitable for me to remain here. I dared to defy the laws of the cosmos merely to be with you. But now our karmic bond has come to an end, and I must take my leave.” The man was shocked and asked, “Then when will this be?” She answered, “Only tonight.” The man was filled with sorrow and could not bear the parting. The beauty said, “It is not that I do not wish to remain with you until the end, to serve you in joy forever. But fate is limited, and we cannot defy it. If I linger any longer, I shall suffer punishment. It will not only harm me, but also bring you harm. Have you not heard of the tale of Yue Nü?” The man’s mind slightly understood, yet he was still filled with sorrow and grief, and could not sleep all night. When the temple bell rang in the mountain and the rooster crowed in the village by the water, she quickly rose to take her leave of him, removing the jade ring from her finger and fastening it to his belt. She said, “When you see this in the future, do not forget our old affection.” Then she parted from him, yet still turned back repeatedly, and only after a long while did she finally disappear. The man wept bitterly and returned home.

    62

    翌日具肴醴，焚镪楮于墓下，作文以吊祭之曰：
    　　惟灵生而淑美，出类超群。禀奇姿于仙圣，锺秀气于乾坤。粲然如花之丽，粹然如玉之温。达则天上之金屋，穷则路左之荒坟。托松楸而共处，对狐兔之群奔。落花流水，断雨残云，中原多事，故国无君。抚光阴之过隙，视日月之奔轮。然而精灵不泯，性识长存。不必仗少翁之奇术，自能返倩女之芳魂。玉匣骖鸾之扇，金泥簇蝶之裙。声泠泠兮环佩，香蔼蔼兮兰荪。方欲同欢而偕老，奈何既合而复分！步洛妃凌波之袜，赴王母瑶池之樽。即之而无所睹，扣之而不复闻。怅后会之莫续，伤前事之谁论。锁杨柳春风之院，闭梨花夜雨之门。恩情断兮天漠漠，哀怨结兮云昏昏。音容杳而靡接，心绪乱而纷纭。谨含哀而奉吊，庶有感于斯文。呜呼哀哉，尚飨！

    Explanation

    62

    The next day, food and wine were prepared, and paper money and paper offerings were burned at the grave. An essay was written to mourn and offer sacrifices, saying:

    May the spirit have been born beautiful and virtuous, standing out and excelling among others. It received extraordinary beauty from the immortals and sages, and gathered the finest qualities from heaven and earth. Brightly like the beauty of flowers, purely like the warmth of jade. If successful, to live in a golden house in heaven; if poor, to be buried in a lonely grave by the roadside. To rest under the pines and cypresses together, to face the running of foxes and rabbits. Fallen flowers and flowing water, broken rain and scattered clouds, there are many troubles in the Central Plains, the old country has no ruler. To feel the fleeting nature of time, to see the sun and moon racing. However, the spirit does not perish, the nature and knowledge remain forever. It is not necessary to rely on the strange techniques of the wizard, the spirit can return on its own. A jade box with a fan carried by a phoenix, a golden skirt with clusters of butterflies. The sound of the jade pendants is clear and cold, the fragrance of the orchids and sweet grass is pervasive. Just as we were about to enjoy happiness together until old age, how can we have been united and then separated! To walk in the shoes of the Luo River fairy, crossing the waves, to go to the wine cup of the Queen Mother of the West in the Jade Pool. To see nothing when approaching, to hear nothing when knocking. To lament that future meetings cannot be continued, to grieve that past events cannot be discussed. To lock the courtyard of willows in the spring breeze, to close the door of pear blossoms in the night rain. The affection has been severed, and the sky is vast and empty, grief and resentment have formed, and the clouds are dark and heavy. The voice and appearance are distant and unreachable, the heart and mind are confused and chaotic. To respectfully offer condolences with sorrow, perhaps this writing will touch someone. Alas, alas, may the spirit enjoy the offering.

    63

    从此遂绝矣。生独居旅邸，如丧配耦。试期既迫，亦无心入院，惆怅而归。
    　　亲党问其故，始具述之，众咸叹异。生后终身不娶，入雁荡山采药，遂不复还。
    　　牡丹灯记
    　　方氏之据浙东也，每岁元夕，于明州张灯五夜，倾城士女，皆得纵观。至正庚子之岁，有乔生者，居镇明岭下，初丧其耦，鳏居无聊，不复出游，但倚门伫立而已。十五夜，三更尽，游人渐稀，见一丫鬟，挑双头牡丹灯前导，一美人随后，约年十七八，红裙翠袖，婷婷袅袅，迤逦投西而去。生于月下视之，韶颜稚齿，真国色也。神魂飘荡，不能自抑，乃尾之而去，或先之，或后之。

    Explanation

    63

    From this point onward, they were completely severed. The man lived alone in a temporary lodging, feeling as if he had lost his spouse. The exam period was already approaching, and he had no heart to enter the academy; he returned home in a state of melancholy. When relatives and friends asked him about the reason, he began to fully recount it, and everyone expressed admiration or surprise. Afterward, he remained unmarried for life, entered Yandang Mountain to gather herbs, and never returned.

    The Peony Lantern Record

    During the time when the Fang family occupied Zhe Dong, every year during the Lantern Festival, in Mingzhou, lanterns were displayed for five nights, and all the city's men and women were allowed to view them. In the year 1350, there was a man named Qiao who lived at the foot of Zhenming Ridge. He had recently lost his wife and lived in a state of loneliness and boredom, no longer going out. He merely leaned against the door and stood there. On the 15th night, at the end of the third watch, the number of tourists gradually decreased. He saw a maidservant carrying a double-headed peony lantern in front, followed by a beautiful woman, about seventeen or eighteen years old, with a red skirt and green sleeves, graceful and slender, slowly and gracefully headed westward. He looked at her under the moonlight, and she had a beautiful face and youthful teeth, truly a national beauty. His soul and spirit were wandering, and he could not restrain himself. Then he followed her, sometimes leading her, sometimes following her.

    64

    行数十步，女忽回顾而微哂曰：“初无桑中之期，乃有月下之遇，似非偶然也。”生即趋前揖之曰：“敝居咫尺，佳人可能回顾否？”女无难意，即呼丫鬟曰：“金蓬，可挑灯同往也。 ”于是金莲复回。生与女携手至家，极其欢昵，自以为巫山洛浦之遇，不是过也。生问其姓名居址，女曰：“姓符，丽卿其字，漱芳其名，故奉化州判女也。先人既殁，家事零替，既无弟兄，仍鲜族党，止妾一身，遂与金莲侨居湖西耳。 ”生留之宿，态度妖妍，词气婉媚，低帏昵枕，甚极欢爱。天明，辞别而去，暮则又至。

    Explanation

    64

    After walking dozens of steps, the woman suddenly turned back and smiled slightly, saying, "We had no prearranged meeting, yet we met by the moonlight, which seems not by chance." The man immediately approached her and bowed, saying, "My home is very close, would a beautiful lady like you consider coming back?" The woman showed no reluctance and called out to her maid, "Jinpeng, let's carry a lamp and go together." Thus, Jinlian returned. The man and the woman walked hand in hand to his home, where they were extremely intimate and affectionate, feeling as if they were experiencing the legendary encounter between Emperor Xuanzong and Yang Guifei, not exaggerating it at all. The man asked her name and address, and she replied, "My surname is Fu, my courtesy name is Liqing, and my given name is Shufang. I am the daughter of a former state judge. My father has passed away, and the family affairs are in decline. I have no brothers, and there are few relatives. I am alone, so I live temporarily in the western part of the lake with Jinlian." The man kept her for the night. She was charming and graceful in demeanor, her words and tone were gentle and alluring. Under the low curtain, they were very intimate and loving. At dawn, she bid farewell and left, but she would come again at night.

    65

    如是者将半月，邻翁疑焉，穴壁窥之，则见一粉骷髅与生并坐于灯下，大骇。明旦，诘之，秘不肯言。邻翁曰：“嘻！子祸矣！人乃至盛之纯阳，鬼乃幽阴之邪秽。今子与幽阴之魅同处而不知，邪秽之物共宿而不悟，一旦真元耗尽，灾眚来临，惜乎以青春之年，而遂为黄壤之容也，可不悲夫！ ”生始惊惧，备述厥由。邻翁曰：“彼言侨居湖西，当往物色之，则可知矣。”生如其教，径投月湖之西，往来于长堤之上、高桥之下，访于居人，询于过客，并言无有。

    Explanation

    65

    For about half a month, things continued in this manner, and the old neighbor became suspicious. He poked a hole in the wall to look, and saw a white skeleton sitting with the living under the lamp, which greatly frightened him. The next morning, he questioned the young man, but the latter kept the matter secret and would not speak. The old neighbor said, “Ah! You are in great trouble! Humans are the purest yang, the most vigorous of all, while ghosts are foul and dark, the impure yin. Now you dwell with these spirits of the dark and obscure without knowing it, and share a dwelling with these impure things without realizing it. Once your true essence is exhausted, calamity will come upon you. It is a pity that in the prime of youth, you will become nothing but dust — is this not a most sorrowful fate?” The young man was then struck with fear and fully recounted the cause. The old neighbor said, “He said he resides in the western part of the lake. You should go there and search for him, and you will learn the truth.” The young man followed his advice and went directly to the western side of Moon Lake, moving back and forth along the long dike and under the high bridge, asking the local residents and inquiring of passersby — but all said they knew of no one.

    66

    日将夕矣，乃入湖心寺少憩，行遍东廊，复转西廊，廊尽处得一暗室，则有旅榇，白纸题其上曰：“故奉化符州判女丽卿之柩。”柩前悬一双头牡丹灯，灯下立一明器婢子，背上有二字曰金莲。生见之，毛发尽竖，寒栗遍体，奔走出寺，不敢回顾。是夜借宿邻翁之家，忧怖之色可掬。邻翁曰：“玄妙观魏法师，故开府王真人弟子，符箓为当今第一，汝宜急往求焉。 ”明旦，生诣观内。法师望见其至，惊曰：“妖气甚浓，何为来此？”生拜于座下，具述其事。

    Explanation

    66

    The day was nearly over, and so he entered the Huaxin Temple to rest briefly. He walked through the eastern corridor and then turned around to walk through the western corridor. At the end of the corridor, he found a dark room where there was a coffin of a traveler. A white paper was inscribed on it, reading: "The coffin of Lady Liqing, daughter of the former Fu Zhou Judge." In front of the coffin hung a double-headed peony lamp, and under the lamp stood a figurine of a servant. On the back of the figurine were two characters that read "jinlian." Upon seeing this, the man's hair stood on end, and he shivered all over. He ran out of the temple without daring to look back. That night, he stayed at the neighbor's house, and his face showed visible fear and worry. The neighbor said, "The Taoist priest Wei from Xuanmiao Temple is a disciple of the former official and Taoist master Wang. His talismans are the best in the current era. You should go quickly and seek his help." The next morning, the man visited the temple. The Taoist priest saw him arrive and was surprised, saying, "The aura of evil is very strong. Why did you come here?" The man bowed before him and detailed the matter.

    67

    法师以朱符二道授之，令其—置于门，一置于榻，仍戒不得再往湖心寺。生受符而归，如法安顿，自此果不来矣。一月有余，往衮绣桥访友。留饮至醉，都忘法师之戒，径取湖心寺路以回。将及寺门，则见金莲迎拜于前曰：“娘子久待，何一向薄情如是！ ”遂与生俱入西廊，直抵室中。女宛然在坐，数之曰：“妾与君素非相识，偶于灯下一见，感君之意，遂以全体事君，暮往朝来，于君不薄。奈何信妖道士之言，遽生疑惑，便欲永绝？薄幸如是，妾恨君深矣！今幸得见，岂能相舍？ ”即握生手，至柩前，柩忽自开，拥之同入，随即闭矣，生遂死于柩中。邻翁怪其不归，远近寻问，及至寺中停柩之室，见生之衣裾微露于柩外，请于寺僧而发之，死已久矣，与女之尸俯仰卧于内，女貌如生焉。寺僧叹曰：“此奉化州判符君之女也，死时年十七，权厝于此，举家赴北，竟绝音耗，至今十二年矣。不意作怪如是！ ”遂以尸柩及生殡于西门之外。

    Explanation

    67

    The master priest gave him two red talismans, instructing him to place one at the door and one on the bed, and warned him not to return to Huixin Temple. The young man received the talismans and returned home, placing them as instructed, and indeed, he did not come back. After more than a month, he went to Guxiu Bridge to visit a friend. He stayed to drink until he was drunk, completely forgetting the master priest's warning, and took the path directly to Huixin Temple on his way back. As he approached the temple gate, he saw a golden lotus flower bowing before him and said, "Lady, you have been waiting for a long time. Why have you been so cold-hearted?" She then took the young man with her into the west corridor, straight to the room. The woman was sitting there as if nothing had happened, and she scolded him, saying, "I have never met you before. We met by chance under the lamp, and I was moved by your intentions, so I devoted myself entirely to you, coming and going every day, treating you no differently. Why did you believe the words of the evil Taoist and suddenly doubt me? To be so unfaithful, I deeply resent you. Now that I have finally met you, how could I let you go?" She immediately took the young man's hand and led him to the coffin, which suddenly opened by itself. She embraced him and they both entered, and the coffin closed immediately. The young man died inside the coffin. The elderly neighbor was surprised that he had not returned and searched far and wide. When they reached the room in the temple where the coffin was placed, they saw the young man's sleeve slightly visible outside the coffin. They asked the temple monk to open the coffin, and it was found that the young man had been dead for a long time, lying with the woman's body inside, and the woman looked as if she were alive. The temple monk sighed and said, "This is the daughter of Fu Jun, the magistrate of Fenghua Prefecture. She died at the age of seventeen and was temporarily buried here. Her family moved north and there has been no news of them ever since, for twelve years now. Who would have thought that such strange things would happen!" They then buried the coffins and the young man outside the west gate.

    68

    自后云阴之昼，月黑之宵，往往见生与女携手同行，一丫鬟挑双头壮丹灯前导，遇之者辄得重疾，寒热交作；荐以功德，祭以牢醴，庶获痊可，杏则不起矣。居人大惧，竞往玄妙观谒魏法师而诉焉。法师曰：“吾之符箓，止能治其未然，今祟成矣，非吾之所知也。闻有铁冠道人者，居四明山顶，考劾鬼神，法术灵验，汝辈宜往求之。 ”众遂至山，攀缘藤草，蓦越溪涧，直上绝顶，果有草庵一所，道人凭几而坐，方看童子调鹤。众罗拜庵下，告以来故。道人曰：“山林隐士，旦暮且死，乌有奇术！君辈过听矣。

    Explanation

    68

    After dark, on cloudy days and moonless nights, people often saw the man and the woman walking hand in hand, with a young servant girl carrying a lantern with two heads leading the way. Those who encountered them immediately fell seriously ill, suffering from fever and chills. To cure them, they offered good deeds and sacrifices with meat and wine, hoping for recovery. If not cured, the illness would be fatal. The residents were greatly afraid and all went to the Xuanmiao Temple to consult with Master Wei. Master Wei said, "My talismans can only prevent problems before they occur. Now the evil spirit has already manifested, and it is beyond my knowledge. I have heard of an Iron Hat Taoist who lives on the top of Four Bright Mountains. He investigates and punishes ghosts and spirits, and his magic is effective. You should go to seek him." The people then went to the mountain, climbing using vines and grass, leaping across streams, and ascending directly to the summit. Indeed, there was a thatched hut, and the Taoist was leaning on a table, watching a young boy tame a crane. The people knelt and bowed at the foot of the hut, telling him about the reason for their visit. The Taoist, a hermit living in the mountains, said, "I am about to die soon. How could I have any special skills! You have been misled."

    69

    ”拒之甚严。众曰：“某本不知，盖玄妙魏师所指教耳。 ”始释然曰：“老夫不下山已六十年，小子饶舌，烦吾一行。 ”即与童子下山，步履轻捷，径至西门外，结方丈之坛，踞席端坐，书符焚之。忽见符吏数辈，黄巾锦祆，金甲雕戈，皆长丈余，屹立坛下，鞠躬请命，貌甚虔肃。道人曰：“此间有邪祟为祸，惊扰生民，妆辈岂不知耶？宜疾驱之至。 ”受命而往，不移时，以枷锁押女与生并金莲俱到，鞭菙挥扑，流血淋漓。道人呵责良久，令其供状。将吏以纸笔授之，遂各供数百言。今录其略于此。

    Explanation

    69

    The Daoist rejected them with great severity. The crowd said, "I originally did not know; it was taught by the mysterious Master Wei." He then said, "I have not come down from the mountain for sixty years. Youngster, you are talking too much, trouble me to go once." He immediately went down the mountain with his attendant, walking lightly and nimbly, and arrived at the western gate. He set up a square altar, sat cross-legged on the mat, wrote a talisman, and burned it. Suddenly, several officials of the talisman appeared, wearing yellow headbands and brocade robes, with golden armor and engraved spears, all over ten feet tall, standing firmly at the foot of the altar, bowing and asking for orders. Their appearance was very devout and solemn. The Daoist said, "There are evil spirits causing harm and disturbing the people here. You are not unaware of this, are you? They should quickly drive them here." Upon receiving the command, they went without delay, with shackles, they brought the woman, the man, and the golden lotus together. They whipped and beat them, causing blood to flow profusely. The Daoist scolded for a long time and ordered them to confess. The officials gave them paper and pens, and they each confessed several hundred words. Now recording their brief accounts here.

    70

    乔生供曰：
    　　伏念某丧室鳏居，倚门独立，犯在色之戒，动多欲之求。不能效孙生见两头蛇而决断，乃致如郑子运九尾狐而爱怜。事既莫追，侮将奚及！
    　　符女供曰：
    　　伏念某青年弃世，白昼无邻，六魄虽离，一灵未混。灯前月下，逢五百年欢喜冤家；世上民间，作千万人风流话本。迷不知返，罪安可逃！
    　　金莲供曰：
    　　伏念某杀青为骨，染素成胎，坟垄埋藏，是谁作俑而用？面目机发，比人具体而微。既有名字之称，可乏精灵之异！因而得计，岂敢为妖！
    　　供毕，将吏取呈。道人以巨笔判曰：
    　　盖闻大禹铸鼎，而神奸鬼秘莫得逃其形；温峤燃犀，而水府龙宫俱得现其状。惟幽明之异趣，乃诡怪之多端。遇之者不利于人，遭之者有害于物。故大厉入门而晋景殁，妖豕啼野而齐裹殂。降祸为妖，兴灾作孽。是以九天设斩邪之使，十地列罚恶之司，使魑魅魍魉，无以容其奸，夜叉罗剎，不得肆其暴。

    Explanation

    70

    Qiao Sheng stated:
    I humbly reflect upon myself, a widower living alone, leaning on the door and standing alone, having violated the precept against lust and acting on many desires. Unable to act decisively like Sun Shuao who saw a two-headed snake, I instead indulged in the beauty of a nine-tailed fox like Zheng Ziqi. The matter can no longer be undone, what can be done now that we have been wronged!

    Fu Nu stated:
    I humbly reflect upon myself, a young woman who has left the world, alone during the day with no neighbors, my six spirits separated but my soul still intact. In the light of the lamp and moon, I met a beloved enemy after five hundred years; in the world and among the people, I became a tale of romance for millions. Lost and not returning, how can I escape blame!

    Jin Lian stated:
    I humbly reflect upon myself, a book with bones, a fetus formed from white paper, buried in a grave, who created me and used me? With facial features and organs, I am a miniature version of a human. Having a name and form, I lack the spiritual essence! Thus achieving my purpose, how dare I be an evil spirit!

    After the statements were completed, the officials took them to present. The Taoist priest judged with a large brush:
    I have heard that Yu the Great cast the tripod, and the forms of gods, demons, and spirits could not escape their true nature; Wen Qiao burned a rhinoceros horn, and the forms of dragons and palaces were revealed. Only the differences between the visible and invisible worlds, and the many forms of the strange. Those who encounter them are harmed, and those who suffer from them are damaged. Therefore, the ghost entering the gate caused the death of Duke Jing of Jin, and the demon pig crying in the wild caused the death of King Qi. Bringing disaster and becoming an evil spirit, causing calamity and committing sins. Thus, the gods and spirits in the nine heavens and ten earths set up officials to punish evil, making the demons and monsters unable to hide their evil, and the demons and ogres unable to act violently.

    71

    矧此清平之世，坦荡之时，而乃变幻形躯，依附草木，天阴雨湿之夜，月落参横之晨，啸于梁而有声，窥其室而无睹，蝇营狗苟，牛狠狼贪，疾如飘风，烈若猛火。乔家子生犹不悟，死何恤焉。符氏女死尚贪淫，生可知矣！况金莲之怪诞，假明器而矫诬。惑世诬民，违条犯法。狐绥绥而有荡，鹑奔奔而无良。恶贯已盈，罪名不宥。陷人坑从今填满，迷魂阵自此打开。烧毁双明之灯，押赴九幽之狱。判词已具，主者奉行急急如律令。即见三人悲啼踯躅，为将吏驱捽而去。道人拂袖入山。明日，众往谢之，不复可见，止有草庵存焉。急往玄妙观访魏法师而审之，则病瘖不能言矣。

    Explanation

    71

    In this peaceful era and open time, they transform their forms and bodies, clinging to grass and trees, making sounds in the beams on rainy nights and early mornings when the moon sets, yet being unseen when observed. They live in a sycophantic and fawning manner, being as cruel and greedy as bulls and wolves, moving as swiftly as a gust of wind and burning as fiercely as a wildfire. The son of the Qiao family still does not understand when alive, how much less when dead? The daughter of the Fu family still desires lust even in death, how much more so when alive! How much more so, then, for the bizarre and fabricated nature of the "Golden Lotus," using false objects and deceit. Deceiving the world and misleading the people, violating laws and regulations. Foxes are wanton and quails are unprincipled. Evil deeds have reached their full measure, and no mercy will be shown. Traps are filled from now on, and confusion is opened from this point. The double lamps are burned, and they are sent to the underworld. The judgment is ready, and the executor shall carry it out swiftly as by law. Immediately, three people are seen weeping and hesitating, being driven away by officials. The Taoist waves his sleeves and enters the mountains. The next day, the crowd goes to thank him, but he is no longer visible, only a thatched hut remains. Hasten to the Xuanmiao Temple to consult with Master Wei for examination, but he is ill and mute, unable to speak.

    72

    渭塘奇遇记
    　　至顺中，有王生者，本士族子，居于金陵。貌莹寒玉，神凝秋水，姿状甚美，众以奇俊王家郎称之。年二十，未娶。有田在松江，因往收秋租，回舟过渭塘，见一酒肆，青旗出于檐外；朱栏曲槛，缥缈如画；高柳古槐，黄叶交坠；芙蓉十数株，颜色或深或浅，红葩绿水，上下相映；白鹅一群，游泳其间。生泊舟岸侧，登肆沽酒而饮，斫巨螯之蟹，烩细鳞之鲈，果则绿橘黄橙，莲塘之藕，松坡之栗，以花磁盏酌真珠红酒而饮之。肆主亦富家，其女年十八，知音识字，态度不凡，见生在座，频于幕下窥之，或出半面，或露全体，去而复来，终莫能舍。

    Explanation

    72

    A Strange Encounter at Wei塘

    During the reign of Emperor Shun of the Yuan Dynasty, there was a young man named Wang, a member of the scholarly class, living in Jinling. He had a face as clear and cold as jade, and his gaze was calm and deep like autumn water. His appearance was exceptionally beautiful, and everyone praised him as the extraordinary and handsome young man from the Wang family. At the age of twenty, he was still unmarried. He owned land in Songjiang and went there to collect the autumn rent. On his return journey, he passed through Wei塘 and saw a wine shop. A green flag was hung outside the eaves; the red pillars and curved railings were picturesque, and the tall willows and ancient locust trees had their yellow leaves falling. There were ten or so lotus flowers, some deep and some light in color, with red petals and green water, reflecting each other above and below. A group of white geese swam among them.

    Wang anchored his boat near the shore, entered the wine shop, bought wine, and drank it. He enjoyed large crabs with big claws and fine-scaled fish, and the fruits included green oranges, yellow tangerines, lotus root from a pond, and chestnuts from a pine slope. He drank precious red wine from delicate porcelain cups. The innkeeper was also a wealthy person, and his daughter, who was eighteen years old, was well-educated and had an extraordinary demeanor. She saw Wang sitting there and frequently peered out from behind the curtain, sometimes showing half her face, sometimes her whole body, and repeatedly returning, unable to tear herself away.

    73

    生亦留神注意，彼此目成久之。已而酒尽出肆，怏怏登舟，如有所失。是夜遂梦至肆中，入门数重，直抵舍后，始至女室，乃一小轩也。轩之前有葡萄架，架下凿池，方圆盈丈，甃以文石，养金鲫其中；池左右植垂丝桧二株，绿荫婆娑，靠墙结一翠柏屏，屏下设石假山三峰，岌然竞秀；草则金钱绣墩之属，霜露不变色。窗间挂一雕花笼，笼内畜一绿鹦鹉，见人能言。轩下垂小木鹤二只，衔线香焚之。案上立一古铜瓶，插孔雀尾数茎，其傍设笔砚之类，皆极济楚。架上横一碧玉箫，女所吹也。壁下贴金花笺四幅，题诗于上，诗体则效东坡四时词，字画则师赵松雪，不知何人所作也。

    Explanation

    73

    The person also paid close attention, and they looked at each other for a long time. Soon after the wine was finished, they left the shop, boarded the boat with a sense of discontent, as if something were lost. That night, he dreamed of reaching the shop, entering through several doors, directly reaching behind the house, and finally arriving at the woman's room, which was a small pavilion. In front of the pavilion, there was a grape trellis, under which a pond was carved, circular and square, a full zhang in size, lined with decorative stone, and containing golden carp; on both sides of the pond, two weeping junipers were planted, their green shade swaying, against the wall, a screen of green cypress was formed, and below it, three peaks of stone artificial mountains were placed, towering and competing in beauty; the grass was of the sort of money-shaped embroidered cushions, remaining vibrant even in frost and dew. Between the windows, an intricately carved cage was hung, inside which a green parrot was kept, able to speak when seen by people. Under the pavilion, two small wooden cranes were hanging, holding incense sticks that were burning. On the table, an ancient bronze vase stood, with several stems of peacock feathers inserted, and beside it, brushes, inkstones, and other stationery were placed, all extremely neat. On the shelf, a jade flute lay horizontally, the one the woman blew. Below the wall, four sheets of gold flower paper were stuck, on which poems were written, the form imitating Su Dongpo's poems about the four seasons, the calligraphy and painting studying Zhao Mengfu, and it was unknown who had written it.

    74

    第一幅云：
    　　春风吹花落红雪，杨柳荫浓啼百舌。
    　　东家蝴蝶西家飞，前岁樱桃今岁结。
    　　秋千蹴罢鬓鬖髿，粉汗凝香沁绿纱。
    　　侍女亦知心内事，银瓶汲水煮新茶。
    　　第二幅云：
    　　芭蕉叶展青鸾尾，萱草花含金凤嘴。
    　　一双乳燕出雕梁，数点新荷浮绿水。
    　　困人天气日长时，针线慵拈午漏迟。
    　　起向石榴阴畔立，戏将梅子打莺儿。

    Explanation

    74

    First poem:
    Spring wind blows petals to the ground, resembling a red snowfall.
    Willows provide dense shade, and the cuckoo bird calls.
    Butterflies fly from one house to another, and cherries that were planted last year are now bearing fruit this year.
    After playing with the swing, she brushes her hair, and the scent of sweat and perfume permeates through the green silk.
    The servant girl knows her inner thoughts, and she uses a silver bottle to draw water to brew new tea.

    Second poem:
    Banana leaves spread like the tail of a green phoenix.
    Daylily flowers contain the beak of a golden phoenix.
    A pair of young swallows emerge from an intricately carved beam, and several new lotus leaves float on the green water.
    The oppressive heat of summer makes people feel lethargic, and someone lazily picks up needlework during the afternoon, when time seems to drag on.
    She stands under the shade of a pomegranate tree and playfully throws a plum at a singing bird.

    75

    第三幅云：
    　　铁马声喧风力紧，云窗梦破鸳鸯冷。
    　　玉炉烧麝有余香，罗扇扑萤无定影。
    　　洞箫一曲是谁家？河汉西流月半斜。
    　　要染纤纤红指甲，金盆夜捣凤仙花。
    　　第四幅云：
    　　山茶未开梅半吐，风动帘旌雪花舞。
    　　金盘冒冷塑狻猊，绣幕围春护鹦鹉。
    　　倩人呵笔划双眉，脂水凝寒上脸迟。
    　　妆罢扶头重照镜，凤钗斜压瑞香枝。
    　　女见生至，与之承迎，执手入室，极其欢谑，会宿于寝。鸡鸣始觉，乃困卧篷窗底耳。
    　　自后归家，无夕而不梦焉。一夕，见架上玉箫，索女吹之。女为吹《落梅风》数阕，音调嘹亮，响彻云际。一夕，女于灯下绣红罗鞋，生剔灯花，误落于上，遂成油晕。一夕，女以紫金碧甸指环赠生，生解水晶双鱼扇坠酬之，既觉，则指环宛然在手，扇坠视之无有矣。生大为奇，遂效元稹体，赋会真诗三十韵以记其事。诗曰：
    　　有美闺房秀，天人谪降来。风流元有种，慧黠更多才。

    Explanation

    75

    The third scroll reads:
    The sound of iron horses is loud, the wind force is intense; the dream of the mandarin ducks in the cloud window is broken, and they feel cold.
    The jade stove burns musk, leaving a lingering fragrance; the silk fan flutters, chasing fireflies with no fixed shadow.
    Who plays the flute in the cave? The Milky Way flows westward, and the moon is half slanted.
    To dye the delicate red fingernails, grinding the begonia flower in a golden basin at night.
    The fourth scroll reads:
    The camellia has not yet bloomed, and the plum blossoms are half open; the wind moves the curtain, and snowflakes dance.
    The golden plate is cold, shaping the lion; the embroidered curtain surrounds the spring, protecting the parrot.
    Asking someone to warm the brush to draw the eyebrows, the lip balm freezes cold, taking time to apply to the face.
    After finishing the makeup, leaning on the head to look in the mirror again, the phoenix hairpin is tilted, pressing on the lucky fragrance branch.
    The woman sees the man arrive, welcomes him, takes his hand into the room, and they engage in playful banter, spending the night together in the bedroom. They wake up at the crow of the rooster, having fallen asleep under the thatched window.
    Afterward, when returning home, she dreams of him every night. One night, she sees the jade flute on the stand and asks the woman to play it. The woman plays several pieces of "The Falling Plum Blossom Wind," the melody is loud and clear, resounding through the clouds. One night, the woman embroiders red silk shoes by the light of the lamp, and the man pricks the lamp flower, accidentally dropping it onto the shoe, forming an oil stain. One night, the woman gives the man a purple gold and jade ring, and the man gives her a crystal double fish fan pendant in return. After waking up, the ring is still in his hand, but the fan pendant is nowhere to be seen. The man is greatly surprised and writes a poem in the style of Yuan Zhen, thirty rhymes to record the event. The poem reads:
    There is a beauty in the boudoir, a celestial being who has descended. Her charm and grace are innate, and her wit and intelligence are even more remarkable.

    76

    碾玉成仙骨，调脂作艳胎。腰肢风外柳，标格雪中梅。
    　　合置千金屋，宜登七宝台。妖姿应自许，妙质孰能陪？
    　　小小乘油壁，真真醉彩灰。轻尘生洛浦，远道接天台。
    　　放燕帘高卷，迎人户半开。菖蒲难见面，荳蔻易含胎。
    　　不待金屏射，何劳玉手栽。偷香浑似贾，待月又如崔。
    　　筝许秦宫夺，琴从卓氏猜。箫声传缥缈，烛影照徘徊。
    　　窗薄涵鱼魫，炉深喷麝煤。眉横青岫远，鬓亸绿云堆。
    　　钗玉轻轻制，衫罗窄窄裁。文鸳游浩荡，瑞凤舞毰毶。
    　　恨积鲛绡帕，欢传琥珀杯。孤眠怜月姊，多忌笑河魁。
    　　化蝶能通梦，游蜂浪作媒。雕栏行共倚，绣褥坐相偎。
    　　啖蔗逢佳境，留环得异财。绿荫莺并宿，紫气剑双埋。
    　　良夜难虚度，芳心未肯摧。残妆犹在臂，别泪已凝腮。
    　　漏滴何须促，钟声且莫催。峡中行雨过，陌上看花回。
    　　才子能知尔，愚夫可语哉！鲰生曾种福，亲得到逢莱。

    Explanation

    76

    The Jade is carved into fairy bones, and fat is refined into a beautiful form. The waist is as graceful as a willow swaying in the wind, and the character is as noble as a plum blossom in the snow.
    She is worthy of being placed in a golden house and suitable for ascending a seven-treasure platform. Her charming appearance should be her own, and no one can match her exquisite qualities.
    She rides in a fine carriage, captivating others with her true allure. Light dust arises by the Luo River, and distant paths connect to the mystical Mount Tiantai.
    The curtains are high and rolled up, and the door is half-open, welcoming guests. The rare herb calamus is hard to meet, but the young bitter orange flower easily contains its bud.
    She does not need a golden screen to enhance her beauty, nor does she require delicate hands to plant her. Her charm is like that of Jia Baoyu, and her waiting for the moon is like that of Cui Yingying.
    Her zither can rival the music of the Qin palace, and her qin is guessed to come from the family of Zuo Qiuming. The sound of the flute travels mysteriously, and the flickering candlelight illuminates her wandering steps.
    Thin windows hold the shimmering scales of fish, and a deep incense burner emits the fragrance of musk. Her eyebrows are like distant green mountains, and her hair is piled like green clouds.
    Her hairpins are delicately crafted from jade, and her silk robes are tightly fitted. A pair of mandarin ducks swims in the vast waters, and a phoenix dances gracefully.
    Her sorrows are accumulated on a silk handkerchief, and her joys are passed through a precious cup. She sympathizes with the moon goddess in her solitary sleep and often smiles at the river god.
    She can inspire dreams like a butterfly and attract admirers like a bee. She leans on carved railings together, and sits on embroidered cushions, close to each other.
    She finds sweetness in sugar cane and discovers rare treasures. Green shade shelters pairs of birds, and purple qi conceals two swords.
    A good night is hard to waste, and her beautiful heart refuses to be crushed. Her makeup still lingers on her arm, and her tears of farewell have already welled up on her cheeks.
    The dripping water does not need to be hurried, and the ringing bell should not be rushed. She has traveled through the gorge and returned to the road, seeing flowers again.
    Only a talented scholar can understand her, and a foolish person cannot speak to her! A humble person has sown good fortune and personally reached the land of Penglai.

    77

    诗讫，好事者多传诵之。明岁，复往收租，再过其处，则肆翁甚喜，延之入内。生不解意，逡巡辞避。坐定，翁以诚告之曰：“老拙惟一女，未曾适人，去岁，君子所至，于此饮酒，偶有所睹，不能定情，因遂染疾，长眠独语，如醉如痴，饵药无效，昨夕忽语曰：‘明日郎君至矣，宜往侯之。 ’初以为妄，固未之信，今而君子果涉吾地，是天假其灵而赐之便也。 ”因问生婚娶未曾，又问其门阀氏族，甚喜。肆翁即握生手，入于内室，至女所居轩下，门窗户闼，则皆梦中所历也；草木台沼、器用什物，又皆梦中所识也。女闻生至，盛妆而出，衣服之丽，簪饵之华，又皆梦中所识也。女言：“去岁自君去后，思念切至，每夜梦中与君相会，不知何故。 ”生曰：“吾梦亦如之耳。 ”女历叙吹箫之曲，绣鞋之事，无不吻合者。又出水晶双鱼扇坠示生，生亦举紫金碧甸指环以问之。彼此大惊，以为神契。遂与生为夫妇，于飞而还，终以偕老，可谓奇遇矣！

    Explanation

    77

    Upon finishing the poem, many who enjoyed it spread and recited it widely. The following year, the young man went again to collect rent and passed by the same place. The tavern owner was very pleased to see him and invited him into the inner room. The young man did not understand the meaning of the invitation and hesitated, excusing himself and avoiding it. After settling down, the tavern owner spoke to him honestly, saying, "I have only one daughter, who has never married. Last year, when the gentleman visited here and drank wine, he happened to see her, and she could not settle her feelings for him. As a result, she contracted an illness, sleeping long and speaking to herself, as if drunk or in a trance. Despite taking medicine, it was ineffective. Last night, she suddenly said, 'Tomorrow the young master will come, so I should go to meet him.' At first, I thought it was nonsense and did not believe it. Now that the gentleman has indeed entered my place, it seems that heaven has lent its spirit and granted this opportunity. I asked the gentleman if he had married or not, and also inquired about his family background and clan. I am very pleased. The tavern owner immediately took the young man's hand and led him into the inner room, to the pavilion where the daughter lived. The doors and windows, as well as the pavilion itself, were all places he had experienced in his dream; the plants, trees, pavilions, ponds, utensils, and miscellaneous items were all things he had recognized in his dream. The girl, upon hearing the young man's arrival, dressed up and came out. Her clothes were beautiful, and her hairpins and accessories were elegant, all things he had recognized in his dream. The girl said, "Since you left last year, I have missed you deeply. Every night, I meet you in my dreams, but I don't know why." The young man replied, "My dreams are the same as yours." The girl recounted in detail the flute-playing song and the story of the embroidered shoes, and everything matched perfectly. She then took out a crystal double-fish fan pendant to show him, and the young man also took out a purple gold and green jade ring to show her. They were both greatly surprised, thinking it was a spiritual connection. Thus, they became husband and wife, flying together and returning, and they lived happily together until old age, which can be considered a miraculous encounter.
