    剪灯新话卷三
    　　富贵发迹司志
    　　至正丙戌，泰州士人何友仁，为贫寠所迫，不能聊生。因谒城隍祠，过东庑，见一案，榜曰：“富贵发迹司。”友仁祷于神像之前曰：“某生世四十有五，寒一裘，暑一葛，朝、晡粥饭一盂，初无过用妄为之事。然而遑遑汲汲，常有不足之忧，冬暖而愁寒，年丰而苦饥，出无知已之投，处无蓄积之守。妻孥贱弃，乡党绝交，困阨艰难，无所告诉。侧闻大神主富贵之案，掌发迹之权，叩之即有闻，求之无不获。

    Explanation

    78

    The New Tales of the Lamp, Volume Three

    The Record of the Register of Wealth and Status

    In the third year of the Dacheng era (1346), a scholar from Taizhou named He Youren, pressed by poverty, could not sustain himself. He visited the Temple of the City God, passing through the eastern wing, and saw a table with a sign that read, "Register of Wealth and Status." He prayed before the deity's image, saying, "I have lived for forty-five years, with a single coat for winter and a light garment for summer, a bowl of porridge for breakfast and dinner, and no excessive or reckless actions. Yet, I am always anxious and eager, constantly worried about not having enough, feeling cold even in warm winters and hungry even in bountiful harvests. I have no place to go when I leave home and no savings to rely on when I stay. My wife and children are looked down upon, my neighbors and friends have cut ties, and I am in dire straits, facing hardships, with no one to turn to for help. I have heard that the great deity oversees the register of wealth and status, holds the power to elevate one's fortunes, and if asked, will provide answers, and if sought, will never fail to grant requests."

    79

    是以不避呵责，冒渎威严，屏息庭前，鞠躬户下。伏望告以倘来之事，喻以未至之机，指示迷途，提携晦迹，俾枯鱼蒙斗水之活，困鸟托一枝之安，敢不拜赐，深仰于洪造！如或前事有定，后事无由，大数既已难移，薄命终于不遇，亦望明彰报应，使得预知。 ”祷毕，跧伏案幕之下。是夜，东西两廊，左右诸曹，皆灯烛荧煌，人物骈杂，惟友仁所祷之司，不见一人，亦无灯火。独处暗中，将及毕夜，忽闻呵殿之音，初远渐近，将及庙门，诸司判官，皆趋出迎之。及入，纱笼两行，仪卫甚严。

    Explanation

    79

    Therefore, I do not avoid rebuke or criticism, boldly violating authority, holding my breath in front of the court, and bowing deeply before the door. I humbly request to be informed of things that may come, to be enlightened about opportunities that have not yet arrived, to be guided out of confusion, and to be supported if I am obscure. May a dried-up fish receive a little water to revive, and a trapped bird find a branch to rest on. How can I not be grateful and deeply indebted to such great kindness! If the past is already determined, and the future is without reason, the great fate is already difficult to change, and a thin or unfortunate fate ultimately leads to no meeting or chance, I also hope for clear and evident retribution or reward, so that I may know in advance. After finishing the prayer, I crouched and hid under the tablecloth. That night, the east and west corridors, and the various departments on the left and right, were all glowing with lamps and candles, with a crowd of people. Only the office where my friend prayed was empty, with no one and no lights. Alone in the dark, almost until dawn, I suddenly heard the sound of a procession, coming from afar and gradually getting closer, almost reaching the temple gate. The officials from the various departments all hurried out to greet it. As it entered, two rows of lanterns, with a very strict ceremonial guard.

    80

    府君朝服端简，登正殿而坐，判官辈参见既毕，皆回局治事。发迹司主者亦自殿上而来，盖适从府君朝天使回尔。坐定，有判官数人，皆幞头角带，服绯绿之衣，入户相见，各述所理之事。一人曰：“某县某户藏米二千石，近因旱蝗相继，米价倍增，邻境闭籴，野有饿莩，而乃开仓以赈之，但取原价，不求厚利，又为饘粥以济贫乏，蒙活者甚众。昨县神申上于本司，呈于府君，闻已奏知天庭，延寿三纪，赐禄万锺矣。

    Explanation

    80

    The magistrate, dressed in formal attire and carrying a simple writing brush, ascended to the main hall and took his seat. The officials gathered to pay their respects, and once their greetings were concluded, they returned to their duties. The chief of the "发迹司" also arrived from the hall, having just returned from a mission sent by the court on behalf of the magistrate. Once seated, several officials entered, wearing headbands and belts, dressed in red and green robes. They greeted the magistrate and proceeded to report on their respective tasks. One of them said, "In a certain county, a household had stored two thousand stones of rice. Recently, due to successive droughts and locust plagues, the price of rice doubled, and neighboring regions closed their grain markets, leaving fields filled with starving people. Despite this, the household opened its granaries to provide relief, selling the rice at its original price without seeking excessive profit. They also prepared thin porridge to help the poor, saving many lives. Yesterday, the local deity reported this act to our department, which in turn presented it to the magistrate. It has been reported to the heavens, and as a result, the household has been granted an extension of life by 36 years and a generous reward of a large salary."

    81

    ”一人曰：“某村某氏奉姑甚孝，其夫在外，而姑得重痼，医巫无效，乃斋沐焚香祝天，愿以身代，割股以进，固遂得愈。昨天符行下云：某氏孝通天地，诚格鬼神，令生贵子二人，皆食君禄，光显其门，终为命妇以报之。府君下于本司，今已着之福籍矣。 ”一人曰：“某姓某官，爵位已崇。俸禄亦厚，不思报国，惟务贪饕，受钞三百锭，枉法断公事，取银五百两，非理害良民。府君奏于天庭，即欲加其罪，缘本人颇有顽福，故稽延数年，使罹灭族之祸。今早奉命，记注恶簿，惟俟时至尔。 ”一人曰：“某乡某甲，有田数十顷，而贪纵无厌，务为兼并。

    Explanation

    81

    One said, "A certain woman from a certain village showed great filial piety to her mother-in-law. Her husband was away, and her mother-in-law fell gravely ill. Neither medicine nor sorcery could cure her, so she fasted, bathed, burned incense, and prayed to heaven, vowing to take her mother-in-law's place and offering her own flesh. She was thus cured. Yesterday, a heavenly edict was issued, stating: 'This woman's filial piety has reached heaven and earth, her sincerity has moved the spirits. She is to be granted two noble sons, both of whom will serve in the court, bringing glory to her family, and she will ultimately be honored as a noblewoman in return for her virtue.' The local deity has recorded this in the book of blessings."

    Another said, "A certain official with the surname of a certain name holds a high rank. He receives a generous salary, yet he does not think of serving his country. Instead, he is only concerned with greed and excess. He accepted 300 pieces of silver as bribes, perverted the law in handling public affairs, and extorted 500 taels of silver, harming good people unjustly. The local deity has reported this to the heavenly court, and they are ready to punish him. However, due to his own stubborn good fortune, the punishment has been delayed for several years, allowing him to avoid the disaster of clan extermination. This morning, I was ordered to record his evil deeds in the book of evil, and I am waiting for the time to come."

    A third said, "A certain landowner from a certain village owns dozens of hectares of land, yet he is greedy and insatiable, striving for consolidation and annexation."

    82

    邻田之接坟者，欺其势孤无援，贱价售之，又不还其值，令其含忿而死。冥府帖本司勾摄入狱，闻已儿身为牛，托生邻家，偿其所负矣。 ”诸人言叙既毕，发迹司判官忽扬眉盱目，咄嗟长叹而谓众宾日：“诸公各守其职，各治其事，褒善罚罪，可谓至矣。然而无地运行之数，生灵厄会之期，国统浙衰，大难将作，虽诸公之善理，其如之奈何！ ”众问曰：“何谓也？ ”对曰：“吾适从府君上朝帝阍，所闻众圣推论将来之事，数年之后，兵戎大起，巨河之南，长江之北，合屠戮人民三十余万，当是时也，自非积善累仁，忠孝纯至者，不克免焉。

    Explanation

    82

    A neighbor whose field bordered the grave of the deceased took advantage of his isolated and unsupported situation, selling it at a low price and not returning the money, causing him to die with resentment. The underworld issued a decree from the office to summon his soul to hell, where it was learned that his son had been reincarnated as a cow in the neighbor's family, to repay his debt. After the officials had finished recounting their stories, the judge of the Record Office suddenly raised his eyebrows and exclaimed, "Each of you guards your duty and manages your affairs, rewarding good deeds and punishing evil deeds, which can be said to be done to the utmost. However, there is no way to change the course of events, and the time when living beings will face calamity, the national system is gradually declining, and a great calamity is about to occur. Even though the officials do their best, what can they do?" The others asked, "What do you mean by that?" He replied, "I recently came from the lord of the underworld to attend court at the imperial gate, and heard the saints discussing future events. In a few years, a great war will break out, and in the south of the great river and the north of the Yangtze River, over thirty million people will be slaughtered. At that time, unless one has accumulated good deeds and benevolence, and practiced loyalty and filial piety to the utmost, they will not be able to escape."

    83

    岂生灵寡福，当此涂炭乎？抑运数已定，莫之可逃乎？ ”众皆颦蹙相顾曰：“非所知也。 ”遂各散去。友仁始于案下匍匐而出，拜述厥由。判官熟视良久，命小吏取簿籍至，亲自检阅，谓友仁曰：“君后大有福禄，非久于贪困者，自兹以往，当日胜一日，脱晦向明矣。”友仁愿示真详，乃取朱笔，大书一十六字以授友仁曰：“遇日而康，遇月而发，遇云而衰，遇电而没。 ”友仁听讫，以所授置之于怀，因再拜辞出。行及庙门外，天色已曙。

    Explanation

    83

    Are the living beings lacking in good fortune, to be in such a state of suffering? Or is it that fate is already decided, and there is no escape from it?" All present frowned and looked at each other, saying, "We do not know." So they all dispersed. Friend Ren crawled out from under the table, bowed, and explained the cause. The magistrate looked at him for a long time, then ordered a minor official to bring the records, and personally reviewed them. He said to Friend Ren, "You will have great fortune and wealth in the future, not staying long in poverty. From now on, each day will be better than the last, moving from darkness to light." Wishing to see the true details, he took a red pen, wrote sixteen large characters, and gave them to Friend Ren, saying, "When you meet the sun, you will be healthy; when you meet the moon, you will prosper; when you meet the clouds, you will decline; when you meet the lightning, you will perish." After hearing this, he put what was given to him in his bosom and bowed twice before leaving. As he walked to the temple gate, the sky had already dawned.

    84

    急探怀中，则无有矣。归而话于妻子以自慰。不数日，郡有大姓傅日英者，延之以训子弟，月奉束修五锭，家遂稍康。凡居其馆数岁。已而高邮张氏兵起，元朝命丞相脱脱统兵讨之，太师达理月沙颇知书好士，友仁献策于马首，称其意，荐于脱公，署随军参谋，车马仆从，一旦赫然。及脱公征还，友仁遂仕于朝，践历馆阁，翱翔省部，可渭贵矣。未几，授文林郎、内台御史，同列有云石不花者，与之不相能，构于大官，黜为雷州录事。友仁忆判官之言，日月云三字，皆已验矣，深自戒惧，不敢为非。

    Explanation

    84

    Hurriedly searching in his bosom, but found nothing. Returning home, he talked to his wife and children to console himself. Not long after, in the prefecture, there was a prominent family named Fu Rihui who invited him to educate their children, offering him a monthly stipend of five ingots of silver, and his family gradually became more prosperous. He stayed in their household for several years. Later, a rebellion led by Zhang in Gaoyou broke out, and the Yuan dynasty ordered Chancellor Toghon to lead troops to suppress it. Grand Tutor Darimyesh, who was well-versed in books and fond of scholars, was pleased with Youren's strategy presented at the front lines and recommended him to Toghon. Youren was appointed as a military advisor, with carriage, horses, and attendants, and suddenly became prominent. When Toghon returned from his campaign, Youren then served in the imperial court, served in the imperial library, and moved freely among the ministries, truly a person of high rank. Shortly after, he was appointed as a literary officer and an internal court censor. Among his colleagues was Yunshi Buha, who did not get along with him and was influenced by a high-ranking official, leading to his dismissal and sending to serve as a recorder in Leizhou. Youren recalled the magistrate's words about the three characters "sun, moon, cloud," all of which had come true, and deeply warned himself, not daring to do wrong.

    85

    到任二年，有事申总府，吏具牍以进，友仁自署其衔曰：雷州路录事何某。挥笔之际，风吹纸起，于雷字之下，曳出一尾，宛然成一电字，大恶之，亟命易去。是夜感疾，自知不起，处置家事，诀别妻子而终。因详判官所述众圣之语，将来之事。盖至正辛卯之后，张氏起兵淮东，国朝创业淮西，攻斗争夺，干戈相寻，沿淮诸郡，多被其祸，死于兵者何止三十万焉。是以知普夭之下，率土之滨，小而一身之荣悴通寒，大而一国之兴衰治乱，皆有定数，不可转移，而妄庸者乃欲辄施智术于其间，徒自取困尔。

    Explanation

    85

    Having taken office for two years, there were affairs to report to the provincial governor. The officials prepared the document and presented it. Friend Ren (or Ren) inscribed his title: Recorder of the Road of Leizhou, Mr. He. At the moment of writing, the wind blew the paper up, and below the character '雷,' a tail was drawn out, forming the character '电' in a striking manner. He greatly disliked it and quickly ordered it to be changed. That night he felt ill, knowing he would not recover. He arranged his family affairs and bade farewell to his wife and children before passing away. Because he carefully considered the words of the judges about the sages and future events, from the year Xinhao of the Zhi Zheng era onwards, the Zhang family raised an army in Huai East, our dynasty founded its cause in Huai West, fighting and competing, weapons clashed repeatedly, various counties along the Huai River suffered greatly, and how many tens of thousands died in battle. Therefore, it is known that throughout the world, from border to border, from the smallest personal fortunes and misfortunes to the largest national rise and fall, order and chaos, all are predetermined and cannot be changed. But the foolish and incompetent wish to apply their intelligence and strategies, only to bring themselves to ruin.

    永州野庙记
    　　永州之野，有神庙，背山临流，川泽深险，黄茅绿草，一望无际，大木参天而蔽日者，不知其数，风雨往住生其上，人皆畏而事之，过者必以牲牢献于殿下，始克前往，如或不然，则风雨暴至，云雾晦冥，咫尺不辩，人物行李，皆随失之。如是者有年矣。大德间，书生毕应详，有事适衡州，道由庙下，囊橐贫匮，不能设奠，但致敬而行。未及数里，大风振作，吹沙走石，玄云黑雾，自后隐至。回顾，见甲兵甚众，追者可千乘万骑，自分必死，平日能诵《玉枢经》，事势既危，且行且诵，不绝于口。须臾，则云收风止，天地开朗。所迫兵骑。不复有矣。仅而获全，得达衡州，过祝融峰，谒南岳祠，思忆前事，具状焚诉。

    Explanation

    86

    The Temple of the Wilds of Yongzhou

    In the wilds of Yongzhou, there is a temple, backed by mountains and facing a river, with deep and perilous rivers and marshes surrounding it. The landscape is covered with yellow grass and green vegetation, stretching as far as the eye can see. Tall trees reach up to the sky and block the sunlight, and storms and rains often arise above it. People all fear and worship it, and those who pass by must offer sacrificial animals at the temple's steps to proceed. If not so, storms and winds suddenly arrive, dark clouds and black mist obscure everything, and one cannot distinguish even at close range. People and their belongings all disappear. This has been the case for many years.

    During the Dade period, a scholar named Bi Yingxiang had business in Hengzhou and passed by the temple on his way. His bags and pouches were poor and lacking, and he could not set up an offering, so he paid respect and continued on his way. Not even a few miles away, a strong wind arose, blowing sand and stones, and dark clouds and black mist appeared behind him. Looking back, he saw many armored soldiers, with pursuers numbering in the thousands of chariots and tens of thousands of horses. He thought he would surely die. He could recite the Yujuzhijing daily, and the situation was already dangerous. He continued walking and reciting, without ceasing. In a moment, the clouds cleared and the wind stopped, and the sky and earth became clear. The soldiers and horses that had been pursuing him were no longer there. He barely survived and reached Hengzhou, passing through Zhurong Peak and visiting the Southern Mountain Temple. Recalling the previous events, he wrote a detailed account and burned it as an offering.

    87

    是夜，梦駃卒来追，与之偕行，至大宫殿，侍卫罗列，曹局分市。駃卒引立大庭下，望殿上挂玉栅帘，帘内设黄罗帐，灯烛辉煌，光若白昼，严邃整肃，寂而不哗。应祥屏息俟命。俄一吏朱农角带，自内而出，传呼曰：“得旨问与何人有讼？”伏而对曰：“身为寒儒，性又愚拙。不知名利之可求，岂有田宅之足竞！布衣蔬食，守分而巳。且又未尝一入公门，无以仰答威问。 ”吏曰：“日间投状，理会何事？ ”应祥始悟，稽首而白曰：“实以贫故，出境投人，道由永州，过神祠下，行囊罄竭，不能以牲醴祭事，触神之怒，风雨暴起，兵甲追逐，狼狈颠踣，几为所及，惊怖急迫，无处申诉，以致唐突圣灵，诚非得已。 ”吏入，少顷复出，曰：“得旨追对。”即见吏士数人，腾空而去。俄顷，押一白须老人，乌巾道服，跪于阶下。

    Explanation

    87

    On that night, Ying Xiang dreamed of a swift soldier coming to pursue him, and they went together to a great palace. The guards were lined up, and the departments and offices were arranged. The swift soldier led him to stand in the great courtyard, where he looked up at the jade lattice curtain hung on the hall, with a yellow brocade canopy set inside the curtain. The lamps and candles were brilliant, the light like daytime, and the atmosphere was strict, profound, neat, and solemn, quiet without clamor. Ying Xiang held his breath waiting for orders. Soon, a clerk with red horns and a belt appeared, coming out from inside, and called out saying, "Received the order to ask who he was in dispute with." Ying Xiang prostrated and replied, "I am a poor scholar, my nature is also foolish and clumsy. I do not know that fame and profit can be sought, how could there be enough land and houses to compete for. Wearing coarse clothes and eating vegetables, just keeping to my lot. And I have never entered a public office, unable to answer the stern questions." The clerk asked, "Submitted a petition during the day, what business is it?" Ying Xiang suddenly realized and knelt and said respectfully, "Indeed, because of poverty, I left the country and sought help from others, traveling through Yongzhou, passed by a shrine. My traveling bag was empty, unable to offer sacrifices with meat and wine, offending the deity's anger, sudden storms arose, soldiers chased, in a desperate and stumbling state, almost caught, in a state of fear and urgency, nowhere to appeal, resulting in rudely intruding upon the holy, truly not by choice." The clerk went in, a short while later came out again, saying, "Received the order to be summoned for questioning." Immediately, several officials and soldiers flew into the air and left. Soon, they led an old man with a white beard, wearing a black cap and Taoist robe, kneeling at the steps.

    88

    吏宣旨诘之曰：“汝为一方神祗，众所敬奉，奈何辄以威祸恐人，求其祀飨，迫此儒士，几陷死地，贪婪苦虐，何所逃刑！ ”老人拜而对曰：“某实永州野庙之神也，然而庙为妖蟒所据，已有年矣，力不能制，旷职已久。向者驱驾风雨，邀求奠酹，皆此物所为。非某之过。 ”吏责之曰：“事既如此，何不早陈？ ”对曰：“此物在世已久，兴妖作孽，无与为比。社鬼祠灵，承其约束；神蛟毒虺，受其指挥。每欲奔诉，多方抵截，终莫能达。

    Explanation

    88

    The official announced the imperial edict and questioned him, saying, "You are a local deity, revered by many. Why do you constantly threaten people with calamity to demand worship? You have pressured this scholar, nearly causing his death. Your greed and cruelty, where can you escape punishment?" The old man bowed and replied, "I am indeed the deity of a wild temple in Yongzhou. However, the temple has been occupied by a venomous snake for many years, and I have been unable to control it, neglecting my duties for a long time. Previously, I would summon wind and rain, demanding sacrifices, all of which were done by this creature. It is not my fault." The official reprimanded him, saying, "If things are as you say, why didn't you report it earlier?" The old man replied, "This creature has existed for a long time, causing chaos and evil, unmatched by others. Local spirits and temple deities all submit to its commands; mythical dragons and poisonous snakes all follow its orders. Whenever I try to report it, it obstructs me in many ways, and I cannot reach anyone."

    89

    今者非神使来追，亦焉得到此！ ”即闻殿上宣旨，令士吏追勘。老人拜恳曰：“妖孽已成，辅之者众，吏士虽往，终恐无益，非自神兵剿捕，不可得也。 ”殿上如其言，命一神将领兵五千而往。久之，见数十鬼卒，以大木舁其首而至，乃一朱冠白蛇也。置于庭下，若五石缸焉。吏顾应祥令还，欠伸而觉，汗流浃背。事讫回途，再经其处，则殿宇偶像，荡然无遗。问于村甿，皆曰：“某夜三更后，雷霆风火大作，惟闻杀伐之声，惊咳叵测。
    旦往视之，则神庙已为煨烬，一巨白蛇长数十丈，死于林木之下，而丧其元。其余蚺虺螣蝮之属无数，腥秽之气，至今未息。 ”考其日，正感梦时也。应祥还家，白昼闲坐，忽见二鬼使至前曰：“地府屈君对事。”即挽其臂以往。及至，见王者坐大厅上，以铁笼罩一白衣绎帻丈夫，形状甚伟。自陈：“在世无罪，为书生毕应祥枉告于南岳，以致神兵降代，举族歼夷，巢穴倾荡，冤苦实甚。

    Explanation

    90

    ”应祥闻言，知为蛇妖挟仇捏诉，乃具陈其害人祸物、兴妖作怪之事，对辩于铁笼之下，往返甚苦，终不肯服。王者乃命吏牒南岳衡山府及帖永州城隍司征验其事。己而，衡山府及永州城隍司回文，与毕应祥所言实事相同，方始词塞。王者殿上大怒，叱之曰：“生既为妖，死犹妄诉，将白衣妖孽押赴酆都，永不出世！ ”即有鬼卒数人驱押之去，受其果报。王谓应祥曰：“劳君一行，无以相报”命吏取毕姓薄籍来，于应祥名下，批八字云：“除妖去害，延寿一纪。”应祥拜谢而返。及门而寤，乃曲肱几上尔。

    Explanation

    90

    Yingxiang, upon hearing the words, knew it was the snake demon holding a grudge and fabricating accusations. He then fully presented the cases of harming people, causing disasters, and creating supernatural disturbances, and debated in front of the iron cage. The back-and-forth was very arduous, and the snake demon finally refused to admit defeat. The king then ordered officials to send documents to the South Yue Hengshan Prefecture and the Yongzhou City God Temple to verify the matter. Later, the replies from the South Yue Hengshan Prefecture and the Yongzhou City God Temple confirmed the facts as stated by Bi Yingxiang, and only then did the snake demon become speechless. The king, greatly angered on the throne, scolded him, saying, "Since you were an evil spirit in life, you still fabricate accusations in death. You will be taken to Fengdu and never be reborn!" Immediately, several ghost soldiers took him away to suffer his karmic retribution. The king said to Yingxiang, "I thank you for your effort; there is nothing I can give you in return." He ordered officials to bring the registry of the Bi family, and on Yingxiang's name, wrote eight characters saying, "To eliminate the evil spirit and remove harm, extending his life by one cycle of twelve years." Yingxiang bowed in thanks and returned. Upon reaching the door, he woke up, and it was just his arm resting on the table.

    申阳洞记
    　　陇西李生，名德逢，年二十五，善骑射，驰骋弓马，以胆勇称，然而不事生产，为乡党贱弃。天历间，父友有任桂州监郡者，因往投焉。至则其人已殁，流落不能归。郡多名山，日以猎射为事，出没其间，末尝休息，自以为得所乐。有大姓钱翁者，以赀产雄于郡，止有一女，年及十七，甚所钟爱，未尝窥门，虽姻亲邻里，亦罕见之。一夕，风雨晦冥，失女所在，门窗户闼，扃鐍如故，莫知所从往。闻于官，祷于伸，访于四境，悄无踪迹。

    Explanation

    91

    Record of the Shenyang Cave

    Li Sheng of Longxi, whose name was DeFeng, was twenty-five years old. Skilled in riding and archery, he was renowned for his courage and bravery, yet he did not engage in productive work and was thus looked down upon by his fellow townspeople. During the Tianli era, a friend of his father held the position of supervisor of Guizhou, so Li went to seek him out. Upon arrival, he found that the man had already died, and so Li became a wanderer, unable to return home. The prefecture was rich in mountains, and Li made hunting and shooting his daily occupation, moving in and out of these regions without ever resting, believing he had found his joy.

    There was a wealthy man named Qian, who was the most powerful figure in the prefecture by virtue of his wealth. He had only one daughter, who was seventeen years old, and he treasured her greatly. She had never stepped outside the gates of the house, and even relatives and neighbors rarely saw her. One night, amid wind and rain, the sky darkened and obscured. The daughter had disappeared. The doors and windows were locked as usual, and no one knew where she had gone. The matter was reported to the authorities, prayers were made to the heavens, and a search was conducted throughout the entire region, but no trace of her was found.

    92

    翁念女切至，设誓曰：“有能知女所在者，愿以家财—半给之，并以女事焉。 ”虽求寻之意甚切，而荏苒将及半载，竟绝音响。生一日挟镞持弧出城，遇一麞，逐之不舍，遂越冈峦，深入涧谷，终莫能及。日巳曛黑，又迷来路，彷徨于垄坂之侧，莫知所适。已而烟昏云瞑，虎啸猿啼，远近黯然，若一更之后。遥望山顶，见一古庙，委身投之。至则尘埃堆积，墙壁倾颓，兽蹄鸟迹，交杂于中。生虽甚怖，然无可奈何，少憩庑下，将以待旦。未及瞑目，忽闻传导之声，自远而至。生念深山静夜，安得有此？疑其为鬼神，又恐为盗劫，乃攀缘槛楣，伏于梁间，以窥其所为。

    Explanation

    92

    The old man was deeply anxious about his daughter and took an oath, saying: "Whoever can discover where my daughter is, I will give them half of my family wealth, and I will also treat my daughter as their wife." Although his desire to find her was intense, time passed slowly and nearly reached half a year, and finally, all sound and communication ceased. One day, the young man took his bow and arrows and went out of the city. He encountered a deer and chased it without letting go, crossing over hills and mountains, and deeply into valleys and gullies, but ultimately could not catch it. The sun had already turned dark, and he lost his way back, wandering at the side of ridges and slopes, not knowing where to go. Soon after, the sky darkened and the clouds thickened, and tigers roared while apes cried. Near and far, everything grew dark, as if it were after the first watch of the night. Looking far up the mountain, he saw an ancient temple and cast himself into it. Upon arriving, he found dust accumulated and walls collapsed, with animal tracks and bird prints mixed together inside. Though the young man was greatly frightened, there was nothing he could do, so he took a short rest under the eaves, intending to wait until dawn. Before he could close his eyes, he suddenly heard the sound of footsteps approaching from afar. Thinking to himself, "In such a deep mountain and quiet night, how could there be such a sound?" He suspected it was ghosts or spirits, but also feared it might be bandits. So he climbed the railings, hid under the beam, and peered to see what they were doing.

    93

    须臾，及门，有二红灯前导，为首者顶三山冠，绛帕首，披淡黄袍，束玉带，径据神案而坐。从者十余辈，各执器仗，罗列阶下，仪卫虽甚整肃，而状貌则皆豭貜之类也。生知为邪魅，取腰间箭，持满一发，正中坐者之臂，失声而走，群党一时溃散，莫知所之。久之，寂然，乃假寐待旦。则见神座边鲜血点点，从大门而出，沿路不绝，循山而南，将及五里，得—大穴，血踪由此而入。生往来穴口，顾盼之际，草根柔滑，不觉失足而坠。乃深坑万仞，仰不见天，自分必死。旁边微觉有路，寻路而行，转入幽遽，咫尺不辨。

    Explanation

    93

    In a short while, the scholar arrived at the gate, where two red lanterns led the way. The leader wore a three-peak cap, a red headscarf, a light yellow robe, and a jade belt, sitting directly on the altar. His followers, numbering over ten, each held weapons and arranged themselves below the steps. Although the ceremonial guard was very orderly, their appearance was like that of boars and badgers. The scholar recognized them as evil spirits and took an arrow from his waist, drew it to the full, and shot it, hitting the arm of the one sitting. The leader screamed and ran away, and the group dispersed immediately, no one knowing where they went. After a while, it became silent, and the scholar pretended to sleep until dawn. Then he saw spots of fresh blood near the altar, which left through the main gate, continuing along the road without interruption, following the mountain to the south, about five miles, where he found a large cave. The blood trail entered here. The scholar went back and forth at the cave entrance, in the blink of an eye, the grass roots were soft and slippery, and he unconsciously stepped on it and fell. It was a deep pit thousands of feet deep, looking up, he could not see the sky, and he thought he was surely going to die. He faintly felt a path on the side, followed the path, turned into a dark and secluded place, within arm's reach, he could not see.

    94

    更前百步，豁然开朗，见一石室，榜曰：申阳之洞。守门者数人，装束如昨夕庙中所睹。见生，惊曰：“子为何人，而遽至此？”生磬折作礼而答曰：“下界凡氓，久居城府，以医为业。因乏药材，入山采拾，贪多务得，进不知止。不觉失足，误坠于斯。触冒尊灵，乞垂觅宥。 ”守门者闻言，似有喜色，问之曰：“汝既业医，能为人治疗乎？”生曰：“此分内事也。 ”守门者大喜，以手加额曰： “天也！ ”生请其故。曰：“吾君申阳侯，昨因出游，为流矢所中，卧病在床，而汝惠然来斯，是天以神医见贶也。 ”乃邀生坐于门下，踉跄趋入，以告于内。

    Explanation

    94

    Advancing another hundred steps, the scene suddenly opened up, revealing a stone chamber inscribed as "The Cave of Shenyang." Several guardians stood there, dressed as seen in the temple the previous night. Upon seeing the man, they were startled and asked, "Who are you, and why have you come here so suddenly?" The man bowed deeply in a formal gesture and replied, "I am an ordinary person from the mortal world, long residing in the city, making a living as a doctor. Due to a lack of medicinal herbs, I entered the mountains to collect them, greedy for much and eager to gain, advancing without knowing when to stop. I did not realize I had offended the sacred spirit and am begging for mercy and forgiveness." The guardians, upon hearing this, seemed pleased and asked, "Since you are a doctor, can you treat others?" The man replied, "This is my duty." The guardians were greatly delighted, placing their hands on their foreheads and said, "Heavenly will!" The man inquired why, and they explained, "Our lord, the Duke of Shenyang, was injured by a flying arrow yesterday while out, lying ill in bed. You have graciously come here, which is a heavenly bestowal upon us." They then invited the man to sit below the door and hurriedly entered to inform those inside.

    95

    顷之，出而传其主之命曰：“仆不善摄生，自贻伊戚，祸及股肱，毒流骨髓，厄运莫逃，残生待尽。今而幸值神医，获赐良剂，是受病者有再生之乐，而治病者有全生之恩也。敢不忍死以待！ ”生遂摄衣而入，度重门，及曲房，帷幄衾褥，极其华丽。见一老猕猴，偃卧石榻之上，呻吟之声不绝。美人侍侧者三，皆绝色也。生诊其脉，抚其疮，诡曰：“无伤也，予有仙药，非徒治病，兼可度世，服之则能后天不老，而凋三光矣。今之相遇，盖亦有缘耳。 ”遂倾囊出药，令其服之。

    Explanation

    95

    Soon after, he went out and conveyed his master's command: "I have not taken care of myself well, bringing upon myself sorrow, misfortune has affected my limbs, poison has spread to my bone marrow, misfortune cannot be avoided, and my remaining life is waiting to be exhausted. Now, fortunately, I have encountered a divine physician and received a good medicine. This means the sick person has the joy of being reborn, and the healer has the grace of saving lives. Dare not die before receiving the treatment!" The narrator then took off his outer garment and entered, passing through heavy doors and reaching a secluded room. The curtains, beds, and bedding were extremely luxurious. He saw an old monkey lying on a stone bed, with moaning sounds never stopping. Three beautiful women were serving at the side, all of extraordinary beauty. The narrator examined the monkey's pulse and touched its wound, then said deceitfully, "There is no harm. I have divine medicine, not only for treating illness but can also transcend the world. If taken, it can make one not age after birth, and can make the three lights wither. Today's meeting must also be due to fate." He then emptied his bag to take out the medicine and ordered the monkey to take it.

    群妖闻度世之说，喜得长生，皆罗拜于前曰：“尊官信是神人，今幸相遇！吾君既获仙丹永命，吾等独不得沾刀圭之赐乎？”生遂罄其所赍，遍赐之，皆踊跃争夺，惟恐不预。其药盖毒之尤者，用以淬箭镞而射鸷兽，无不应弦而倒。有顷，群妖一时仆地，昏眩无知矣。生顾宝剑悬于石壁，取而悉斩之，凡戳猴大小三十六头。疑三女为妖，欲并除之。皆泣而言曰：“妾等皆人，非魅也。不幸为妖猴所摄，沉陷坑阱，求死不得。今君能为妾除害，即妾再生之主也，敢不惟命是听！ ”问其姓名居址，其—即钱翁之女，其二亦皆近邑良家也。生虽能除去群妖，然无计以出。

    96

    The evil spirits, upon hearing the doctrine of transcending the world, rejoiced at the prospect of immortality and all knelt and bowed before him, saying, "Your Excellency is truly a divine being; we are fortunate to meet you! Our lord has obtained the elixir of immortality and eternal life. Why can't we also receive a small portion of this elixir?" The protagonist then gave away all that he had brought, distributing it among them. They all eagerly competed for it, fearing they would not get a share. The elixir was the most toxic of poisons, used to temper the arrowheads and shoot fierce beasts, causing them to fall dead at the sound of the bowstring. Soon after, the evil spirits all collapsed, becoming unconscious and unaware. The protagonist, seeing the magical sword hanging on the stone wall, took it and cut them all down, killing thirty-six monkeys, both large and small. Suspecting that the three women were also demons, he wanted to eliminate them as well. They all wept and said, "We are all human, not demons. Unfortunately, we were captured by the evil monkeys, trapped in pits and traps, unable to die. Now that you can rid us of this harm, you are our savior. How dare we not obey your commands?" He asked for their names and addresses, and found that one of them was the daughter of Mr. Qian, while the other two were also from nearby towns of good families. Although the protagonist was able to eliminate the evil spirits, he had no way to escape.

    愤闷之际，忽有老父数人，不知自何来，皆身被褐裘，长须乌喙，推一白衣者居前，向生列拜曰：“吾等虚星之精，久有此土，近为妖猴所据，力弗能敌，屏避他方，俟其便而图之。不意君能为我扫除仇怨，荡涤凶邪，敢不致谢！ ”各于袖中出金珠之属，置于生前。生曰：“若等既具神通，何乃见欺于彼，自伏孱劣耶？”白衣者曰：“吾寿止五百岁，彼已八百岁，是以不敌。然吾等居此，与人无害也，功成行满，当得飞游诸天，出入自在耳。非若彼之贪淫肆暴，害人祸物。今其稔恶不已，举族夷灭，盖亦获咎于天，假手于君耳。

    97

    In a moment of deep frustration, several elderly men suddenly appeared, unknown from where they came. They were all dressed in coarse, unadorned garments, with long beards and black mustaches. They pushed one man in white robes to the front and bowed in a row, saying, "We are the spirits of the celestial stars, long having this land. Recently, it has been taken over by a demon monkey, and we cannot resist them. We have retreated to another place, waiting for an opportunity to deal with them. Unintended that you could clear away our grievances and purge the evil and wickedness! How dare we not express our thanks!" Each of them took out gold and jewels from their sleeves and placed them in front of the person. The person said, "You all possess supernatural powers, why are you being deceived by them, why are you so weak and inferior?" The man in white robes replied, "My lifespan is only five hundred years, they have already lived eight hundred years, that is why we cannot compete. However, we live here, we do not harm people. When our deeds are complete and our conduct is fulfilled, we will be able to fly and travel through the heavens, with freedom to come and go. Unlike them, who are greedy, lewd, and violent, harming people and things. Now their wickedness has accumulated and is not stopping, the entire family will be exterminated, they have indeed incurred the wrath of heaven, it is by your hand that they will be punished."

    爱卿传
    　　罗爱爱，嘉兴名娼也，色貌才艺，独步一时。而又性识通敏，工于侍词，以是人皆敬而慕之，称为爱卿。佳篇丽什，传播人口。风流之士，咸修饰以求狎，懵学之辈，自视缺然。郡中名士，尝以季夏望日，会于鸳湖凌虚阁避暑，玩月赋诗。爱卿先成四首，座间皆搁笔。诗曰：
    　　画阁东头纳晚凉，红莲不似白莲香。
    　　一轮明月天如水，何处吹萧引凤凰？
    　　月出天边水在湖，微澜倒浸玉浮图。
    　　搴帘欲共姮娥语，肯教霓裳一曲无？
    　　手弄双头茉莉枝，曲终不觉鬓云欹。

    Explanation

    99

    Love Minister's Biography

    Lu Aiai, a renowned courtesan of Jiaxing, was unparalleled in her beauty, talent, and skill in the arts. Her intellect was keen and perceptive, and she excelled in the use of language. Because of these qualities, people admired and respected her, and she was affectionately called "Love Minister." Her beautiful and elegant writings spread widely among the populace. Men of elegance and refinement sought her company, while those who were less educated felt inadequate in comparison. Once, during the full moon day of the sixth month, the notable scholars of the prefecture gathered at the Pavilion of the Empty Sky on Swan Lake to escape the summer heat and enjoy the moon while composing poetry. Love Minister completed four poems first, and everyone else put down their brushes in admiration. Her poems read:

    At the eastern end of the painted pavilion, the evening coolness is welcomed,
    The red lotus is unlike the white lotus in fragrance.
    A round bright moon like water in the sky,
    Where is the flute playing to attract the phoenix?

    The moon rises from the horizon, the lake mirrors the sky,
    Gentle ripples reflect on the jade pagoda.
    Pulling the curtain to converse with Chang'e,
    Would Chang'e allow the song of the rainbow robe to be absent?

    Holding a branch of double-headed jasmine,
    By the time the song ends, her hair has fallen slightly.

    100

    佩环响处飞仙过，愿偕青鸾一只骑。
    　　曲曲栏干正正屏，六铢衣薄懒来凭。
    　　夜深风露凉如许，身在瑶台第一层。
    　　同郡有赵氏子者，第六，亦簪缨族，父亡母存，家赀巨万，慕其才色，纳礼聘焉。爱卿入门，妇道甚修，家法甚饬，择言而发，非礼不行。赵子嬖而重之。未久，赵子有父党为吏部尚书，以书自大都召之，许授以江南一宫。赵子欲往，则恐贻母妻之忧，不往。则又失功名之会，踌躇未决。爱卿谓之曰：“妾闻男子生而桑弧蓬矢以射四方，丈夫壮而立身扬名以显父母，岂可以恩情之笃，而误功名之期乎？君母在堂，温凊之奉，甘旨之供，妾任其责有余矣。但年高多病，而君有万里之行，昔人所渭事主之日多，报亲之日少，君宜常以此为念。望太行之孤云，抚西山之颓日，不可不早归耳。 ”赵子遂卜日为京都之行，置酒酌别于中堂。酒三行，爱卿请赵子捧觞为太大人寿，自制《齐天乐》一阕，歌以侑之。其词曰：

    Explanation

    100

    Where the sound of jade pendants and rings is heard, a fairy passes by; I wish to ride one green phoenix together.
    Curved railings and straight screens, wearing a thin six-zhu robe, I am too lazy to lean on the railing.
    The night is deep, and the wind and dew are so cool; I am in the highest level of the jade platform.
    There is a man named Zhao from the same county, the sixth son, also from a distinguished family. His father has passed away, and his mother is still alive, with a fortune of ten thousand. Admiring his talent and beauty, he was invited to marry her. Lady Ai entered the household, and she was very virtuous and disciplined. She spoke only when necessary and followed proper etiquette. Zhao loved and respected her greatly. Not long after, Zhao had a relative who became the Minister of Personnel. He wrote a letter from the capital, inviting Zhao to take a position in the south. Zhao wanted to go, but he was worried about causing distress to his mother and wife. If he didn't go, he would miss out on an opportunity for fame and success. He hesitated and could not make a decision. Lady Ai said to him, "I have heard that men are born with bows made of mulberry and arrows made of thorn to shoot at all directions. Men should establish themselves and bring honor to their parents when they grow up. How can one let deep affection hinder the pursuit of fame and success? Your mother is still alive, and I can take care of her needs and provide her with good food and warmth. But she is old and often ill, and you have a long journey ahead. As the ancients said, the days spent serving the master are many, but the days spent honoring the parents are few. You should always keep this in mind. Looking at the solitary clouds over Mount Taihang and touching the setting sun over the Western Hills, you must return early." Zhao then chose a date for his journey to the capital and held a farewell banquet in the hall. After three rounds of wine, Lady Ai asked Zhao to raise a cup for his mother's birthday. She composed a poem titled "Qitianle" and sang it as a toast. The poem goes:

    Translation of the poem "Qitianle":

    Where the sound of jade pendants and rings is heard, a fairy passes by;
    I wish to ride one green phoenix together.
    Curved railings and straight screens, wearing a thin six-zhu robe, I am too lazy to lean on the railing.
    The night is deep, and the wind and dew are so cool;
    I am in the highest level of the jade platform.

    101

    恩情不把功名误，离筵又歌金缕。白发慈亲，红颜幼妇，君去有谁为主？流年几许？况闷闷愁愁，风风雨雨。凤折鸾分，未知何日更相聚！蒙君再三分付：向堂前侍奉，休辞辛苦。官诰蟠花，宫袍制锦，待要封妻拜母。君须听取：怕日薄西山，易生愁阻。早促归程，彩衣相对舞。
    　　歌罢，坐中皆垂泪。赵子乘醉，解缆而行。至都，则尚书以病免，无所投托，迁延旅邸，久不能归。太夫人以忆子之故，感病沉重，伏枕在床。爱卿事之甚谨，汤药必亲尝，饘粥必亲煮。求神礼佛，以逭其灾；虚辞诡说，以宽其意。缠绵半载，因遂不起。临终，呼爱卿而告之曰：“吾子以功名之故，远赴皇都，遂绝昔耗。吾又下幸罹疾，新妇事我至矣！今而命殂，无以相报。但愿吾子早归，新妇异日有子有孙，皆如新妇之孝敬。苍天有知，必不相负！ ”言讫而殁。爱卿哀毁如礼，亲造棺椁。葬于白苎村。既葬，旦夕哭临灵几前，悲伤过度，为之瘦痟。

    Explanation

    101

    Affection does not hinder one's pursuit of fame and success, yet at the farewell banquet, the Jinlü (Golden Threads) is sung. With white-haired, loving parents and a young, beautiful wife, who will take charge when you depart? How many years have passed? Moreover, with gloomy and sorrowful feelings, amidst wind and rain. The phoenix and the crane part ways, and it is unknown when we will meet again! I beg you to listen carefully once more: serve your parents diligently, do not shirk the hard work. Official documents adorned with intricate patterns and court robes woven with fine brocade await to honor your wife and mother. You must heed this: fear the setting sun on the western mountain, as it easily brings sorrow and obstacles. Hasten your return, and dance together in colorful garments.

    After the song, all present wept. Zhao Zi, drunk, untied the ropes and set off. Upon arriving in the capital, the Shangshu (Cabinet Minister) fell ill and resigned, leaving Zhao Zi without a place to go, prolonging his stay in the inn, unable to return home for a long time. The respected mother, due to missing her son, fell gravely ill and lay in bed. The beloved wife took care of her with great diligence, personally tasting the medicine and cooking the porridge. She sought divine protection and offered prayers to the Buddha to ward off calamities; she used gentle words and deceptions to soothe her mother's mind. After half a year of tending, the mother finally passed away. On her deathbed, she called out to the beloved wife and said, "My son, for the sake of fame and success, went far to the imperial capital, and we have not heard from him since. I, too, have fallen ill, and you have taken care of me so well! Now that my life is ending, I have nothing to repay you. I only hope that my son returns soon, and that your future children and grandchildren will all be as filial and respectful as you. Heaven, if you know, will surely not let you down!" She then passed away. The beloved wife, deeply grieved and following proper mourning rites, personally prepared the coffin. She was buried in Baiwu Village. After the burial, she mourned at the spirit table every day and night, her sorrow so great that she became emaciated and wasted away.

    至正十六年，张士诚陷平江，十七年，达丞相檄苗军师杨完者为江浙参政，拒之于嘉兴。不戢军士。大掠居民。赵子之居，为刘万户者所据，见爱卿之姿色，欲逼纳之。爱卿以甘言给之，沐浴入合，以罗巾自缢而死。万户奔救之，已无及矣。乃以绣褥裹尸，瘗于后圃银杏树下。未几，张氏通款，浙省杨参政为所害，麾下皆星散。赵子始间关海道，由太仓登岸，径回嘉兴，则城郭人民皆非旧矣。投其故宅，荒废无人居，但见鼠窜于梁，鸮鸣于树，苍苔碧草，掩映阶庭而已。求其母妻，不知去向，惟中堂岿然独存，乃洒扫而息焉。明日，行出东门外，至红桥倒，遇旧使老苍头于道，呼而问之，备述其详：则老母辞堂，生妻去世矣。遂引赵子至白苎村其母葬处，指松柏而告之曰：“此皆六娘子之所种植也。”指茔垄而告之曰：“此皆六娘子之所经理也。太夫人以郎君不归，感念成疾，娘子奉之至矣，下幸而死，卜葬于此。

    102

    In the sixteenth year of the Hongwu era, Zhang Shicheng captured Pingjiang. In the seventeenth year, the Chancellor issued an order appointing Yang Wanzhe, a military commander, as the Deputy Governor of Jiang-Zhe, to resist Zhang's forces at Jiaxing. The soldiers were not disciplined and raided the residents. Zhaos' residence was taken over by Liu, a military officer, who saw Aiqing's beauty and wanted to force himself upon her. Aiqing spoke sweet words to him, bathed, entered her room, and hanged herself with a silk scarf. Liu rushed to save her, but it was too late. He then wrapped her body in a brocade cushion and buried it under a ginkgo tree in the garden. Soon after, Zhang's forces made peace. Yang, the Deputy Governor, was killed, and his troops scattered. Zhaos journeyed back by sea, landing at Taicang, and returned directly to Jiaxing. The city and its people were no longer as they once were. He returned to his old home, which was now deserted. He only saw rats scurrying on the beams, owls calling from the trees, and moss and green grass covering the steps and courtyard. He searched for his mother and wife, but could not find them. Only the main hall remained standing, and he cleaned it and rested there. The next day, he went out the east gate and came to Hongqiao. He met an old servant on the road, called out to him, and asked for details. The servant told him that his mother had left the house, and his wife had passed away. The servant then led Zhaos to the place where his mother was buried in Bai Zhu Village. Pointing to the pines and cypresses, he said, "These were all planted by Lady Liu." Pointing to the grave mound, he said, "This was all managed by Lady Liu." Grandmother Lady Liu became ill due to missing her son, and Lady Liu cared for her until she died and was buried here.

    103

    娘子身被衰麻，手扶棺榇，亲自负土，号哭墓下。葬之三月，而苗军入城，宅舍被占。有刘万户者，欲以非礼犯之，娘子不从，即遂缢死，就于后圃瘗之矣。 ”赵子大伤感，即至银杏村下发视之，颜貌如生，肌肤不改。赵子抚尸大恸，绝而复苏。乃沐以香汤，被以华服，买棺附葬于母坟之侧，哭之曰：“娘子平日聪明才慧，流辈不及。今虽死矣，岂可混同凡人，使绝音晌。九原有知，愿赐一见。虽显晦殊途，人皆忌惮，而恩情切至，实所不疑。

    103

    The lady, dressed in mourning attire, supported the coffin with her hands, personally carried soil to dig the grave, and wept aloud at the burial site. After the burial for three months, the Miao army entered the city, and her house was occupied. There was a man named Liu, a county magistrate, who intended to violate her with impropriety. The lady refused, and immediately hanged herself, and she was buried in the garden behind the house. S. Zhao was greatly saddened and went to the Silver Apricot Village to view her body. Her appearance was as if she were still alive, and her skin was unchanged. Zhao embraced her body and wept bitterly, fainting and then reviving. He then washed her with fragrant water, dressed her in fine clothing, bought a coffin, and buried her next to her mother's grave. He cried, saying, "Lady, you were always intelligent and wise, outstanding among your peers. Now that you are dead, how can you be mixed with ordinary people, causing the sounds of the world to cease? If there is awareness in the netherworld, I wish to see you once. Even though our paths are different, people fear and respect you, and the bond of affection is profound, and I truly do not doubt it."

    104

    ”于是出则祷于墓下，归则哭于圃中。将及一旬，月晦之夕，赵子独坐中堂，寝不能寐，忽闻暗中哭声，初远渐近，觉其有异，即起祝之曰：“倘是六娘子之灵，何吝一见而叙旧也？ ”即闻言曰：“妾即罗氏也，感君想念，虽在幽冥，实所恻怆，是以今夕与君知闻耳。 ”言讫，如有人行，冉冉而至，五六步许，即可辨其状貌，果爱卿也。淡妆素服，一如其旧，惟以罗巾拥其项。见赵子，施礼毕，泣而歌《沁园春》一阕，其所自制也。词曰：
    　　一别三年，一日空秋，君何不归？记尊嫜抱病，亲供药饵，高茔埋葬，亲曳麻衣。夜卜灯花，晨占鹊喜，雨打梨花昼掩扉。谁知道，把恩情永隔，书信全稀！于戈满目交挥，奈命薄时乖履祸机。向销金帐里，猿惊鹤怨，香罗巾下，玉碎花飞。要学三贞，须拼一死，免被旁人话是非。君相念：算除非画里，重见崔徽！

    Explanation

    104

    After nearly ten days, on the last day of the month, S. Zi sat alone in the main hall, unable to sleep. Suddenly, he heard a faint cry in the darkness, which grew louder and closer. Sensing something unusual, he rose and addressed the sound: "If you are the spirit of Lady Liu, why hesitate to appear and reminisce with me?" Immediately, a voice replied, "I am Lady Liu. I am moved by your remembrance, even though I am in the afterlife. That is why I have come to you tonight." After speaking, a figure appeared, moving slowly toward him. When she was about five or six steps away, her form became clear—indeed, it was Lady Liu. She wore a simple, modest dress, just as she had before, with only a silk scarf around her neck. Seeing S. Zi, she bowed, then wept and sang a self-composed Qinyuan Chun (沁园春) poem. The lyrics read:

    "Three years apart, a day feels like an empty autumn. Why haven't you returned? Remember the time when my husband and I were ill, and I personally prepared medicine. I buried our ancestors, wearing mourning clothes. At night, I divined the auspiciousness of the lamp's flower; in the morning, I sought good omens in the crows' calls. Rain beat on the pear blossoms, and I shut the door during the day. Who would have known that our love would be forever separated, and our letters would become scarce? The world is filled with strife, and fate is cruel. In the golden chamber, the monkeys and cranes are startled; under the fragrant silk handkerchief, jade and flowers shatter. To learn the three virtues, one must be willing to die, to avoid being talked about by others. You think of me: perhaps only in a painting can we meet again, like Cui Hui."

    105

    每歌一句，则悲啼数声，凄惶怨咽，殆不成腔。赵子延之入室，谢其奉母之孝，莹墓之劳，杀身之节，感愧不已。乃收泪而自叙曰：“妾本倡流，素非良族。山鸡野骛，家莫能驯；路柳墙花。人皆可折。惟知倚门而献笑，岂解举案以齐眉。令色巧言，迎新送旧。东家食而酉家宿。久习遗凤；张郎妇而李郎妻，本无定性。幸蒙君子，求为室家，即便弃其旧染之污，革其前事之失。操持井臼，采掇苹蘩。严祀祖之仪，笃奉姑之道。事以礼，葬以礼，无愧于心；歌于斯，哭于斯，未尝窥户。岂料昊天不吊，大患来临！毒手老拳，交争于四境；长枪大剑，耀武于三军。既据李崧之居，又夺韩翃之妇。良人万里，贱妾一身。岂不知偷生之可安，忍辱之耐久。而乃甘心玉略，决意珠沉。若飞蛾之扑灯，似赤子之入井，乃己之自取，非人之不容。

    Explanation

    105

    Every time a song was sung, she would cry and weep several times, her sorrowful and resentful weeping almost rendering the tune unrecognizable. Zhao Ziyuan entered the room and thanked him for his filial piety towards his mother, the labor of clearing and maintaining the grave, and the virtue of sacrificing oneself, deeply moved and grateful. He then collected his tears and began to narrate himself: "I am originally a courtesan, never from a good family. Like wild chickens and wild ducks, no one can tame them at home; like willows by the roadside and flowers on the walls, everyone can pick them. I only know to stand by the door and offer smiles, do not understand to lift the tray to the level of the eyebrows. With flattering looks and clever words, I welcomed the new and sent off the old. Eating at the eastern house and sleeping at the western house, long accustomed to losing the phoenix; wife of Zhang Lang and wife of Li Lang, originally without a fixed nature. Fortunately, I was favored by a gentleman, seeking a proper household, and immediately abandoned the old stains of impurity, reformed the mistakes of the past. Managed the household chores, gathered herbs and flowers. Strictly observed the rituals of ancestor worship, diligently followed the way of respecting the mother-in-law. Treated with propriety, buried with propriety, without shame in one's heart; sang here, cried here, never looked out the window. Who would have thought that heaven was not merciful, a great calamity arrived! Fists of poison, fought in all directions; long spears and large swords, showed off their martial prowess in the three armies. Having taken over Li Song's residence, also took away Han Hong's wife. My husband is far away, I am alone. Who does not know that living by stealth is safe, enduring humiliation for a long time. But willingly accepted the jade plan, determined to sink like a pearl. Like a moth flying into the flame, like a child falling into a well, it was self-inflicted, not due to others' refusal."

    106

    盖所以愧夫为人妻妾而背主弃家，受人爵禄而忘君负国者也。 ”赵子抚慰良久，因问太夫人安在？曰：“尊姑在世无罪，闻已受生于人间矣。 ”赵子曰：“然则，君何以犹堕鬼趣？ ”对曰：“妾之死也，冥司以妾贞烈，即令往无锡宋家。托为男子。妾以与君情缘之重，必欲俟君一见，以叙怀抱，故迟之岁月耳。今既见君矣，明日即往降生也。君如不弃旧情，可往彼家见访，当以一笑为验。 ”遂与赵子入室欢会，款若平生。鸡鸣而起，下阶敛步，复回顾拭泪云：“赵郎珍重，从此永别矣！”因哽咽伫立。夭色渐明，欻然而逝，不复有睹。但空室俏然，寒灯半灭而己。赵子起而促装，径赴无锡，寻宋氏之居而叩焉，则果得一男子，怀妊二十月矣。然自降生之后，至今哭不辍声。赵子具述其事，愿请见之，果一笑而哭止，其家遂名之曰罗生。赵子求为亲属，自此往来馈遗，音问不绝云。

    Explanation

    106

    This is why one should feel ashamed of being a wife or concubine who betrays her master and abandons her family, or of accepting a position and salary from someone but forgetting one's lord and betraying the country. "Zhaizi comforted her for a long time, then asked where the Lady Mother was. She replied, 'My respected mother-in-law was innocent in life and has been reborn in the human world.' Zhaizi said, 'Then why do you still fall into the realm of ghosts?' She answered, 'When I died, the underworld considered me chaste and loyal, and ordered me to be reborn as a man in the Song family of Wuxi. I was entrusted to be a man. Because of our deep emotional bond, I had to wait for you to see you once and to express my feelings, so I delayed it for many years. Now that I have seen you, I will be reborn tomorrow. If you do not abandon our old feelings, you can visit that family and see me; I will smile once as proof.' She then entered the room with Zhaizi and they enjoyed each other's company as if they had known each other all their lives. At dawn, she got up, descended the steps, and took a few steps, then turned back and wiped her tears, saying, 'Take care, Zhao Lang, this is farewell forever!' She choked up and stood still. As the dawn was gradually brightening, she suddenly disappeared and was no longer seen. Only the empty room remained, with the cold lamp half-extinguished. Zhaizi got up and packed hastily, went directly to Wuxi, and found the residence of the Song family and knocked on the door. Indeed, there was a man there who had been pregnant for twenty months. However, since being born, he has been crying non-stop. Zhaizi explained the whole story and wished to see him. Indeed, he smiled once and stopped crying, and his family then named him Luo Sheng. Zhaizi requested to be relatives, and from then on, they exchanged gifts and visits frequently, and their communication never ceased."

    107

    翠翠传
    　　翠翠，姓刘氏，淮安民家女也。生而颖悟，能通诗书，父母不夺其志，就令入学。同学有金氏子者，名定，与之同岁，亦聪明俊雅。诸生戏之曰：“同岁者当为夫妇。 ”二人亦私以此自许。金生赠翠翠诗曰：
    　　十二阑干七宝台，春风到处艳阳开。
    　　东园桃树西园柳，何不移教一处栽？
    　　翠翠和曰：
    　　平生每恨祝英台，凄抱何为不肯开？
    　　我愿东君勤用意，早移花树向阳栽。

    Explanation

    107

    The Biography of Cui Cui

    Cui Cui, surnamed Liu, was a girl from a common family in Huai'an. Born with keen insight, she was able to understand poetry and books. Her parents did not force her to change her aspirations and allowed her to attend school. Among her classmates was a boy named Jin Ding, also from the same family and of the same age, who was also intelligent and elegant. The students would joke, saying, "Those of the same age should be husband and wife." Both of them privately considered this a promise to each other. Jin Ding wrote a poem for Cui Cui:

    Twelve balustrades of seven treasures, the spring breeze opens up the sunny flowers everywhere.
    The peach trees in the eastern garden and the willows in the western garden, why not plant them together in one place?

    Cui Cui responded with a poem:

    In my life, I often lament Zhu Yingtai, why does the sorrowful heart not open up?
    I wish the eastern lord would use his effort diligently, to move the flower tree to the sunny side early.

    108

    已而翠翠年长，不复至学。年及十六，父母为其议亲，辄悲泣不食。以情问之，初不肯言，久乃曰：“必西家金定，妾已许之矣。若不相从，有死而已，誓不登他门也！ ”父母不得已，听焉。然而刘富而金贫，其子虽聪俊，门户甚不敌。及媒氏至其家，果以贫辞，惭愧不敢当。媒氏曰：“刘家小娘子，必欲得金生，父母亦许之矣。若以贫辞，是负其诚志，而失此一好姻缘也。今当语之曰：‘寒家有子，粗知诗礼，贵宅见求，敢不从命。但生自蓬筚，安于贫贱久矣，若责其聘问之仪，婚娶之礼，终恐无从而致。 ’彼以爱女之故，当不较也。 ”其家从之。媒氏复命，父母果曰：“婚姻论财，夷虏之道，吾知择婿而已，不计其它。但彼不足而我有余，我女到彼，必不能堪，莫若赘之入门可矣。 ”媒氏传命再往，其家幸甚。遂涓日结亲，凡币帛之类，羔雁之属，皆女家自备。过门交拜，二人相见，喜可知矣！是夕，翠翠于枕上作《临江仙》一阕赠生曰：

    Explanation

    108

    Later, when Cui Cui grew older, she no longer attended school. When she reached sixteen, her parents arranged for her marriage, and she would always weep and refuse to eat. When asked about her feelings, at first she refused to speak, but after a long time, she said, "I must marry the son of the family to the west; I have already promised him. If you do not agree, I will die. I swear I will never step into another house!" Her parents had no choice but to agree. However, Liu's family was wealthy while Jin's family was poor. His son was intelligent and handsome, but their social status was far inferior. When the matchmaker came to their house, they indeed refused due to poverty, feeling ashamed and dared not accept. The matchmaker said, "They must want to marry Jin's son, and even the parents have agreed. If they refuse due to poverty, it would be a betrayal of their sincere wishes, and they would lose this good match. Now I will tell them this: 'Our humble family has a son who roughly knows poetry and propriety. Your honorable family has proposed, how could we not comply? However, he has lived in poverty for a long time. If you demand the dowry and wedding rituals, they will ultimately be difficult to provide.' They will not care because of their love for their daughter." Their family agreed. The matchmaker then reported back, and the parents indeed said, "Marriage is based on wealth, a practice of the barbarians. We only know of choosing a husband, not considering other factors. But they have nothing while we have much; our daughter would not be able to endure it there. It would be better to let him come and live in our house." The matchmaker relayed the message again, and the family was very pleased. They then set a date for the wedding, and all the gifts and offerings, such as silk and fine fabrics, and the ceremonial gifts of sheep and geese, were all provided by the bride's family. After the wedding, they bowed to each other at the threshold, and the two met, and their joy was evident. That night, Cui Cui wrote a poem titled "Lin Jiang Xian" and gave it to her husband:

    Translation of the Poem "Lin Jiang Xian"

    Lin Jiang Xian

    On the riverbank, the willows sway,
    Beneath the moon, the waves gently play.
    In this moment, our hearts entwined,
    Our vows, like the river, unending.

    The night is calm, the stars above,
    Our love, a light, forever to prove.
    Through joy and sorrow, we'll stand together,
    Our bond, like the river, forever.

    109

    曾向书斋同笔砚，故人今作新人。洞房花烛十分春！汗沾蝴蝶粉，身惹麝香尘。殢雨尤云浑未惯，枕边眉黛羞颦，轻怜痛惜莫嫌频。愿郎从此始，日近日相亲。
    　　邀生继和。生遂次韵曰：
    　　记得书斋同讲习，新人不是他人。扁舟来访武陵春：仙居邻紫府，人世隔红尘。誓海盟山心已许，几番浅笑轻颦，向人犹自语频频。意中无别意，来后有谁亲？
    　　二人相得之乐，虽孔翠之在赤霄，鸳鸯之游绿水，未足喻也。未及一载，张士诚兄弟起兵高邮，尽陷沿淮诸郡，女为其部将李将军者所掳。至正末，士诚辟土益广，跨江南北，奄有浙西，乃通款元朝，愿奉正朔，道途始通，行旅无阻。生于是辞别内、外父母，求访其妻，誓不见则不复还。行至平江，则闻李将军见为绍兴守御；及至绍兴，则又调屯兵安丰矣；复至安丰，则回湖州驻扎矣。

    Explanation

    109

    Once we studied together in the study, sharing the same writing utensils, but the old friend has become a new person. The bridal chamber is filled with the joy of spring! Sweat soaks into the butterfly powder, and the body is stained with musk dust. Indulging in rain and clouds is still unfamiliar, the brows painted like ink on the pillow are shyly frowning, do not tire of the gentle care and deep affection. Wish for you to start from here, growing closer day by day.

    Inviting the poet to continue the theme. The poet then continued in the same meter:

    Remembering the days we studied together in the study, the new person is not someone else. Coming in a small boat to visit the spring of Wu Ling: living in a fairy abode near the Purple Palace, separated from the mundane world. The vows of the sea and mountains have already been made, several times of light smiles and frowns, still speaking to people frequently. There is no other intention in mind, and after coming, who is close to me?

    The joy of their mutual understanding is such that even the peacock in the red sky or the mandarin ducks in the green waters cannot fully express it. Not even a year had passed when Zhang Shicheng and his brothers raised an army in Gaoyou, capturing all the counties along the Huai River, and the woman was taken by General Li, one of his generals. By the end of the Zhi Zheng era, Zhang Shicheng expanded his territory, spanning north and south of the Yangtze River, and controlling western Zhejiang. He then submitted to the Yuan dynasty, vowing to follow its calendar, and the roads became open, allowing travelers to pass without hindrance. The man thus bid farewell to his parents and sought to find his wife, vowing not to return unless he saw her. He traveled to Pingjiang and heard that General Li was now the governor of Shaoxing; upon reaching Shaoxing, he learned that General Li had been transferred to Anfeng to station troops; and upon arriving in Anfeng, he found that General Li had returned to Zhuzhou for garrison duty.

    110

    生来往江淮，备经险阻，星霜屡移，囊囊又竭，然此心终不少懈；草行露宿，丐乞于人，仅而得达湖州。则李将军方贵重用事，威焰赫奕。生伫立门墙，踌躇窥俟，将进而未能，欲言而不敢。阍者怪而问焉。生曰：“仆，淮安人也，丧乱以来，闻有一妹在于贵府，是以不远千里至此，欲求一见耳。 ”阍者曰：“然则汝何姓名？汝妹年貌若干？愿得详言，以审其实。 ”生曰：“仆姓刘，名金定，妹名翠翠，识字能文。当失去之时，年始十七，以岁月计之，今则二十有四矣。 ”阍者闻之，曰：“府中果有刘氏者，淮安人，其齿如汝所言，识字、善为诗，性又通慧，本使宠之专房。汝信不妄，吾将告于内，汝且止此以待。 ”遂奔趋入告。

    Explanation

    110

    Coming and going in the Jianghuai region, he endured many dangers and difficulties, with the stars and frost changing many times, and his resources depleted, yet his heart never wavered slightly. He slept in the grass and dew, begging from people, barely managing to reach Huzhou. At that time, General Li was powerful and influential, with his authority and influence very strong. The protagonist stood by the gate, hesitating and waiting, about to step forward but unable to, wanting to speak but dared not. The gatekeeper was surprised and asked him. The protagonist said, "I am from Huai'an. Since the time of turmoil and chaos, I heard that my sister is in your noble mansion, so I traveled thousands of miles to get here, just to see her once." The gatekeeper asked, "Then what is your name? How old and what does your sister look like? I hope you can explain in detail to verify the truth." The protagonist replied, "My surname is Liu, and my name is Jinding. My sister's name is Cuicui. She can read and write. When she was lost, she was seventeen years old. Calculating by years, she is now twenty-four." The gatekeeper heard this and said, "There is indeed a Liu lady in the mansion, a woman from Huai'an, whose age matches what you said. She can read and write, is good at poetry, and is intelligent and wise. The master cherishes her deeply. You are not lying. I will inform inside. Please wait here." He then hurriedly went inside to report.

    111

    须臾，复出，领生入见。将军坐于厅上，生再拜而起，具述厥由。将军，武人也，信之不疑，即命内竖告于翠翠曰：“汝兄自乡中来此，当出见之。”翠翠承命而出，以兄妹之礼见于厅前，动问父母外，不能措一辞，但相对悲咽而已。将军曰：“汝既远来，道途跋涉，心力疲困，可且于吾门下休息，吾当徐为之所。 ”即出新衣一袭，令服之，并以帷帐衾席之属设于门西小斋，令生处焉。翌日，谓生曰：“汝妹能识字，汝亦通书否？”生曰：“仆在乡中，以儒为业，以书为本，凡经史子集，涉猎尽矣，盖素所习也，又何疑焉？ ”将军喜曰：“吾自少失学，乘乱崛起。方响用于时，趋从者众，宾客盈门，无人延款，书启堆案，无人裁答。汝便处吾门下，足充一记室矣。 ”

    Explanation

    111

    In a short while, the general emerged again and led the student into an audience. The general was seated on the dais, and the student bowed twice and stood up, explaining the matter in detail. The general, a soldier, believed him without doubt and immediately ordered a servant to inform Cui Cui: "Your brother has come from the countryside; you should meet him." Cui Cui, upon receiving the order, came out and greeted him with the etiquette of brother and sister in front of the hall. She asked about the parents and could not utter a word, but they wept together. The general said, "Since you have traveled far and endured the hardships of the journey, you must be mentally and physically exhausted. You may rest under my roof for now, and I will arrange for you later." He then brought out a new set of clothes and had him put it on, and arranged bedding and furnishings in a small study on the west side of the gate, where the student was to stay. The next day, the general told the student, "Your sister can read; do you also know books?" The student replied, "In the countryside, I have been engaged in scholarship, taking books as my foundation. I have read extensively through the classics, histories, philosophy, and literature, which I have studied habitually. What reason is there to doubt me?" The general was pleased and said, "Since my youth, I lost my education and rose to prominence amidst chaos. I am now in demand and have many followers, with guests filling my door. There is no one to entertain them, and my letters and documents pile up, with no one to respond to them. You can serve under my roof and be sufficient to act as a secretary."

    112

    生，聪敏者也，性既温和，才又秀发，处于其门，益自检束，承上接下，咸得其欢，代书回简，曲尽其意。将军大以为得人，待之甚厚。然生本为求妻而来，自厅前一见之后，不可再得，闺阁深邃，内外隔绝，但欲一达其意，而终无便可乘。荏苒数月，时及授衣，西风夕起，白露为霜，独处空斋，终夜不寐，乃成一诗曰：
    　　好花移入玉阑干，春色无缘得再看。
    　　乐处岂知愁处苦，别时虽易见时难。
    　　何年塞上重归马？此夜庭中独舞鸾。
    　　雾阁云窗深几许？可怜辜负月团圆。
    　　诗成，书于片纸，拆布裘之领而缝之，以百钱纳于小竖，而告曰：“天气已寒，吾衣甚薄，乞挤入付吾妹，令浣濯而缝纫之，将以御寒耳。 ”小竖如言持入。翠翠解其意，拆衣而诗见，大加伤感，吞声而泣，别为一诗，亦缝于内，以付生。诗曰：

    Explanation

    112

    The youth, being clever and intelligent, had a gentle nature and a talent that was outstanding. When he lived in the household, he disciplined himself even more, treating those above and below him with respect and gaining their favor. He wrote letters and replies that fully conveyed his thoughts. The general greatly thought he had found a capable person and treated him very well. However, the youth had originally come to seek a wife. After seeing her once before the hall, he could not see her again. The inner chambers were deep and secluded, with a clear separation between the inside and outside. He only wanted to convey his feelings, but there was no opportunity to do so. Months passed, and it was time for the autumn clothes to be given out. The west wind blew at dusk, and the white dew turned to frost. He stayed alone in an empty room, unable to sleep all night, and composed a poem:

    "Beautiful flowers were moved into the jade railings, and the spring scenery could no longer be seen.
    In moments of joy, one does not know the pain in moments of sorrow; it is easy to part but hard to meet again.
    When will the horse return from the frontier? This night, the phoenix dances alone in the courtyard.
    How deep are the misty halls and clouded windows? It is pitiful to miss the full moon."

    After finishing the poem, he wrote it on a small piece of paper, tore the lining of his fur coat, and sewed it in. He gave a hundred coins to a young servant and instructed him, "The weather is already cold, and my clothes are very thin. Please give this to my sister, have her wash and sew it, so I can use it to keep warm." The young servant took the message as instructed and delivered it to the sister. The sister understood his meaning, tore open the coat, and found the poem. She was deeply moved, and with tears in her eyes, she composed another poem, also sewing it inside the coat to give to the youth. The poem read:

    113

    一自乡关动战锋，旧愁新恨几重重！
    　　肠虽已断情难断，生不相从死亦从。
    　　长使德言藏破镜，终教子建赋游龙。
    　　绿珠碧玉心中事，今日谁知也到侬！
    　　生得诗，知其以死许之，无复致望，愈加抑郁，遂感沉痼。翠翠请于将军，始得一至床前问候，而生病已亟矣。翠翠以臂扶生而起，生引首侧视，凝泪满眶，长吁一声，奄然命尽。将军怜之，葬于道场山麓。翠翠送殡而归，是夜得疾，不复饮药，展转衾席，将及两月。一旦，告于将军曰：“妾弃家相从，已得八载。流离外境，举目无亲，止有一兄，今又死矣。妾病必不起，乞埋骨兄侧，黄泉之下，庶有依托，免于他乡作孤魂也。 ”言尽而卒。将军不违其志，竟附葬于生之坟左，宛然东西二丘焉。

    Explanation

    113

    Since the war began at the hometown frontier, old sorrows and new grievances piled upon each other!
    Though the heart is broken, the feelings are hard to sever; if not together in life, then together in death.
    She long kept her broken mirror, as did Lady Xie, and finally Cao Zhi composed a poem about a dragon.
    The inner feelings of Green Pearl and Jade, who today knows that this has come to me?
    He received a poem, knowing she had promised to die for him, no longer holding out hope, he became even more depressed, eventually falling ill. Cui Cui requested the general, and only then was she allowed to visit his bedside, but his illness had already worsened. Cui Cui supported him with her arm and helped him sit up; he turned his head and looked sideways, tears filling his eyes, and sighed deeply once, then passed away. The general pitied him and buried him at the foot of Daochang Mountain. Cui Cui returned home after the funeral, that night she fell ill, stopped taking medicine, and lay restless in her bed for nearly two months. One day, she told the general, "I left my family to follow him, and it has been eight years. Wandering in foreign lands, I have no relatives, only one brother, who is now dead. My illness is sure to take my life, I ask to be buried beside my brother, in the underworld, I might find some solace, and avoid being a lonely spirit in a foreign land." She spoke her last words and then died. The general did not go against her wish and finally buried her beside his grave, forming two mounds, east and west.

    114

    洪武初，张氏既灭，翠翠家有一旧仆，以商贩为业，路经湖州，过道场山下，见朱门华屋，槐柳掩映，翠翠与金生方凭肩而立。遽呼之入，访问父母存殁，及乡井旧事。仆曰：“娘子与郎安得在此？”翠翠曰：“始因兵乱，我为李将军所掳，郎君远来寻访，将军不阻，以我归焉，因遂侨居于此耳。 ”仆曰：“予今还淮安，娘子可修一书以报父母也。 ”翠翠留之宿，饭吴兴之香糯，羹苕溪之鲜鲫，以乌程酒出饮之。明旦，遂修启以上父母曰：

    Explanation

    114

    In the early years of the Hongwu reign, after the Zhang family was destroyed, Cui Cui had an old servant who made a living by trading. He passed by Huzhou and went down Daochang Mountain, where he saw a grand house with willows and locust trees, and Cui Cui and Jin Sheng were standing side by side. He called her in abruptly and inquired about the survival of her parents and old stories from her hometown. The servant asked, "How could the lady and the gentleman be here?" Cui Cui explained, "At first because of the turmoil of war, I was captured by General Li. The gentleman came to find me, and the general did not obstruct, allowing me to return. So, I have been living temporarily in this place." The servant said, "I am returning to Huai'an now. The lady can write a letter to report to her parents." Cui Cui kept him for the night and served him fragrant glutinous rice from Wu Xing, a soup made of fresh carp from the Tiao River, and wine from Wu Cheng to drink. The next morning, she wrote a letter to report to her parents, saying:

    115

    伏以父生母育，难酬罔极之恩；夫唱妇随，夙着三从之义。在人伦而已定，何时事之多艰！ ；曩者汉日将颓，楚氛甚恶，倒持太阿之柄，擅弄潢池之兵。豕长蛇，互相吞并；雄蜂雌蝶，各自逃生。不能玉碎于乱离，乃至瓦全于仓卒。驱驰战马，随逐征鞍。望高天而八翼莫飞，思故国而三魂屡散。良辰易迈，伤青鸾之伴木鸡；怨偶为仇，惧乌鸦之打丹凤。虽应酬而为乐，终感激而生悲。夜月杜鹃之啼，春风蝴蝶之梦。时移事往，苦尽甘来。今则杨素览镜而归妻，王敦开合而放妓，蓬岛践当时之约，潇湘有故人之逢。

    Explanation

    115

    Bow to the reciprocal care of father and mother, the boundless kindness of which is hard to repay; the husband leads and the wife follows, embodying the ancient virtues of the Three Obediences. These roles are already established in human relationships, yet how many times have things been difficult! In the past, the Han dynasty was on the verge of collapse, and the atmosphere of Chu was extremely hostile. Power was misused, like holding a legendary sword upside down, and unauthorized military actions were carried out, akin to playing with a small pond's waters. Chaotic and destructive forces, like pigs and snakes, devoured each other; different types of people, like male bees and female butterflies, tried to save themselves. Unable to die honorably in chaos, they survived pragmatically in a hasty situation. Driven by war horses, they fled on battle saddles. Looking to the high heavens, they could not fly with eight wings; longing for their homeland, their spirits scattered. Good times easily pass, lamenting the loss of noble companions; a once-loving couple became enemies, fearing harm to a noble entity. Though they socialized for pleasure, ultimately, they felt gratitude and sorrow. The cuckoo's cry under the moonlight, the fleeting dreams of spring butterflies. Times change and events pass, after suffering comes sweetness. Now, Yang Su looks into a mirror and reunites with his wife, Wang Dun opens a door and releases his concubines, fulfilling a promise on Penglai Island, and meeting an old friend by the Xiao and Xiang rivers.

    116

    自怜赋命之屯，不恨寻春之晚。章台之柳，虽已折于他人；玄都之花，尚不改于前度。将谓瓶沉而簪折，岂期壁返而珠还。殆同玉萧女两世姻缘，难比红拂妓一时配合。天与其便，事非偶然。煎鸾胶而续断弦，重谐缱绻；托鱼腹而传尺素，谨致丁宁。未奉甘旨，先此申复。父母得之，甚喜。其父即赁舟与仆自淮徂浙，径奔吴兴。至道场山下畴昔留宿之处，则荒烟野草，狐兔之迹交道，前所见屋宇，乃东西两坟耳。方疑访间，适有野僧扶锡而过，叩而问焉。则曰：“此故李将军所葬金生与翠娘之坟耳，岂有人居乎？ ”大惊。取其书而视之，则白纸一幅也。

    Explanation

    116

    Grieving over one's own fate, yet not resenting the late arrival of spring. The willows on Changtai, though broken by others; the flowers in Xuandu, still unchanged from before. One might have thought the vase would sink and the hairpin would break, but who would have expected the wall to return and the pearl to be restored. It is akin to the two-life marriage of Yu Xiao Nu, hard to compare with the one-time union of Hong Fu. Heaven has granted convenience, and the matter is not by chance. Melting phoenix glue to mend the broken strings, to rekindle the tender bond; entrusting a letter to a fish's belly, carefully conveying the message. Before fulfilling the duty to serve one's parents, I first express this response. The parents, upon receiving it, were very pleased. The father immediately rented a boat and traveled with the servant from Huai to Zhejiang, directly heading to Wuxing. Just as they were wondering and looking around, a wild monk passed by with his staff, and they asked him.     117

    时李将军为国朝所戮，无从诘问其详。父哭于坟下曰：“汝以书赚我，令我千里至此，本欲与我一见也。今我至此，而汝藏踪秘迹，匿影潜形。我与汝，生为父子，死何间焉？妆如有灵，毋齐一见，以释我疑虑也。 ”是夜，宿于坟。以三更后，翠翠与金生拜跪于前，悲号宛转。父泣而抚问之，乃具述其始末曰：“往者祸起萧墙，兵兴属郡。不能效窦氏女之烈，乃致为沙咤利之躯。忍耻偷生，离乡去国。恨以惠兰之弱质，配兹驵侩之下材。惟知夺石家买笑之姬，岂暇怜息国不言之妇。叫九阍而无路，度一日而三秋。

    117

    At the time, General Li was executed by the state, and there was no way to inquire into the details. The father wept at the grave and said, "You tricked me with a letter, causing me to travel thousands of miles to be here, originally wishing to meet you once. Now that I am here, and you hide your tracks, conceal your shadow and form. You and I, living as father and son, what difference does death make? If you have any spirit, do not hide from me, to dispel my doubts." That night, he stayed at the grave. After the third watch, Cuicui and Jinsheng knelt before him, weeping and wailing. The father wept and comforted them, and they then recounted the beginning and end of their story: "In the past, trouble arose within the family, and military actions were taken in the counties. Unable to emulate the bravery of the Dou family's daughter, thus becoming the body of Shazhali. Enduring shame to survive, leaving home and country. Hating to match the delicate nature of a noble lady with the lowly skills of a commoner. Only knowing how to take away the laughing girl from the Shi family, how could they spare time to pity the silent woman of Xi. Calling at the nine gates but finding no way, a day feels like three autumns."

    118

    良人不弃旧恩，特勤远访，托兄妹之名，而仅获一见，隔伉俪之情，而终遂不通。彼感疾而先殂，妾含冤而继殒。欲求袝葬，幸得同归。大略如斯，微言莫尽。 ”父曰：“我之来此，本欲取汝还家，以奉我耳。今汝已矣，将取汝骨迁于先垄，亦不虚行一遭也。 ”复泣而言曰：“妾生而不幸，不得视膳庭闱；殁且无缘，不得首丘茔垄。然而地道尚静，神理宜安，若更迁移，反成劳扰。况溪山秀丽，草木荣华，既已安焉，非所愿也。”因抱持其父而大哭。父遂惊觉，乃一梦也。明日，以牲酒奠于坟下，与仆返棹而归。

    118

    The husband did not abandon his old kindness, and the special envoy made a distant visit, pretending to be siblings, and only managed to meet once, separated by marital affection, and ultimately unable to communicate. He fell ill and died first, and I, feeling wronged, died afterward. I desired a joint burial and was fortunate enough to be buried together. Roughly like this, subtle words cannot fully express the situation. "The father said, 'I came here originally intending to take you back home to serve me. Now that you are gone, I will move your bones to the family tomb, and this journey will not be in vain.' He wept again and said, 'I was unfortunate in life, unable to see the court and family; even in death, I am without connection, unable to return to the family tomb. However, the earth's nature is still calm, and the divine order should be at peace. If we were to move again, it would only cause more trouble. Moreover, the surroundings are beautiful, with flourishing vegetation. Having already found peace here, it is not what I desire.' He then embraced his father and wept greatly. The father woke up, realizing it was a dream. The next day, he offered sacrifices at the grave and returned with the servant by boat."

    119

    至今过者指为金、翠墓云。
    　　剪灯新话卷四
    　　龙堂灵会录
    　　吴江有龙王堂，堂，盖庙也，所以奉事香火，故谓之堂。或以为右崖陡出，若塘岸焉，故又谓之龙王塘。其地左吴淞而右太湖，风涛险恶，众水听汇，过者必致敬于庙庭而后行，夙着灵异，具载于范石湖所编《吴郡志》。元统间，闻生子述者，以歌诗鸣于吴下。因过其处，适值龙挂，乃白龙也，毊鬣下垂，如一玉住，鳞甲照耀，如明镜数百片；转侧于乌云之内，良久而没。子述自以为平生奇观，莫之能及。雨止，登庙，周览既毕，乃题古风一章于庑下曰：
