    To this day, those who pass by point to it as the tomb of Jin and Cui.

    Records of the Spiritual Gathering at the Dragon Hall

    In Wujiang, there is a Dragon King Hall. The hall, it is a temple, dedicated to serving incense and fire, hence it is called a hall. Some say the right cliff protrudes steeply, like a pond bank, therefore it is also called Dragon King Pond. The place is on the left of Wusong and on the right of Taihu Lake. The wind and waves are dangerous, and all waters converge. Those who pass by must pay respect at the temple before proceeding. Long known for its spiritual marvels, all recorded in Fan Shihu's compilation of Wu County Gazetteer. During the Yuantong era, there was a man named Zishu who became famous for his songs and poems in Wu. Because he passed by the place, he just happened to encounter a dragon hanging. It was a white dragon, with long hair hanging down, like a piece of jade. Its scales were shining brightly, like hundreds of pieces of bright mirrors. Turning and moving within dark clouds, for a long time before disappearing. Zishu thought it was the most extraordinary sight of his life, no one could match it. When the rain stopped, he climbed the temple, after thoroughly viewing everything. He then wrote a chapter of ancient style poetry under the eaves, saying:

    (Note: The actual content of the poem is not provided in the source text, so it is omitted here.)

    120

    龙王之堂龙作主，栋宇青红照江渚，岁时奉事孰敢违，求晴得晴雨得雨。平生好奇无与侔，访水寻山遍吴楚，扁舟一叶过垂虹，濯足沧浪浣尘土。神龙有心慰劳苦，变化凤云快观睹，毊尾蜿蜒玉柱垂，鳞甲光芒银镜舞。村中稽首朝翁姥，船上燃香拜商贾，共说神龙素有灵，降福除灾敢轻侮！我登龙堂共龙语，至诚感格龙应许。汲挽湖波作酒浆，采掇江花当肴脯。大字淋漓写庭户，过者惊疑居者怒。世间不识谪仙人，笑别神龙指归路。

    Explanation

    120

    The Dragon King's Hall is ruled by dragons, with its colorful structures reflecting on the riverbanks. Who dares to disobey the annual rites and offerings? Prayers for clear skies or rain are answered. Throughout my life, I have been curious and unique, traveling extensively through water and mountains in the regions of Wu and Chu. I passed under the Rainbow Bridge in a small boat and washed my feet in the Canglang River to cleanse the dust. The dragon has compassion and responds to my efforts, transforming clouds and winds into spectacular sights. Its tail winds around like a jade pillar, and its scales and armor shine like silver mirrors. Villagers bow respectfully to the dragon king, and people on boats burn incense to worship merchants. Everyone says the dragon has always been divine, bringing blessings and removing disasters, and no one dares to disrespect it. I ascended the dragon hall and conversed with the dragon, and my sincere devotion moved the dragon to grant my requests. It drew lake waves to make wine and soup and gathered river flowers as food. Large, wet characters were written on the hall, surprising passersby and angering residents. People in the world do not recognize the exiled immortal, and I laughed goodbye to the dragon, pointing out the way home.

    121

    题毕，回舟，卧于蓬下。忽有鱼头鬼身者，自庙而来，施礼于前曰：“龙王奉邀。 ”子述曰：“龙玉处于水府，贱子游于尘世，风马牛之不相及也。虽有严命，何以能至！ ”鱼头者曰：“君毋苦，但请瞑目，少顷即当至矣。 ”子述如言，但闻风水声，久之，惭止，开目，则见殿宇峥嵘，仪卫森列，寒光逼人，不可睇视，真所谓水晶宫也。王闻其至，冠眼剑佩而出，延之上阶，致谢曰：“日间蒙惠高作，伺旨既佳，笔势又妙，庙庭得此，光彩倍增。是以屈君至此，欲得奉酬。 ”坐未定，阍者传言客至，王遽出门迎接。见有三人同入，其一高冠巨履，威仪简重；其一乌帽青裘，风度潇洒；其—则葛巾野服而已。分次而坐。王谓子迷曰：“君不识三客乎？乃越范相国，晋张使君，唐陆处士耳，世所渭吴地三高是也。

    Explanation

    121

    After completing his task, he returned to the boat and lay down under the awning. Suddenly, a figure with a fish head and a ghostly body appeared from the temple, bowed before him, and said, "The Dragon King invites you." Zi Shu replied, "The Dragon King resides in the water realm, while I wander in the mortal world; as different as wind and cattle, how could we possibly meet? Even with a strict command, how could I possibly reach there?" The fish-headed figure said, "Please do not worry. Just close your eyes, and in a moment, you will arrive." Following his instructions, Zi Shu only heard the sound of wind and water. After a while, the sound gradually stopped. Opening his eyes, he saw a grand palace with guards arrayed, and the cold light was so intense that it was difficult to look at. It was truly a crystal palace. Upon hearing that Zi Shu had arrived, the Dragon King, wearing a crown, sword, and jade ornaments, came out and invited him up the steps, expressing thanks by saying, "During the day, you honored us with your excellent work. The taste is excellent, and the brushwork is wonderful. The temple gains great luster from this. That is why I have humbly invited you here, wanting to offer a return favor." They had not yet sat down when the gatekeeper announced that guests had arrived. The Dragon King hurriedly went out to greet them. Three people entered together: one wore a tall hat and large shoes, with a dignified and solemn demeanor; one wore a black hat and a green fur coat, with a graceful and carefree bearing; and the third wore a simple headband and a rustic robe. They sat in order. The Dragon King said to Zi Shu, "Do you not recognize these three guests? They are the former Prime Minister of Yue, the former Envoy of Jin, and the former Scholar of Tang, known as the Three Highs of Wu."

    122

    ”王对三客言子述题诗之事，俱各传观，称赞不已。王曰：“诗人远临，贵客偕至，赏心乐事，不期而同。 ”即命左右设宴于中堂，凡铺陈之物，饮馔之味，皆非人世所有。酒至，方欲饮，阍者奔入曰：“吴大夫伍君在门。”王急起迎之。既入，范相国犹据首席，不能谦避。伍君勃然变色而谓王曰：“此地乃吴国之境，王乃吴地之神，吾乃吴国之忠臣，彼乃吴国之仇人也。吴俗无知，妄以三高为目，立亭馆以奉之。王又延之入室，置之上座，曩日吞吴之恨，宁忍忘之耶？ ”即数范相国：“汝有三大罪，而人罔知，故千载之下，得以欺世而盗名。吾今为汝一白之，使大奸无所容，大恶不得隐矣！ ”相国默然，请闻其说。乃曰：“昔勾践志于复仇，卧薪尝胆，十年生聚，十年教训。以此战伐，孰能御之？何至假负薪之女，为诲淫之事，出此鄙计，不以为惭。吴既已亡，又不能除去尤物，反与共载而去。

    Explanation

    122

    The king spoke to the three guests about the matter of the poem inscribed on the subject. They all passed it around to view and praised it without end. The king said, "The poet has come from afar, and the esteemed guests have arrived together, finding enjoyment and delight in this unexpected coincidence." He immediately ordered his attendants to set up a banquet in the central hall. All the items displayed and the flavors of the food and drink were not of this world. When the wine arrived, he was just about to drink when the gatekeeper rushed in and said, "The Grand Master Wu of Wu is at the door." The king hurriedly got up to welcome him. Once inside, the Prime Minister Fan still occupied the chief seat and could not be modest and yield. Grand Master Wu suddenly changed color and said to the king, "This place is the territory of Wu, you are the god of Wu, I am a loyal minister of Wu, and he is an enemy of Wu. The customs of Wu are ignorant, falsely calling the Three Highs by their titles and building pavilions to honor them. You also invited him into the room and placed him in the upper seat. Can you still forget the hatred of the past when Wu was swallowed?" He then accused the Prime Minister Fan, saying, "You have three great crimes, which people do not know, so for a thousand years, you have been able to deceive the world and steal a reputation. I will now expose you once, so that great evil will have no place to hide!" The Prime Minister remained silent and asked to hear the explanation. Grand Master Wu continued, "In the past, King Goujian of Yue was determined to avenge himself, sleeping on firewood and tasting gall, gathering strength for ten years, and training for ten years. With this, who could resist him in battle? How could he go so far as to use a woman carrying firewood, to teach lewdness, come up with this lowly plan, and not be ashamed? After Wu had already perished, he could not even remove the precious object, but instead took it along with him."

    123

    昔太公蒙面以斩妲己，高颎违令而诛丽华，以此方之，孰得孰失？是谋国之不臧也。既已灭吴，以勾践为人，长颈鸟喙，可与共患难，不可与同逸乐，浮海而去，以书遗大夫种云：‘蜚鸟尽，良弓藏；狡兔死，走狗烹，子可以去矣。 ’夫自不能事君，又诱其臣与之偕去，令其主孤立于上，国空无人，于心安乎？昔鲍叔之荐管仲，萧何之追韩信，以此方之，轨是孰非？是事君之不忠也。既已去位，本求高蹈。何乃聚敛积实。耕于海滨，父子力作，以营千金，屡散而复积，此欲何为哉？昔鲁仲连辞金而不受，张于房辟谷而远引，以此方之，孰贤孰愚？是持身之不廉也。负此三大罪，安得居吾之上乎？ ”相国面色如土，不敢出声。久之，乃曰：“子之罪我则然矣！愿闻子之所事。”伍君曰：“吾以家族之不幸。遍游诸国，不避艰险，终能用吴以复父兄之仇，又能为夫盖复父之仇，则孝为有余矣。

    Explanation

    123

    In ancient times, Jiang Ziya covered his face to execute Lady Xi Shi, and Gao Jing disobeyed orders to kill Li Hua. Comparing these two actions, which is more justifiable? This is detrimental to the state. After having conquered Wu, considering Gou Jian's character—long-necked and bird-like, capable of sharing hardships but not enjoying ease—he fled by sea, leaving a letter to Fan Li saying, "When the birds are all caught, the good bow is put away; when the rabbits are all killed, the hunting dogs are cooked. You may leave now." By his own inability to serve his master and by enticing his ministers to follow him away, he left his master isolated at the top, with the state left without leaders. How could he feel at peace with such actions? In contrast, Bao Shu recommended Guan Zhong, and Xiao He pursued Han Xin. Comparing these actions, which is more virtuous? This is disloyalty to his master. After leaving his position, he sought to rise above ordinary life. Why did he then accumulate wealth? He farmed by the sea, working tirelessly with his father, amassing a fortune, only to scatter and gather it again. What was his purpose? In contrast, Lu Zhonglian refused gold and Zhang Yu Fang practiced fasting and retreated. Comparing these actions, who is wiser and who is foolish? This is unscrupulous conduct. Bearing these three great sins, how can he be above me? The chancellor's face turned pale, and he dared not speak. After a long time, he said, "You have accused me, but I wish to hear what you are doing." Wu Jun replied, "Because of the misfortune of my family, I traversed many states, without avoiding hardships and dangers. Finally, using Wu, I avenged my father and brothers, and also avenged my father-in-law. There is more than enough filial piety."

    Serving Wu until death without leaving, fulfilling one's aspirations for the ruler, even though suffering the cruel fate of execution by the sword, never uttering any words of complaint—such loyalty is more than sufficient. The ruler did not continue to employ me, and even until my death, I was able to foresee the disaster that befell Wu and consider the worries after death—such foresight is more than sufficient. If I were still alive, then the low point of seeking refuge in Kuaiji could be turned around, and the battle of Zui Li could not be won through deceit; the rulers and ministers of Yue would be too busy to have time for morning meals, and how could they achieve success in our country? I have often argued that the fall of Wu did not lie in the advancement of Xi Shi, but in my own being slandered; the rise of Yue did not lie in the use of Zong and Li, but in my own being killed. If I had not died, then Xi Shi, the woman from Zhu Luo, would have been sufficient for the enjoyment of the harem; the splendor of the palace would have been sufficient to boast of in the front hall; the Terrace of Gusu would not have been accessible to deer; the Temple of Virtue would not have quickly become overgrown with millet and sorghum! Only by harming my own integrity and injuring my own supporters did I allow my enemies to take advantage of the opportunity and my rival state to exploit the gap, which happened by chance. Was this the achievement of replacing the state or the strategy for the state? The chancellor was at a loss for words and thus vacated his position to yield to me.     The Legal Record of the Supreme Void
    Feng Da Yi, whose given name was Qi, was a madman from Wu and Chu. He relied on his talent and looked down on others, did not believe in ghosts and spirits, and would confront any strange phenomena that depended on grass and wood, that shocked the world and startled the common people. He would raise his arm to face them, and upon arrival, he would bully and humiliate them until he had destroyed their shrines or sunk their images. He went forward boldly without regard for consequences, and thus people also praised him for his courage and spirit.
    During the Ding Chou year of the Yuan Dynasty, he was living as an immigrant in an old nearby village near the eastern gate of Shangcai. At that time, it was after a war and destruction, and the place was desolate with no one living there, covered in yellow sand and white bones. Before he arrived, the slanting sun was setting in the west, and gloomy clouds were rising all around. There was no inn, so where could he find a place to rest? There was an ancient pine forest by the road, so he entered and leaned against a tree for a brief rest. Owls and night birds were calling from in front, and foxes and wolves were howling behind. Soon, a group of crows landed in a circle, some standing on one foot and crying, others flapping their wings and dancing, making strange and unpleasant sounds, forming a circle in formation. There were also eight or nine dead bodies lying stiffly on either side. A cold wind was blowing softly, and rain was falling suddenly. A loud thunderclap, and the dead bodies rose up in a circle, seeing Feng Da Yi under the tree, they eagerly rushed to follow him.

    129

    大异急攀缘上树以避之，群尸环绕其下，或啸或詈，或坐或立，相与大言曰：“今夜必取此人！不然，吾属将有咎”已而云收雨止，月光穿漏，见一夜叉自远而至，头有二角，举体青色，大呼阔步，径至林下，以手撮死尸，摘其头而食之，如啖瓜之状；食讫，饱卧，鼾睡之声动地。大异度不可久留，乘其熟寐，下树迸逸，行不百步，则夜叉已在后矣，舍命而奔，几为所及。遇一废寺，急入投之，东西廊皆倾倒，惟殴上有佛像一躯，其状甚伟。见佛背有一穴，大异计穷，窜身入穴，潜于腹中，自渭得所托，可无虞矣。

    Explanation

    129

    "Da Yi climbed the tree hastily to avoid them, as a group of corpses surrounded him below, some howling, some cursing, some sitting, some standing. Together, they loudly declared, 'We will definitely take this person tonight! Otherwise, we will be in trouble.' After a while, the clouds dispersed and the rain stopped, and the moonlight shone through. He saw a night demon come from afar, with two horns on its head and its entire body blue. It shouted loudly and took large steps, directly to the forest below, picking up the corpses with his hands and removing their heads to eat them, like eating a melon. After eating, it lay full, and the sound of its snoring shook the ground. Da Yi realized he could not stay long, taking advantage of the demon's deep sleep, he jumped down the tree and fled. Not even a hundred steps, and the night demon was already behind him. He raced for his life, nearly caught up with him. He came across an abandoned temple and rushed in to take refuge. The east and west corridors were all collapsed, only the upper part of the hall had one Buddha statue. He saw a hole in the back of the Buddha, ran out of options, and crept into the hole, hiding inside the Buddha's body. Feeling he had found a safe place, he was no longer in danger."

    忽闻佛像鼓腹而笑曰：“彼求之而不得，吾不求而自至，今夜好顿点心，不用食斋也！ ”即振迅而起，其行甚重，将十步许，为门限所碍。蹴然仆地，土木狼籍，胎骨糜碎矣。大异得出，犹太言曰：“胡鬼弄汝公，反自掇其祸矣！”即出寺而行。遥望野中，灯烛荧煌，诸人揖让而坐。喜甚，弛往赴之。及至，则皆无头者也，有头者则无一臂，或缺一足。大异不顾而走。诸鬼怒曰：“吾辈方此酣畅，此人大胆，敢来冲突！正当执之以为脯胾耳。 ”即踉蹡哮吼，或搏牛粪而掷，或攫人骨而投，无头者则提头以趁之。

    130

    Suddenly, a Buddha statue laughed with its belly and said, "Those who seek it cannot attain it, but what is not sought comes to me naturally. Tonight is a good time for a snack, no need to fast!" It then rose quickly, moving with great weight, and took about ten steps before being hindered by the threshold. Looking far into the wilderness, he saw lights flickering, and people were bowing and sitting. He was very happy and hurried to join them. Upon arrival, he found that they were all headless, and those with heads had no arms or were missing a foot. Great Yi turned and ran away.     前阻一永，大异乱流而渡，诸鬼至永。则不敢越。蓦及半里，大异回顾，犹闻喧哗之声，靡靡不已。须臾，月堕，不辨蹊径，失足坠一坑中，其深无底，乃鬼谷也。寒沙瞇目，阴气彻骨，群鬼萃焉。有赤发而双角者，绿毛而两翼者，鸟喙而獠牙者，牛头而兽面者，皆身如蓝靛，口吐火焰，见大异至，相贺曰：“仇人至矣！ ”即以铁纽系其颈，皮繂拴其腰，驱至鬼王之座下，告曰：“此即在世不信鬼神，凌辱吾徒之狂土也。 ”鬼玉怒责之曰：“汝具五体而有知识。岂不闻鬼神之德其盛矣乎？孔子圣人也，犹曰敬而远之。

    131

    A river named Yong blocked the way ahead, and a strange person crossed the turbulent waters. Various ghosts arrived at the River Yong and dared not cross. Suddenly, the strange person reached halfway and looked back, still hearing the sound of noise continuing without stopping. In a moment, the moon set, and the path became unclear. The strange person lost his footing and fell into a bottomless pit, which was identified as the Ghost Valley. The cold sand blinded his eyes, and the chilling energy penetrated to the bone. A multitude of ghosts gathered there. There were those with red hair and two horns, those with green fur and two wings, those with a bird's beak and fangs, and those with a cow's head and a beast's face. All had bodies like indigo and spewed flames from their mouths. Seeing the strange person arrive, they greeted each other saying, "The enemy has arrived!" They immediately used an iron chain to bind his neck and a leather rope to tie his waist, driving him to the seat of the Ghost King to report, saying, "This is the person in the world who disbelieved in ghosts and spirits and insulted our followers." The Ghost Jade angrily scolded him, saying, "You have five limbs and knowledge. Do you not know that the virtue of ghosts and spirits is great? Confucius is a sage, and still said to revere and keep a distance."

    132

    大《易》所谓载鬼一车，《小雅》听谓为鬼为蜮。他如《左传》所纪，晋景之梦，伯有之事，皆是物也。汝为河人，犹言其无？吾受汝侮久矣！今幸相遇，吾乌得而甘心焉。 ”即命众鬼卸其冠裳，加以棰楚，流血淋漓，求死不得。鬼王乃谓之曰：“汝欲调泥成酱乎？汝欲身长三丈乎？ ”大异念泥岂可为酱，因愿身长三丈。众鬼即捽之于石床之上，如搓粉之状，众手反复而按摩之，不觉渐长，已而扶起，果三丈矣，袅袅如竹竿焉。众笑辱之，呼为长竿怪。

    Explanation

    132

    The Yijing speaks of a cart full of ghosts, and the Xiao Ya mentions acting like ghosts or spirits. Similarly, the Zuo Zhuan records events such as the dream of Duke Jing of Jin and the story of Bo You—all of these are related to such phenomena. You, as a river person, still dare to deny their existence? I have suffered your insults for a long time! Now that we have met, how can I not feel satisfied? He immediately ordered the ghosts to remove his clothes and beat him severely, causing him to bleed profusely and unable to die. The ghost king then said to him, "Do you want to turn mud into paste? Or do you want to grow to three zhang in height?" He was greatly surprised and thought that mud could not be turned into paste, so he wished to grow to three zhang in height. The ghosts then dragged him onto a stone bed and handled him like dough, massaging him repeatedly with their hands. Gradually, he grew taller, and when they lifted him up, he was indeed three zhang tall, slender and tall like a bamboo pole. The ghosts laughed and mocked him, calling him the "Long Pole Ghost."

    Explanation

    133

    The king then said to him, "Do you want to cook your right side into a juice? Do you want to be a foot shorter?" The strange man was troubled by his height and could not stand on his own. He wished to be a foot shorter. The ghosts then drove him to a stone bed, pressing him flat like dough, and with great force, his bones cracked loudly. They lifted him up, and indeed he was a foot shorter, round and resembling a large crab. The crowd laughed and mocked him, calling him a crab monster. The strange man stumbled on the ground, unable to bear the pain. Beside him, an old ghost clapped and laughed, saying, "You usually do not believe in ghosts, so why are you in this form today?" Then he asked the crowd, "He may be disrespectful, but he has also suffered greatly; he is pitiful, please forgive him!" The old ghost then lifted and shook the strange man with his two hands, and he was restored to his original state.     ”老鬼曰：“然则，以何物赠之？ ”一鬼曰：“吾赠以拨云之角。 ”即以两角置于大异之额，岌然相向。一鬼曰：“吾赠以哨风之嘴。”即以一铁嘴加于其唇，尖锐如鸟喙焉。一鬼曰：“吾赠以朱华之发。”即以赤水染其发，皆鬅鬙而上指，其色如火。一鬼曰：“吾赠以碧光之睛。”即以二青珠嵌于其目，湛湛而碧色矣。老鬼遂送之出坑曰：“善自珍重，向者群小溷渎，幸勿记怀也。”大异虽得出，然而顶拨云之角，戴哨风之嘴，被朱华之发，含碧光之睛，俨然成一奇鬼。到家，妻孥不敢认；出市，众共聚观。

    The old ghost said, "Then, what shall we give him?" One ghost replied, "I will give him the horns that can clear the clouds." He placed two horns on the forehead of the strange being, standing tall and facing each other. Another ghost said, "I will give him the mouth that can whistle the wind." He placed an iron beak on his lips, sharp as a bird's beak. A third ghost said, "I will give him the hair dyed with the color of the red flower." He dyed his hair with the red water, making it frizzy and pointing upwards, its color like fire. A fourth ghost said, "I will give him the eyes with the green light." He placed two green pearls in his eyes, deep and green in color. The old ghost then sent him out of the pit, saying, "Take good care of yourself. Although the strange being managed to get out, he now had the horns that could clear the clouds on his head, the mouth that could whistle the wind, the hair dyed with the color of the red flower, and the eyes with the green light, and he had become a strange ghost. When he returned home, his wife and children did not dare to recognize him; when he went out into the market, the crowd gathered to watch.

    He was regarded as a monster, and children would scream and run away. He then shut himself in his room, refusing to eat, and died in anger and frustration.     Three days later, during the day, there was a great storm. The fog was everywhere, and thunder and lightning shook the entire world. Roofs and tiles were flying, and large trees were uprooted. It cleared up after a night. The pit where he fell turned into a large lake, spreading over several miles, and the water was all red. Suddenly, a voice came from the coffin, saying, "The lawsuit has been won! All the ghosts have been destroyed without a trace. I will not be appointed to any position because of my integrity, but I have been appointed as the judicial officer of the Great Void Hall. The position is very important, and I will not return to the human world again." His family performed a ritual and buried him. In the air, there seemed to be a spirit.

    修文舍人传
    　　夏颜，字希贤，吴之震泽人也。博学多闻，性气英迈，幅巾布裘，游于东西两浙间。喜慷慨论事，迭迭不厌，人每倾下之。然而命分甚薄，日不暇给，尝喟然长叹曰：“夏颜，汝修身谨行，奈何不能润其家乎？”则又自解曰：“颜渊困于陋巷，岂道义之不足也？贾谊屈于长沙，岂文章之不赡也？校尉封拜而李广不侯，岂智勇之不逮也？侏儒饱死而方朔苦饥，岂才艺之不敏也？盖有命焉，不可幸而致。吾知顺受而已，岂敢非理妄求哉！ ”

    The Biography of the Literary Attendant

    Xia Yan, courtesy name Xi Xian, was from Zhenze in Wu. He was broadly learned and well-informed, with a noble and vigorous spirit. Wearing a simple headband and a rough, unadorned robe, he wandered between the eastern and western regions of Zhejiang. He enjoyed speaking boldly and passionately about matters, doing so repeatedly without tiring, and people often admired him for his eloquence. However, his fate was quite meager, and he often found himself unable to provide for his family. Once, he sighed deeply and said, "Xia Yan, you have cultivated your character and conducted yourself with care, yet why are you unable to provide for your family?" Then he explained to himself, "Yan Hui lived in a humble lane, but was he lacking in virtue? Jia Yi was demoted to Changsha, but was his writing insufficient? Li Guang was never granted a title of nobility despite his military achievements, but was he lacking in wisdom and courage? Dongfang Shuo lived in poverty despite his talents, but was he lacking in skill? There is fate at work, which cannot be achieved by chance. I know that I must accept my fate, and dare not seek what is unreasonable!"

    137

    至正初，客死润州，葬于北固山下。友人有与之契厚者，忽遇之于途。见颜驱高车，拥大盖，峨冠曳佩，如侯伯状，从者各执其物，呵殿而随护，风采扬扬，非复住日，投北而去。友人不敢呼之。
    　　一日，早作，复遇之于里门，颜遽搴帷下车而施揖曰：“故人安否？”友人遂与叙旧，执手款语，不异平生。乃问之曰：“与君隔别未久，而能自致青云，立身要路。车马仆从，如此之盛；衣服冠带，如此之华，可谓大丈夫得志之秋矣！不胜健羡之至！ ”颜曰：“吾今隶职冥司，颇极清要。故人下问，何敢有隐，但途路之次，未暇备述，如不相弃，可于后夕会于甘露寺多景楼，庶得从容时顷，少叙间阔，不知可乎？望勿以幽冥为讶，而负此诚约也。 ”友人许之。告别而去。是夕，携洒而往，则颜已先在，见其至，喜甚，迎谓曰：“故人真信士，可谓死生之交矣！ ”乃言曰：“地下之乐，不减人间，吾今为修文舍人，颜渊、卜商旧职也。

    Explanation

    137

    In the early years of the Zhi Zheng era, he died as a guest in Runzhou and was buried at the foot of Beigushan. A friend who had a close bond with him suddenly met him on the road. Seeing Yan driving a high carriage, carrying a large canopy, wearing an elaborate hat and dragging a pendant, appearing like a marquis or a high-ranking official, his attendants each holding their respective items, shouting to clear the way and following to protect him, his demeanor was radiant, no longer the same as before, he headed north and left. The friend dared not call out to him.

    One day, early in the morning, he met him again at the city gate. Yan quickly drew the curtain, got out of the carriage, and bowed, saying, "How is my old friend?" The friend then conversed with him, holding hands and speaking warmly, no different from their days of old. He then asked, "Not long ago, you were separated from me, yet you have now risen to a high position, established yourself in a key role. Your carriage, horses, servants, and attendants are so numerous; your clothes, hats, and accessories are so splendid. You can truly say that this is the season when a great man achieves his aspirations! I cannot help but envy you greatly!" Yan replied, "I am now employed in the underworld, holding a very important position. My old friend has asked me, how could I keep anything hidden? But on the journey, I have not had the time to fully explain. If you do not abandon me, we can meet at the Duojing Tower in Ganlu Temple tomorrow night. Perhaps we can spend some time together, briefly catching up, do you think that would be possible? I hope you will not be surprised by my presence in the underworld and will not break this sincere agreement." The friend agreed. They bade farewell and parted ways. That evening, he brought wine and went there, and Yan was already there. Seeing him arrive, Yan was very happy, greeted him, and said, "My old friend is truly a man of integrity, you can truly say that we are friends who transcend life and death!" He then said, "The pleasures of the underworld are not inferior to those of the human world. I am now the Director of Cultural Affairs, a position once held by Yan Hui and Bo Yi."

    冥司用人，选擢甚精，必当其才，必称其职，然后官位可居，爵禄可致，非若人间可以贿赂而通，可以门第而进，可以外貌而滥充，可以虚名而攫取也。试与君论之：今夫人世之上，仕路之间，秉笔中书者，岂尽萧、曹、丙、魏之徒乎？提兵阃外者，岂尽韩、彭、卫、霍之流乎？馆阁擒文者，岂皆班、扬、董、马之辈乎？郡邑牧民者，岂皆龚、黄、召，杜之俦乎？骐骥服盐车而驽骀厌刍豆，凤凰栖枳棘而鸱鸮鸣户庭，贤者槁项黄馘而死于下，不贤者比肩接迹而显于世，故治日常少，乱日常多，正坐此也。冥司则不然、黜陟必明，赏罚必公，昔日负君之贼，败国之臣，受穹爵而享厚禄者，至此必妥其殃，昔日积善之家，修德之士，阨下位而困穷途者，至此必蒙其福。盖轮口之数，报应之条，至此而莫逃矣。 ”遂引满而饮，连举数觥，凭栏观眺，口占律诗二章，吟赠友人曰：

    Explanation

    138

    The administration of the underworld is extremely meticulous in its selection and promotion, ensuring that individuals are matched with their talents and suited for their positions. Unlike in the human world, where one can advance through bribery, family background, superficial appearances, or false reputations, the underworld ensures that each person is placed in a role that fits their abilities and character. Those who hold positions in the central government, command troops outside the capital, work in the imperial library, or govern towns and counties are all selected with great care.

    In the human world, it is common to see virtuous people die in obscurity with emaciated necks and yellow faces, while unvirtuous people rise to prominence. This inversion of merit and status leads to fewer good days and more bad days, precisely because of this. In the underworld, however, promotions and demotions are clearly defined, and rewards and punishments are fair. Those who betrayed their rulers, ruined their countries, and enjoyed high ranks and generous salaries in life will surely face their misfortunes here. Conversely, those who accumulated good deeds, cultivated virtue, and were in lowly positions and poor circumstances in life will surely receive their blessings here. The cycles of fate and the laws of retribution are inescapable here.

    After these reflections, the speaker raised his cup and drank, then raised several more. Leaning on the railing, he looked out and composed two regulated verse poems, which he recited to his friend.

    笑拍阑干扣玉壶，林鸦惊散渚禽呼。
    　　一江流水三更月，两岸青山六代都。
    　　富贵不来吾老矣，幽明无间子知乎？

    139

    Laughing, I clapped the railing and tapped the jade vase, startling the crows in the woods and scattering the birds on the shore.
    A river flows beneath the third watch of the moon, with green mountains on both banks, a sight that has seen six dynasties.
    Wealth and honor have not come to me in my old age, but do you know the truth that lies beyond the visible and invisible?
    If others ask about my future prospects, I would say that accumulating virtue and practicing benevolence is the smooth path.
    My body is drenched in dew and mist under a vast, dark night sky, and the reflection of the mountains and water blend into one.
    By the Iron Pot City, people enjoy the moon, and from beyond the Ghost Gate, travelers return home.
    Fame and success cannot buy me a thousand poems, and life and death are no different from a dream.
    Thankfully, I have a friend who understands this meaning, and we engage in intellectual conversation late into the night on a bamboo bed.
    After reciting these lines, I scratched my head and said, "The highest virtue is to establish moral character, followed by achieving honor, and then by leaving behind words. In my lifetime, I have no notable moral achievements or accomplishments to recount, but I have compiled a collection of writings, not less than several hundred volumes. I have also written over a thousand articles, all deeply researched and crafted with intention. Since the sudden changes, my family affairs have declined; there are no children to open the door, and no intellectual companions outside. Thieves have stolen, and pests and rodents have destroyed, leaving only one-tenth of what was once there—it is truly regrettable. I hope my friend will show compassion for my talent, care for our friendship, and provide material support, as Zijian did with his precious sword, and as Sima Guang did with his grain-laden boat. Use resources wisely and practice kindness without expecting returns. Inscribed on durable materials, these works will be shared with those who appreciate them, perhaps avoiding the fate of decaying like grass and trees—this would be a gift from my friend. Speaking of this, I am deeply grateful and humbled!"
    The friend agreed. I was overjoyed, raised a cup, and bowed in thanks, expressing my earnest gratitude.

    已而，东方渐曙，告别而去。友人吴中，访其家，除散亡零落外，犹得遗文数百篇，并所薯《汲古录》、《通玄志》等书，亟命工镂版，鬻之予肆，以广其传。颜复到门致渤。自此往来无间，其家吉凶祸福，皆前期报之。三年之启，友人感疾，颜来访问，因谓曰：“仆备员修文府，日月已满，当得举代。冥间最重此职，得之甚难。君若不欲，则不敢强；万一欲之，当与尽力。所以汲汲于此者，盖欲报君镂版之恩耳。人生会当有死，纵复强延数年，何可得居此地也？ ”友人欣然许之，遂处置家事，不复治疗，数日而终。

    140

    After a while, it was just getting light in the east, and they bid farewell and left. The friend from Wu visited his family, except for the scattered and lost ones, still obtained hundreds of pages of his writings, along with the collected works Ji Gu Lu and Tong Xuan Zhi and other books. He quickly ordered craftsmen to carve the blocks and sold them at a shop to spread his teachings. Yan returned to the door to express thanks. From then on, they visited each other without interruption, and all the joys, sorrows, misfortunes, and blessings of his family were reported to him in advance. After three years, the friend fell ill, and Yan came to visit, and he said, "I serve in the Bureau of Literature, the time has been fulfilled, and I should be promoted. This position is highly valued in the afterlife, and it is very difficult to obtain. If you do not want it, I will not force you; if you want it, I will do my best to help. The reason I am so eager about this is to repay your kindness in carving the blocks. Human life will eventually end in death, even if you try to prolong it by a few years, how can you stay in this place?" The friend happily agreed, and so he disposed of his family affairs, stopped treating his illness, and died after a few days.

    鉴湖夜泛记
    　　处士成令言，不求闻达，素爱会稽山水。天历间，卜居鉴湖之滨，诵“千岩竞秀，万壑争流”之句，终日遨游不辍。常乘一叶小舟，不施篙橹，风帆浪揖，任其所之，或观鱼水涯，或盟鸥沙际，或苹洲狎鹭，或柳岸闻鸳。沿湖三十里，飞者走者，浮者跃者，皆熟其状貌，与之相忘，自去自来，不复疑俱。而樵翁、耕叟、渔童、牧竖遇之，不问老幼，俱得其欢心焉。初秋之夕，泊舟千秋观下，金凤乍起，白露未零，星斗交辉，水天一色，时闻菱歌莲唱，应答于洲渚之间。

    141

    A Nightly Cruise on Jianhu Lake

    The reclusive scholar Cheng Lingyan did not seek fame or official rank, but had always loved the mountains and waters of Kuaiji. During the reign of the Yuan Emperor Tugh Temür (the Tianli era), he chose to settle by the shores of Jianhu Lake, reciting the lines “A thousand peaks vie in beauty, ten thousand ravines contend in flow,” and roamed continuously throughout the day. He often sailed in a small boat, using neither oars nor paddles, his sail filled by the wind and his boat gently met by the waves, allowing it to go wherever it would. Sometimes he watched fish along the water’s edge, sometimes he made a pact with seagulls at the sandbanks, sometimes he played with egrets on the reed-covered islets, and sometimes he listened to the calls of mandarin ducks by the willow-lined shore.

    For thirty li along the lake, all creatures—flying, running, floating, leaping—were familiar to him. He lived in harmony with them, forgetting their presence and his own, coming and going freely, no longer fearing or suspecting them. When woodcutters, farmers, fishermen’s children, and herders met him, regardless of their age, they all found him pleasing and friendly.

    On a late summer evening, he moored his boat below the Qianqiu Pavilion. The golden phoenix had just risen, the white dew had not yet fallen, the stars shone together, and the lake and sky merged into one color. Occasionally, the songs of fishermen and villagers, singing of lotus and water chestnuts, echoed back and forth between the islets.

    142

    令言卧舟中，仰视天汉，如白练万丈，横亘于南北，纤云扫迹，一尘不起。乃扣船舷，歌宋之问明河之篇，飘飘然有遗世独立，羽化登仙之意。舟忽自动，其行甚速，风水俱駃，一瞬千里，若有物引之者。令言莫测。须臾，至—处，寒气袭入，清光夺目，如玉田湛湛，琪花瑶草生其中，如银海洋洋，异兽神鱼泳其内。乌鸦群鸣，白榆乱植。令言度非人间，披衣而起，见珠宫岌然，宫阙高耸。有一仙娥，自内而出，被冰绡之衣，曳霜纨之帔，戴翠凤步摇之冠，蹑琼纹九章之履。侍女二人，一执金柄障扇，一捧玉环如意，星眸月貌，光彩照人。

    Explanation

    142

    令言躺在船上，仰望银河，如同一条万丈长的白练，横跨南北，细云扫过，没有一丝尘埃。他敲击船舷，吟唱宋之问的《明河》诗篇，心中飘飘然，有遗世独立、羽化登仙之感。船忽然自动前行，速度极快，风和水都迅猛无比，瞬间行了一千多里，仿佛有某种力量在牵引着它。令言感到困惑不解。不久，船到达一处，寒气扑面而来，清光夺目，宛如一片晶莹的玉田，珍贵的花草生长其中，又如一片广阔的银海，奇异的野兽和神鱼在水中游弋。乌鸦群鸣，白榆树杂乱地生长。令言猜想这不是人间，便披上衣服起身，只见一座座珠宫巍峨耸立，宫殿高耸入云。一位仙娥从宫中走出，身穿冰绡之衣，披着霜纨之帔，头戴翠凤步摇冠，脚踏琼纹九章履。两名侍女，一人手持金柄遮阳扇，一人捧着玉环如意，她星眸月貌，光彩照人。

    绿衣人传
    　　天水赵源，早丧父母，未有妻室。延佑间，游学至于钱塘，侨居西湖葛岭之上，其侧即宋贾秋壑旧宅也。源独居无聊，尝日晚徙倚门外，见一女子，从东来，绿衣双鬟，年可十五六，虽不盛妆浓饰，而姿色过人，源注目久之。明日出门，又见，如此凡数度，日晚辄来。源戏问之曰：“家居何处，暮暮来此？”女笑而拜曰：“儿家与君为邻，君自不识耳。”源试挑之，女欣然而应，因遂留宿，甚相亲昵。明旦，辞去，夜则复来。如此凡月余，情爱甚至。源问其姓氏居址，女曰： “君但得美妇而已，何用强知。”问之不已，则曰：“儿常衣绿，但呼我为绿衣人可矣。 ”终不告以居址所在。源意其为巨室妾媵，夜出私奔，或恐事迹彰闻，故不肯言耳，信之不疑，宠念转密。

    The Green-Garbed Woman
    In the early years of the Yuan Dynasty, Zhao Yuan, from Tianshui, lost his parents at a young age and was not yet married. During the reign of Emperor Wenzong, he traveled and studied to Qiantang, residing temporarily near West Lake on Ge Ling, where the former residence of Jia Qiuhe, a prominent official during the Southern Song Dynasty, stood. Zhao Yuan lived alone and felt bored, often lingering at the gate in the evening. One day, he saw a woman coming from the east, dressed in green and with two braids, who appeared to be about fifteen or sixteen years old. Although she was not heavily adorned, her beauty surpassed the ordinary. Zhao Yuan stared at her for a long time. The next day, when he went out, he saw her again, and this happened several times, with her arriving every evening.

    Zhao Yuan playfully asked her, "Where do you live, and why do you come here every evening?" The woman smiled and bowed, saying, "My home is next to yours; you just don't recognize it." Zhao Yuan tried to flirt with her, and she happily responded, so they spent the night together, becoming very close. The next morning, she left, but she returned at night. This continued for over a month, and their affection grew deep. Zhao Yuan asked her about her name and address, but she said, "You just got a beautiful wife; why do you need to know more?" When he persisted, she said, "I always wear green; just call me the Green-Garbed Woman." She never revealed her address. Zhao Yuan thought she might be a concubine from a wealthy household who had run away secretly at night, fearing that her actions would become known publicly, so she did not speak. He believed her without doubt and cherished her more deeply.

    150

    一夕，源被酒，戏指其衣曰：“此真可谓‘绿兮衣兮，绿衣黄裳者也。”女有惭色，数夕不至。及再来，源叩之，乃曰：“本欲相与偕老，奈何以婢妾待之，令人忸怩而不安，故数日不敢侍君之侧。然君已知矣，今不复隐，请得备言之。儿与君，旧相识也，今非至情相感，莫能及此。 ”源问其故，女惨然曰：“得无相难乎？儿实非今世人，亦非有祸于君者，盖冥数当然，夙缘未尽耳。 ”源大惊曰：“愿闻其详。”女曰：“儿故宋秋壑平章之侍女也。

    本临安良家子，少善弈棋，年十五，以棋童入侍，每秋壑朝回，宴坐半闲堂，必召儿侍弈，备见宠爱。是时君为其家苍头，职主煎茶，每因供进茶瓯，得至后堂。君时年少，美姿容，儿见而慕之，尝以绣罗钱箧，乘暗投君。君亦以玳瑁脂盒为赠，彼此虽各有意，而内外严密，莫能得其便。后为同辈所觉，谗于秋壑，遂与君同赐死于西湖断桥之下。君今已再世为人，而儿犹在鬼箓，得非命欤？ ”言讫，呜咽泣下。源亦为之动容。久之，乃曰：“审若是，则吾与汝乃再世因缘也，当更加亲爱，以偿畴昔之愿。 ”自是遂留宿源舍，不复更去。源素不善奕，教之弈，尽传其妙，凡平日以棋称者，皆不能敌也。

    Originally, he was a son of a respectable family in Lin'an, skilled in chess from a young age.     每说秋壑旧事，其所目击者，历历甚详。尝言：秋壑一日倚楼闲望，诸姬皆侍，适二人乌巾素服，乘小舟由湖登岸。一姬曰：“美哉，二少年！”秋壑曰：“汝愿事之耶？当令纳聘。”姬笑而无言。逾时，令人捧一盒，呼诸姬至前曰：“适为某姬纳聘。”启视之，则姬之首也，诸姬皆战栗而退。又尝贩盐数百艘至都市货之。太学有诗曰：

    Whenever he talks about the old stories of Qiuhè, what he personally witnessed, he describes in great detail. After some time, he had someone bring a box and called the other concubines forward, saying, 'Just now, I paid a dowry for a certain concubine.' When he opened it, it was the head of the concubine, and the other concubines all trembled and withdrew. He also once sent hundreds of ships to the city to sell salt. The Imperial College had a poem that said:"

    153

    昨夜江头涌碧波，满船都载相公鹾；
    　　虽然要作调羹用，未必调羹用许多！
    　　秋壑闻之，遂以士人付狱，论以诽谤罪。又尝于浙西行公田法，民受其苦，或题诗于路左云：
    　　襄阳累岁困孤城，豢养湖山不出征。
    　　不识咽喉形势地，公田枉自害苍生。
    　　秋壑见之，捕得，遭远窜。又尝斋云水千人，其数已足，末有一道士，衣裾褴褛，至门求斋。主者以数足，不肯引入，道士坚求不去，不得已于门侧斋焉。斋罢，覆其钵于案而去，众悉力举之，不动。启于秋壑，自往举之，乃有诗二句云：“得好休时便好休，收花结子在漳州。”始知真仙降临而不识也。

    Explanation

    153

    Last night at the riverhead, green waves surged, and the boat was fully loaded with salt for the officials;
    Though it might be used to make a spoon, it's not necessary to use so much!
    Upon hearing this, Autumn Ravine had the scholars imprisoned and charged them with slander. He once implemented the public land policy in Zhe West, causing great suffering among the people, some of whom wrote poems on the roadside:
    For years, Xiangyang has been besieged in a lonely city, nurturing lakes and mountains without going to war.
    Not knowing the strategic importance of the throat area, the public land policy has harmed the common people in vain.
    Autumn Ravine saw these poems, captured the writers, and exiled them far away. Once, he offered a meal to a thousand cloud and water monks, and the number was already full. At the end, there was a Taoist priest with tattered clothes who came to the door seeking a meal. The host, thinking the number was complete, refused to let him in. The Taoist persisted and would not leave, so they could not help but give him a meal at the side of the door. After the meal, he placed his bowl on the table and left. Everyone tried to lift the bowl, but it wouldn't move. They reported this to Autumn Ravine, who went himself to lift the bowl. There were two lines of poetry inside: "When it's time to rest, rest well; gather flowers and bear fruit in Zhangzhou." It was then that they realized a true immortal had descended but was not recognized.

    154

    然终不喻“漳州”之意，嗟乎！孰知有漳州木绵庵之厄也！又尝有艄人泊舟苏堤，时方盛暑，卧于舟尾，终夜不寐，见三人长不盈尺，集于沙际，一曰：“张公至矣，如之奈何？ ”一曰：“贾平章非仁者，决不相恕！ ”一曰：“我则已矣，公等及见其败也！ ”相与哭入水中。次日，渔者张公获一鳖，径二尺余，纳之府第。不三年而祸作。盖物亦先知，数而不可逃也。源曰：“吾今日与汝相遇，抑岂非数乎？ ”女曰：“是诚不妄矣！ ”源曰：“汝之精气，能久存于世耶？ ”女曰：“数至则散矣。 ”源曰：“然则何时？ ”女曰：“三年耳。 ”源固未之信。

    Explanation

    154

    Yet still cannot comprehend the meaning of "Zhangzhou." Alas! Who could have known about the calamity at the Mulan Temple in Zhangzhou? Once, a boatman moored his boat at Su Causeway, and it was the height of summer. He lay at the stern of the boat, unable to sleep all night, and saw three figures no taller than a foot, gathered at the edge of the sand. One said, "Zhang has arrived; what can be done about it?" Another said, "Jia Pingzhang is not a benevolent person; he will never forgive!" The third said, "I am finished; you will witness his downfall!" They wept and then entered the water together. The next day, the fisherman Zhang caught a turtle, more than two feet in diameter, and took it to his mansion. Within three years, disaster struck. Indeed, things also know fate, and it is unavoidable. The source said, "Is it not fate that we meet today?" The woman replied, "Indeed, it is not false!" The source asked, "Can your spiritual energy persist in the world for long?" The woman answered, "When fate arrives, it disperses." The source asked, "Then when?" The woman replied, "In three years." The source still did not believe it.

    155

    及期，卧病不起。源为之迎医，女不欲，曰：“曩固已与君言矣，因缘之契，夫妇之情，尽于此矣。 ”即以手握源臂，而与之诀曰：“儿以幽阴之质，得事君子，荷蒙不弃，周旋许时。往者一念之私，俱陷不测之祸，然而海枯石烂，此恨难消，地老天荒，此情不泯！今幸得续前生之好，践往世之盟，三载于兹，志愿已足，请从此辞，毋更以为念也！ ”言讫，面壁而卧，呼之不应矣。源大伤恸，为治棺榇而殓之。将葬，怪其柩甚轻，启而视之，惟衣衾钗珥在耳。乃虚葬于北山之麓。源感其情，不复再娶，投灵隐寺出家为僧，终其身云。

    　　秋香亭记

    Explanation

    155

    By the appointed time, she lay ill and unable to rise. Yuan went to fetch a doctor for her, but the woman did not want to. She said, "I have already told you before, the karmic bond, the affection of husband and wife, has ended here." She held Yuan's arm with her hand and bid farewell to him, saying, "I, as a being from the netherworld, was able to serve a gentleman, grateful for not being abandoned, spent some time together. The past, a single selfish thought, both fell into unforeseen calamity, however, until the sea dries up and the rocks crumble, this resentment is hard to erase, until the earth ages and the sky fades, this feeling will not fade. Now fortunately, we can continue our previous life's good relationship, fulfill the vow of our past lives, for three years now, our wishes are fulfilled. Please let me depart from here, do not think of me any further." She then lay facing the wall, and could not be called back.

    Yuan was greatly saddened and grieved, prepared the coffin and dressed her for burial. When preparing for burial, he found the coffin unusually light, opened it to see, only the clothes, bedding, and jewelry remained. So he buried her in a symbolic grave at the foot of North Mountain. Moved by her feelings, he did not remarry, went to Lingyin Temple to become a monk, and lived out his life as such.

    Appendix
    Record of the Chrysanthemum Pavilion

    156

    至正间，有商生者，随父宦游姑苏，侨居乌鹊桥，其邻则弘农杨氏第也。杨氏乃延佑大诗人浦城公之裔。浦城娶于商，其孙女名采采，与生中表兄妹也。浦城已殁，商氏尚存。生少年，气禀清淑，性质温粹，与采采俱在童卯。商氏，即生之祖姑也。每读书之暇，与采采共戏于庭，为商氏所钟爱，尝抚生指采采谓曰： “汝宜益加进修，吾孙女誓不适他族，当令事汝，以续二姓之亲，永以为好也。 ”女父母乐闻此言，即欲归之，而生严亲以生年幼，恐其怠于学业，请俟他日。生、女因商氏之言，倍相怜爱。
    　　数岁，遇中秋月夕，家人会饮沾醉，遂同游于生宅秋香亭上，有二桂树，垂荫婆娑，花方盛开，月色团圆，香气浓馥，生、女私于其下语心焉。是后，女年稍长，不复过宅，每岁节伏腊，仅以兄妹礼见于中堂而已。闺阁深邃，莫能致其情。后一岁，亭前桂花始开，女以折花为名，以碧瑶笺书绝句二首，令侍婢秀香持以授生，嘱生继和，诗曰：

    Explanation

    156

    During the reign of Emperor Wen of Yuan, there was a young man named Shang Sheng, who accompanied his father on official travels to Suzhou and temporarily resided near the Wuer Bridge. His neighbor was the residence of the Hongnong Yang family. The Yang family were descendants of the great poet Pu Cheng from Putian during the Yuan dynasty. Pu Cheng had married into the Shang family, and his granddaughter, named Cai Cai, was Shang Sheng's cousin. Pu Cheng had passed away, but his wife, Shang Sheng's grandmother, was still alive. Shang Sheng was a young man of noble character and gentle disposition, and he grew up alongside Cai Cai. Shang Sheng's grandmother, who was his paternal grandmother, often took him aside and pointed to Cai Cai, saying, "You should strive to improve yourself further. My granddaughter has vowed not to marry into any other family. She will be your wife, continuing the bond between our two families, and ensuring a lasting and harmonious relationship." Cai Cai's parents were delighted to hear this, and they wished to arrange the marriage immediately. However, Shang Sheng's strict father, fearing that his son might neglect his studies, suggested waiting until a more appropriate time. As a result, Shang Sheng and Cai Cai, influenced by their grandmother's words, grew to love each other even more deeply.

    A few years later, during the Mid-Autumn Festival, the family gathered for a feast and drank until they were slightly intoxicated. They then strolled together to the Qiuxiang Pavilion in Shang Sheng's home. There, two osmanthus trees provided a lush canopy, their flowers in full bloom, and the moon was round and bright, filling the air with a fragrant aroma. Shang Sheng and Cai Cai secretly spoke to each other beneath the trees, sharing their deepest feelings. After this, as Cai Cai grew older, she no longer visited Shang Sheng's home. They only met occasionally during the major festivals, exchanging greetings as cousins in the main hall. The separation between them deepened, and their emotional connection remained hidden. The following year, when the osmanthus flowers began to bloom again, Cai Cai used the excuse of picking flowers to send a message to Shang Sheng. She wrote two short poems on fine, high-quality paper and had her maid Xiuxiang deliver them to him, asking him to compose a response. The poems read:

    [Insert the two short poems here]

    157

    秋香亭上桂花芳，几度风吹到绣房。
    　　自恨人生不如树，朝朝肠断屋西墙！
    　　秋香亭上桂花舒，用意殷勤种两株。
    　　愿得他年如此树，锦裁步障护明珠。
    　　生得之，惊喜，遂口占二首，书以奉答，付婢持去。诗曰：
    　　深盟密约两情劳，犹有余香在旧袍。
    　　记得去年携手处，秋香亭上月轮高。
    　　高栽翠柳隔芳园，牢织金笼贮彩鸳。
    　　忽有书来传好语，秋香亭上鹊声喧。
    　　生始慕其色而已，不知其才之若是也，既见二诗，大喜欲狂。但翘首企足，以待结褵之期，不计其它也。女后以多情致疾，恐生不知其眷恋之情，乃以吴绫帕题绝句于上，令婢持以赠生。诗曰：
    　　罗帕熏香病裹头，眼波娇溜满眶秋。
    　　风流不与愁相约，才到风流便有愁。

    Explanation

    157

    The Fragrant Osmanthus Pavilion

    The osmanthus flowers on the Fragrant Osmanthus Pavilion exude a pleasant fragrance, carried by the wind to the embroidered room several times.
    I regret that human life is not as enduring as trees, and every day my heart breaks at the west wall of the house!
    On the Fragrant Osmanthus Pavilion, the osmanthus flowers bloom, and two trees were planted with great care and effort.
    I wish that in the future, I would be like these trees, protected by a brocade screen to safeguard the precious pearl.
    He received it, was surprised and delighted, then composed two poems, wrote them down to reply, and sent them through a servant. The poems read:
    Deep and secret vows bind our hearts, and there is still a lingering fragrance on the old robe.
    I remember where we held hands last year, under the full moon over the Fragrant Osmanthus Pavilion.
    Planting tall green willows to separate the fragrant garden, weaving a golden cage to keep colorful mandarin ducks.
    Suddenly a letter came with good news, and the noisy crow on the Fragrant Osmanthus Pavilion symbolized the good omen.
    He was only attracted by her appearance, not knowing her talent was so great. After seeing the two poems, he was extremely happy and almost went crazy. He looked forward eagerly, waiting for the wedding day, not counting other things.
    Later, she fell ill due to her deep affection, fearing he would not understand her longing. She wrote a quatrain on a handkerchief made of Wu silk and had a servant deliver it to him. The poem read:
    The handkerchief scented with perfume wrapped around her head while she was sick, her eyes were full of autumn-like charm.
    Charm and beauty do not agree with sorrow, as soon as charm and beauty arrive, sorrow follows.

    158

    生感叹再三，未及酬和。适高邮张氏兵起，三吴扰乱，生父挈家南归临安，展转会稽、四明以避乱；女家亦北徙金陵。音耗不通者十载。吴元年，国朝混一，道路始通。时生父已殁，独奉母居钱塘故址，遣旧使老苍头往金陵物色之，则女以甲辰年适太原王氏，有子矣。苍头回报，生虽怅然绝望，然终欲一致款曲于女，以导达其情，遂市剪彩花二盝，紫绵脂百饼，遣苍头赍往遗之。恨其负约，不复致书，但以苍头己意，托交亲之故，求一见以觇其情。王氏亦金陵巨室，开彩帛铺于市，适女垂帘独立，见苍头趦趄于门，遽呼之曰：“得非商兄家旧人耶？ ”即命之入，询问动静，颜色惨怛。苍头以二物进，女怪其无书，具述生意以告。女吁嗟抑塞，不能致辞，以酒馔待之。约其明日再来叙话。苍头如命而往。女剪乌丝襕，修简遗生曰：伏承来使，具述前因。天不成全，事多间阻。盖自前朝失政，列郡受兵，大伤小亡，弱肉强食，荐遭祸乱，十载于此。

    Explanation

    158

    The young man sighed repeatedly but had not yet responded. Just as the Zhang clan from Gaoyou started a rebellion, the Three Wu regions were in turmoil. His father took his family south to Lin'an and temporarily stayed in Shaoxing and Siming to avoid the chaos. The woman's family also moved north to Jinling. There was no news or communication for ten years. In the first year of Wu, the nation was unified, and the roads began to be accessible. At that time, the young man's father had already passed away, and he alone supported his mother at their old residence in Qiantang. He sent an old servant to Jinling to look for her, and it turned out that the woman had married a man from Taiyuan's Wang clan in the year Jia Chen and had a child. The old servant returned with the news. The young man was despondent and hopeless, but still wanted to express his feelings to her to convey his sentiments. He then bought two boxes of cut flower decorations and a hundred cakes of purple silk powder and sent the old servant to deliver them to her. He regretted that she had broken the promise and did not write to her, but through the old servant, he asked to meet her to see how she felt. The Wang clan was also a prominent family in Jinling, and they had a silk and fabric shop in the market. The woman was standing alone behind a curtain when she saw the old servant hesitating at the door. She quickly called out to him, "Are you not someone from the merchant's family?" She immediately invited him in, asked about his family, and her expression was sad. The old servant presented the two items, and the woman was surprised that there was no letter. He explained the young man's intentions to her. The woman sighed and was speechless, unable to respond, and treated him to wine and food. She asked him to come back the next day to talk. The old servant went as instructed. The woman cut black silk and wrote a letter to the young man, saying: "I have heard through your messenger about the past events. Heaven did not complete the matter, and many obstacles arose. Since the previous dynasty lost its governance, the regions suffered from war, great losses and small ones, the weak were devoured by the strong, and we repeatedly faced disasters for ten years."

    159

    偶获生存，一身非故，东西奔窜，左右逃逋；祖母辞堂，先君捐馆；避终风之狂暴，虑行露之沾濡。欲终守前盟，则鳞鸿永绝；欲径行小谅，则沟渎莫知。不幸委身从人，延命度日。顾伶俜之弱质，值屯蹇之衰年，往往对景关情，逢时起恨。虽应酬之际，勉为笑欢；而岑寂之中，不胜伤感。追思旧事，如在昨朝。华翰铭心，佳音属耳。半衾未暖，幽梦难通，一枕才欹，惊魂又散。

    Explanation

    159

    Accidentally obtaining survival, my body is no longer my own, I flee in all directions, running left and right in desperation. My grandmother left the hall, my father departed the house; I avoid the fierce winds and fear the dampness of the road. If I want to keep the previous promise, then the message will be permanently lost; if I want to act directly out of small trust, then the ditch will have no one to know. Unfortunately, I entrust myself to others, prolonging life day by day. Considering my frail body, I encounter the difficult old age. Often, the scenery evokes feelings, and encountering the times brings resentment. Even during social interactions, I force a smile and pretend to be happy; but in moments of loneliness, the grief is overwhelming. Recalling past events, as if they happened yesterday. Beautiful letters engrave the heart, pleasant sounds reach the ear. Half of the quilt is not yet warm, the deep dream is hard to communicate. Just leaning on the pillow, the startled spirit disperses again.

    视容光之减旧，知憔悴之因郎；怅后会之无由，叹今生之虚度！岂意高明不弃，抚念过深，加沛泽以滂施，回余光以返照，采葑菲之下体，记萝茑之微踪；复致耀首之华，膏唇之饰，衰容顿改，厚惠何施！虽荷恩私，愈增惭愧！而况迩来形销体削，食减心烦，知来日之无多，念此身之如寄。兄若见之，亦当贱恶而弃去，尚何矜恤之有焉！倘恩情未尽，当结伉俪于来生，续婚姻于后世耳！临楮呜咽，悲不能禁。复制五十六字，上渎清览，苟或察其辞而恕其意，使箧扇怀恩，绨袍恋德，则虽死之日，犹生之年也。诗云：
    　　好姻缘是恶姻缘，只怨干戈不怨天。
    　　两世玉箫犹再合，何时金镜得重圆？
    　　彩鸾舞后肠空断，青雀飞来信不传。

    160

    Seeing the diminished radiance of her face, knowing that her emaciation is due to longing for her husband; grieving over the impossibility of meeting again, lamenting the futility of this life! Who would have thought that you, in your wisdom, would not abandon me, and that your thoughts for me are so deep, bestowing abundant grace and spreading it widely, turning your remaining light to shine upon me, picking the humblest parts of the gourd and the ivy, remembering the faintest traces of the vine; bestowing once again the brilliance of a radiant head, the adornment of painted lips, my aged appearance suddenly changed, what great kindness did you bestow upon me! Though I am burdened with your favor and kindness, it only increases my shame and guilt! How much more so, in recent times, my form has wasted away, my appetite diminished, and my heart troubled, knowing that my days are few, thinking of this body as a temporary lodging. If my brother were to see me, he would surely despise and abandon me, how could there be any pity or compassion left? If our affection is not yet exhausted, we shall be married in our next life, continuing our union in future generations. Writing these words, I weep, unable to hold back my sorrow. Writing these fifty-six characters, I humbly present them for your gracious perusal, if you would examine the words and pardon the meaning, let the fan and the cloth bag remember the kindness, the coarse cloth robe cherish the virtue, then even on the day of my death, it will be as if I am still alive. The poem says:
    A good marriage is a bad marriage, only blaming the wars, not heaven.
    Two lifetimes of the jade flute still come together, when will the golden mirror be reunited?
    After the dance of the colorful phoenix, the intestines are severed, the green bird flies but the message does not reach.

    安得神灵如倩女？芳魂容易到君边！
    　　生得书，虽无复致望，犹和其韵以自遣云：

    161

    How can I find a divine maiden like Qian Nv? Her fragrant soul can easily reach your side!

    Having received the letter, though I no longer harbor hope, I still composed a poem in response to her rhythm:

    The old bond of marriage on the Autumn Fragrance Pavilion,
    I long remember the mid-autumn night.
    The pillow soaked with tears of red makeup,
    The phoenix robe stained with blue sleep, flowers round.
    The broken string no longer mended by the phoenix glue,
    The old box in vain laboring to send the butterfly messenger.

    Its clear light could illuminate both of us.

    Every time I read it, I would waste days without eating or sleeping,
    For I could never forget my feelings.

    The lyrics say: The Moon Lord is hard to rely on,
    The Star Week is easily obstructed,
    The red leaves from the imperial canal can be burned.

    All the dewy flower branches have withered.
    Seeking the late spring,

    The cuckoo is already bored.

    Who would steal the red silk?
    Cherishing the traces of joy forever apart,
    The sorrow of separation is hard to bear!
    Looking back at the Autumn Fragrance Pavilion,

    The leaves fall in a flutter.
    The debt of longing,
    It remains unpaid,
    My heart breaks on this pitiful night!
    Still, I remember the beginning and end,
    To append it to the legends of the past and present,
    So that those who are emotionally sensitive may read it,
    And the sorrow of the beautiful woman is endless;
    So that those who uphold justice may hear it,
    And the heart of the knight remains.
    Who knows if it will end like this?

    162

    寄梅记
    　　朱端朝，字廷之，宋南渡后，肄业上庠，与妓女马琼琼者善，久之，情爱稠密。端朝文华富赡，琼琼识其非白屋久居之人，遂倾心焉，凡百资用，皆悉力给之。屡以终身为托。端朝虽口从，而心不之许，盖以其妻性严，非薄幸也。值秋试，端朝获捷，琼琼喜而劳之。端朝乃益淬励，省业春闱，揭报果复中优等。及对策，失之太激，遂置下甲。初注授南昌尉。琼琼力致恳曰：“妾风尘卑贱，荷君不弃。今幸荣登仕版，行将云泥隔绝，无复奉承枕席。妾之一身，终沦溺矣！诚可怜悯！欲望君与谋脱籍，永执箕帚。虽君内政谨严，妾当委曲遵奉，无敢唐突。万一脱此业缘，受赐于君，实非浅浅。且妾之箱箧稍充，若与力图，去籍犹不甚难。 ”端朝曰：“去籍之谋固易，但恐不能使家人无妒。吾计之亦久矣。

    Explanation

    162

    The Record of Sending the Plum

    Zhu Duanchao, courtesy name Tingzhi, after the Southern Song's establishment, studied at a prestigious academy. He became acquainted with Ma Qiongqiong, a courtesan, and over time, their affection deepened. Duanchao was eloquent and well-versed in literature, and Qiongqiong recognized that he was not a man of humble origins who had long dwelled in poverty. She thus fell deeply in love with him, providing all the resources and expenses he needed with all her strength. She often entrusted her entire life to him. Although Duanchao verbally agreed, in his heart he did not accept her, for his wife was strict, and he was not unfaithful.

    When the autumn examination took place, Duanchao passed successfully, and Qiongqiong rejoiced and cared for him. Encouraged by this, Duanchao redoubled his efforts and prepared diligently for the spring examination. The results were indeed announced, and he once again passed with distinction. However, when he submitted his response, it was deemed too impassioned, and he was placed in the lower division. He was initially appointed as the magistrate of Nanchang.

    Qiongqiong earnestly pleaded with him: "I am of lowly status, a woman of the entertainment world, yet you have not abandoned me. Now that I am fortunate enough to have entered the ranks of officialdom, we are soon to be separated by the vast gulf between heaven and earth, and I will no longer be able to serve you in the intimacy of the bedchamber. My life will ultimately be lost in despair! How pitiable this is! I wish to ask you to help me seek release from my registered status, so that I may forever take on the duties of a wife. Though your household affairs are strict, I will comply with them with all due respect and will not dare to be presumptuous. If I can be released from this karmic bond, I shall be forever grateful to you. Moreover, my chests and boxes are somewhat filled with possessions. If we work together, it should not be too difficult to remove my status."

    Duanchao replied: "The plan to release you from your status is indeed easy, but I fear it may not prevent my family from being jealous. I have considered this matter for a long time."

    163

    盛意既浓，沮之则近无情，从之则虞有辱，奈何！然既出汝心，当徐为调护，使其柔顺，庶得相安，否则计无所措也。 ”一夕，端朝因间，谓其妻曰：“我久居学舍，虽近得一官，家贫，急于干禄，岂得待数年之阙？且所得官，实出妓子马琼琼之赐。今彼欲倾箱箧，求托于我。彼亦小心，能迎合人意，诚能脱彼于风尘，亦仁人之恩也。 ”其妻曰：“君意既决，亦复何辞。 ”端朝喜谓琼琼曰：“初畏不从，吾试叩之，乃忻然相许。 ”端朝于是宛转求脱，而琼琼花籍亦得除去，遂运橐与端朝俱归。既至，妻妾怡然。端朝得琼琼之所携，家遂稍丰。因辟一区，为二阁，以东、西名，东阁以居其妻，令琼琼处于西阁。阙期既满，迓吏前至。端朝以路远俸薄，不欲携累，乃单骑赴任。将行，置酒相别，因瞩曰：“凡有家信，二阁合书一缄，吾覆亦如之。 ”

    Explanation

    163

    The sincere intention is already intense. If you discourage it, it will be close to being heartless; if you follow it, you might fear disgrace. What to do? However, since it comes from your heart, you should gradually adjust and protect it, making it gentle and compliant, perhaps we can live in peace. Otherwise, there is no way out.

    One night, Duan Chao took the opportunity and said to his wife, "I have been staying in the study hall for a long time, although I have recently obtained an official position. My family is poor, and I am eager to earn a salary. How can I wait for several years? Moreover, the position I obtained is actually due to the favor of the courtesan Ma Qiongqiong. Now she wants to empty her boxes and entrust herself to me. She is also careful and can cater to people's wishes. If you can truly free her from the brothel, it would also be a benevolent act."

    His wife replied, "Since your intention is already decided, what more can I say?"

    Duan Chao was pleased and told Ma Qiongqiong, "Initially, I was afraid she wouldn't agree. I tried to persuade her, and she happily agreed."

    Duan Chao then gently sought her release, and Ma Qiongqiong's name was also removed from the brothel register. She then packed her belongings and returned with Duan Chao. After arriving, his wives and concubines were pleased. Duan Chao received what Ma Qiongqiong brought with her, and his family then became somewhat prosperous. He then built a separate area with two pavilions, naming them East and West. The East Pavilion was for his wife, and Ma Qiongqiong was placed in the West Pavilion.

    After the term had expired, the welcoming officials arrived ahead of time. Duan Chao, because the journey was far and the salary was low, did not want to bring along his family. He then rode alone to take up his post. Before leaving, he set up a feast to bid farewell and instructed them, "For any family letters, both pavilions should write one letter, and I will respond in the same way."

    164

    端朝既至南昌，半载方得家人消息，而止东阁一书。端朝亦不介意。既栽覆，西阁亦不及见，索之，颇遭忌嫉，乃密遣一仆，厚给裹足，授以书，嘱之曰：“勿令孺人知之。”书至，端朝发阅，无一宇。乃所画梅雪扇面而已。反复观玩，后写一《减字木兰花》词云：

    Explanation

    164

    Duan Chao had arrived in Nanchang, and after half a year, he finally received news from his family, but it was only a single letter from the East Pavilion. Duan Chao did not mind this. Afterward, he also did not get to see the West Pavilion, and when he sought it, he met with much jealousy. He then secretly sent a servant, gave him a generous allowance for travel expenses, and handed him a letter, instructing him, saying, "Do not let the lady know about it." When the letter arrived, Duan Chao opened and read it, but it contained not a single word. It was only a painted plum and snow fan surface. He repeatedly admired it, and later wrote a poem titled "Reduced-Character Peony Flower," which goes:

    [The poem would follow here, but since the actual content of the poem is not provided in the source text, it is omitted in this translation.]

    165

    雪梅妒色，雪把梅花相抑勒。梅性温柔，雪压梅花怎起头？芳心欲破，全仗东君来作主。传语东君，早与梅花作主人。
    　　端朝自是坐卧不安，日夜思欲休官。盖以侥幸一官，皆琼琼之力，不忘本也。寻竟托疾弃归。既至家，妻妾出迎，怪其未及尽考，忽作归计，叩之不答。既而设酒，会二阁而言曰：”我羁縻千里，所望家人和顺，使我少安。昨见西阁所寄梅扇词，读之使人不遑寝食，吾安得不归哉！ ”东阁乃曰：“君今已仕，试与判此孰是。 ”端朝曰：“此非口舌可尽，可取纸笔书之。 ”遂作《浣溪沙》一阕云：
    　　梅正开时雪正狂，两般幽韵孰优长？且宜持酒细端详。
    　　梅比雪花输一白，雪如梅蕊少些香，无公非是不思量。
    　　自后二阁欢会如初，而端朝亦不复仕矣。

    Explanation

    165

    The Snow and Plum Blossoms Compete in Beauty, the Snow Suppressing the Plum Blossoms. The nature of the plum blossoms is gentle, yet how can the snow, pressing down upon them, allow them to bloom? Their hearts are eager to break forth, relying entirely on the East King to come and take charge. Pass on a message to the East King, urging him to come early and become the master of the plum blossoms.

    Duan Chao was restless, unable to find peace, day and night thinking of resigning from his post. It was because he had obtained this position by chance, all thanks to the efforts of Qiongqiong, and he did not forget his roots. Eventually, he feigned illness and resigned. Upon returning home, his wife and concubines welcomed him, puzzled by his sudden decision to resign before completing his term, and asked him why, but he did not answer. Later, he set up a banquet and spoke to two people, saying, "I have been tied up with official duties for a thousand miles, hoping that my family would be harmonious, allowing me some peace. Yesterday, I read a poem about plum blossoms sent by the person in the western pavilion, and it moved me so much that I could not sleep or eat, how could I not resign?" The person in the eastern pavilion said, "You are now an official, try to judge which of these two poems is better." Duan Chao replied, "This cannot be decided by mere words; you may take paper and pen to write it down." He then composed a poem titled "Huan Xisha," which reads:

    The plum blossoms are just beginning to bloom as the snow rages fiercely, which of the two has a more profound charm? It is best to sip wine and carefully appreciate the beauty.
    The plum blossoms are slightly less white than the snow, and the snow lacks the fragrance of the plum blossoms; neither is entirely without merit.
    Afterward, the two people resumed their friendship as before, and Duan Chao also did not resume his official duties.
